Hajj — Pilgrimage

Ruling on Sending a Badana: When Does It Trigger Ihram?
Ruling on ihram through sending a badana

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sending a badana makes a person muhrim, distinguish the exception for tamattu', and apply the definition of badana including cows.

Core Idea
Sending a badana does not make one muhrim until catching up, except for the badana of tamattu' or qiran.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key point in hajj jurisprudence: when does sending a sacrificial animal ahead of the pilgrim actually place the pilgrim in ihram? The ruling hinges on the distinction between a general badana and the specific badana for tamattu' or qiran. This lesson unpacks the conditions, the intra-Hanafi disagreement on driving, and the definition of badana including cows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: sending a badana (sacrificial animal). The ruling: the sender does not become muhrim until he catches up with the animal.
This is the general rule; there is an exception.
2
Note the exception
Identify the exception: for the badana of tamattu' (and qiran), catching up is not required; the pilgrim becomes muhrim immediately upon sending.
Why? Because this animal is a specific ritual of hajj (هدي).
3
Examine the condition dispute
The author, following al-Jami' al-Saghir, only requires catching up. Al-Mabsut also requires driving initially. Understand the reasoning: the action of the agent is like that of the principal.
The text prefers the first view.
4
Analyze actions that do not suffice
Covering, marking (ish'ar), or garlanding a sheep do not make one muhrim. Ish'ar is disliked by Abu Hanifa but considered good by the Sahibayn.
None of these replace talbiyyah.
5
Understand the definition of badana
Badana includes camels and cows, based on linguistic usage and the hadith of Jabir. The fruit of this definition appears when one vows a badana.
If no intention, a cow or camel is owed.

من البدن . ذكره مسلم في صحيحه وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما إذا التزم بدنة فإن نوى شيئاً فهو على ما نوى لأن المنوي إذا كان من محتملات كلامه فهو كالمصرح به وإن لم يكن له تية فعليه بقرة أو جزور فينحرها حيث شاء في قولهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف فإنه يقيسه على الهدى وهو يختص بمكة اتفاقاً، وهما قاساه على ما إذا التزم جزوراً فإنه لا يختص بمكة اتفاقاً. كذا في المبسوط والله أعلم.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram: He said: (If he sends it [the sacrifice] then goes towards it, he does not become a muhrim until he catches up with it, except in the case of the badana of tamattu') due to the absence of one of three conditions: driving it in the beginning. When he catches up, his intention becomes connected with an act that is specific to it, except for a sacrificial animal that is specific to Hajj by nature, which is the sacrificial animal of tamattu' and qiran. For that, catching up is not needed. 'Tamattu'' includes the customary tamattu' and qiran because what is mentioned in the verse is tamattu' by His statement: 'Whoever performs tamattu' with 'umrah to hajj' up to the end. So it is the proof for both. Therefore the author confined it to tamattu'. Since tamattu' does not occur before the months of Hajj, he did not restrict sending to the months of Hajj, so there was no need to restrict the end. Then the author, following al-Jami' al-Saghir, stipulated only catching up and did not stipulate driving with it. Both were stipulated in al-Mabsut. The first is apparent because the action of the agent in the presence of the principal is like the action of the principal. Thus it is reasoned in Fath al-Qadir. It may be said: He does not need it because he becomes muhrim by catching up even if no one drove it. This reasoning is based on the opinion of those who stipulate driving with catching up. The author indicated that it is necessary to go to the badana of tamattu', sending alone is not sufficient. He said: (If he covers it, or marks it, or garlands a sheep, he does not become a muhrim) meaning even if he drives it, because it is not from the specific rites of Hajj, so nothing takes the place of talbiyyah. Covering is to repel harm from it. Marking (ish'ar) is disliked according to Abu Hanifa – that one pierces the left side of the hump so that blood flows, so it is not from the ritual. According to him [Abu Yusuf] and him [Muhammad], even if it is good, it may be done for treatment. Unlike garlanding (taqlid), it is specific to the sacrifice, so taqlid is more beloved than leaving it unmarked because it is a sunnah of the Prophet. Covering is good following the Sunnah, and it is recommended to give it in charity. As for garlanding a sheep, it is not customary and not a sunnah, so it does not take its place. It is known from the author's exposition that he does not become muhrim by mere intention without talbiyyah or what takes its place, and this is the madhhab. From Abu Yusuf, it is reported that he is content with intention. There is no disagreement that talbiyyah alone is not sufficient without intention. He said: (And badanah are from camels and cows) meaning lexically and legally. Al-Jawhari said: Badana is a female camel or a cow like a camel. As for the hadith of departing on Friday and his conjunction of cow with badana, it is interpreted that he meant by the generic some individuals, i.e., a camel, not everything to which it applies, because if badana were only used for a camel, it would require transfer from the lexical meaning. Then he mentioned what was past from the original and said: It is an incidental matter in which there is an apparent criticism, since being incidental removes the disagreement that he first reported. He said: (It may be said: He does not need it) etc. He said in al-Nahr: This is an apparent oversight, for the subject of the statement of al-Jami' is not that someone else drove, but rather even if no one drove it after he caught up, he becomes muhrim according to the narration of al-Jami'. In al-Fath there is no reasoning for what is in al-Jami' with this; rather he mentioned an independent issue after reporting the disagreement: that he caught up but did not drive, and someone else drove, then it is like his driving because the action of the agent in the presence of the principal is like the action of the principal. Yes, this must be based on the narration of the original: that it is contrary to the principle. The conclusion is that conjunction in the hadith apparently requires difference between them, and the need for transfer from the lexical meaning in the case of its estimation is contrary to the principle, so the apparent is the absence of transfer. So they conflict, and we gave preponderance to what we hold due to what is established in the hadith of Jabir: 'We used to slaughter the badana for seven people.' It was said: 'And the cow?' He said: 'Is it not from the badan?' Muslim reported it in his Sahih. The fruit of the disagreement appears when one undertakes a badana: if he intends something, it is what he intended, because the intended is from the possibilities of his statement, like he explicitly stated. If he had no intention, he owes a cow or a camel, and he sacrifices it wherever he wishes according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], contrary to Abu Yusuf, for he analogizes it to the sacrifice (hadi), and it is specific to Mecca by agreement. The two analogized it to the case where one undertakes a camel, which is not specific to Mecca by agreement. Thus in al-Mabsut. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary Al-Bahr al-Raiq. It addresses the conditions under which sending a sacrificial animal (badana) ahead of a pilgrim makes the pilgrim a muhrim (in a state of ihram). The key ruling: sending an animal alone does not make one muhrim until the person catches up with the animal and intends ihram. However, there is one exception: the badana for tamattu' (combining umrah and hajj) or qiran. For these, the pilgrim becomes muhrim immediately without needing to catch up, because the animal is a specific ritual of hajj. The passage explains that tamattu' includes both the customary tamattu' and qiran, as the Quranic verse for tamattu' serves as the proof for both. The author notes that since tamattu' occurs during the hajj months, there is no need to restrict the timing of sending. The commentator, following al-Jami' al-Saghir, stipulates only catching up as a condition, not driving the animal initially, although al-Mabsut includes both. The reasoning for this is that if the pilgrim catches up, his intention combines with the act of being with the animal, which is a characteristic of the ritual. For the exceptional case, the act itself is a characteristic of hajj, so the pilgrim becomes muhrim. The passage also discusses specific actions like covering, marking (ish'ar), and garlanding (taqlid). None of these alone make one muhrim. Marking is disliked by Abu Hanifa because it causes bleeding, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it good. Garlanding is a sunnah but only for the sacrificial animal, not for a sheep. The passage concludes that intention alone without talbiyyah does not make one muhrim, and talbiyyah alone without intention is also insufficient. The definition of badana includes both camels and cows, based on linguistic and legal usage, supported by a hadith from Jabir in Sahih Muslim that 'we used to slaughter the badana for seven people' and when asked about a cow, the Prophet said 'Is it not from the badan?' This hadith is used to rule that a cow is included in badana. The practical difference appears when one vows a badana: if he intends a specific animal, it is valid; if he has no intention, his obligation is a cow or a camel. There is a difference of opinion where Abu Yusuf analogizes to the hadi (sacrifice of hajj) which is limited to Mecca, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in the latter part) analogize to a camel vow which is not limited, so they allow sacrificing anywhere.

Key Terms
بدنة (badana): A sacrificial animal, specifically a camel or a cow, according to Hanafi definition.
إشعار (ish'ar): Branding or marking the animal by cutting the hump to cause blood flow.
تقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the animal with a pair of sandals or similar to indicate it is a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does sending a badana (sacrificial animal) make a person a muhrim?
A) Immediately upon sending the animal
B) Only when the person catches up to the animal and intends ihram
C) Only if the animal is a sheep
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Sending a badana does not confer ihram until catching up, except for tamattu', and badana includes cows by Hanafi definition.

The Three Types of Hajj and Their Hanafi Ranking
Definition and ranking of the three forms of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of Hajj and their preferred order according to the Hanafi school, and define the key conditions for each.

Core Idea
Qiran is the best form of Hajj, followed by Tamattu', then Ifrad.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on the three types of Hajj. You will learn the definitions of Qiran, Tamattu', and Ifrad, and understand why the Hanafi school ranks Qiran first. We will also address the hadith that some use to argue against Tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
From the passage, list the three types of Hajj in the order mentioned: Qiran, Tamattu', Ifrad.
This order is the Hanafi ranking of virtue.
2
Define each type
For each type, extract the defining characteristics. Qiran: combining 'umrah and hajj with a single ihram from the miqat. Tamattu': performing 'umrah first in the months of hajj, then performing hajj in the same year with a sacrifice. Ifrad: performing hajj alone without 'umrah.
Note the conditions for each, e.g., for Tamattu', the 'umrah must be in the months of hajj and there must be no intercourse between the two.
3
Understand the ranking evidence
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as best based on general preference and the actions of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage notes consensus on permissibility of all three.
The forbiddance by 'Umar and 'Uthman is interpreted as dislike (tanzih), not prohibition, preserving the consensus.
4
Distinguish the four categories of muhrim
The passage describes four categories: mufrid for hajj, mufrid for 'umrah, mutamatti', and qarin. Understand the subcategories under qarin (three ways) and note that the third way is offensive (musi').
5
Address cross-madhhab difference
Note that the Shafi'i school prefers Tamattu' over Qiran. The passage does not detail their evidence, but this awareness is important for comparative fiqh.

قوله : ( في القسمين الأولين أي من أقسام القارن الثلاثة .
Chapter of Qiran: It is the best, then Tamattu', then Ifrad. It is that one raises his voice with 'umrah and hajj from the miqat and says... [the text repeats the badana discussion] ... Similarly, Chapter of Qiran: It is a verbal noun from qarana, form of nasara, and fa'al comes as a verbal noun from the triliteral like libas, meaning bringing two things together: one says qarantu al-ba'irayni when you bring them together with a rope. Its legal meaning will come. Then know that there are four types of muhrim: Mufrid (for hajj) if he enters ihram for hajj alone; or Mufrid for 'umrah if he enters ihram for 'umrah outside the months of hajj and performs tawaf whether he performs hajj that year or not, or he performs tawaf in them and does not perform hajj that year; or he enters ihram in the months of hajj and performs tawaf similarly and does not perform hajj that year; or he performs hajj and has valid intercourse with his family. Mutamatti': one who performs more than half of the tawaf of 'umrah in the months of hajj after entering ihram for it only, then performs hajj that year without valid intercourse. Qarin: one who enters ihram for both together, or adds the ihram of hajj to the ihram of 'umrah before performing most of its tawaf, or adds the ihram of 'umrah to the ihram of hajj before performing tawaf al-qudum even if one circuit. There is no offense in the first two types; the third is a blameworthy qarin. As for ambiguous ihram, like entering ihram for an unspecified rite then assigning it to whichever of hajj or 'umrah or both, and suspended ihram like entering ihram with an ihram like Zayd's, these are not outside the four, as is clear. His statement: (It is best, then Tamattu', then Ifrad) explains two matters: first, the permissibility of all three, which is unanimous except what is established in the two Sahihs from 'Umar and 'Uthman that they used to forbid Tamattu'. Scholars interpreted it as a prohibitive of dislike (tanzih), carrying [the hadith] on... Chapter of Qiran: outside the months of hajj. His statement: 'or he performs tawaf in them' i.e., the months of hajj. His statement: 'and he performs tawaf similarly' i.e., in. His statement: 'similarly' i.e., in the months of hajj. His statement: 'in the first two types' i.e., of the three categories of qarin.
Source pages p. 625

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling from the commentary on the chapter of Qiran. It begins by stating the preference order among the three types of Hajj: Qiran (combining 'umrah and hajj from the miqat) is the best, followed by Tamattu' (performing 'umrah first then hajj in the same year with a sacrifice), then Ifrad (performing hajj alone). The author then defines Qiran linguistically as 'bringing two things together' and explains the four categories of muhrim (those in ihram): (1) Mufrid for hajj, (2) Mufrid for 'umrah, (3) Mutamatti', and (4) Qarin. Each has conditions. For a Qarin, there are three ways: entering ihram for both at once, adding hajj to 'umrah before most tawaf, or adding 'umrah to hajj before tawaf al-qudum. The third is considered offensive (musi'). Ambiguous and suspended ihram are subsumed under these four. The passage also notes the consensus (ijma') on the permissibility of all three types, addressing the reports that 'Umar and 'Uthman forbade Tamattu'; scholars interpret this as a recommendation (tanzih) not prohibition. The commentary further clarifies the meaning of certain phrases in the matn, such as 'outside the months of hajj' and 'in the first two types' of qarin.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): The type of Hajj where one enters ihram for both 'umrah and hajj together from the miqat.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): The type of Hajj where one performs 'umrah first in the months of hajj, then performs hajj in the same year, offering a sacrifice.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): The type of Hajj where one performs hajj alone without 'umrah.
مفرد (mufrid): One who performs ifrad (hajj alone) or one who performs 'umrah alone.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu' (combined 'umrah and hajj with a break).
قارن (qarin): One who performs qiran (combining 'umrah and hajj on one ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of Hajj is considered the best according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the most virtuous form of Hajj, followed by Tamattu' and then Ifrad, with all three being permissible.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Preference for Qiran and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on which Hajj type is best.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the most excellent type of Hajj and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the evidence from this passage.

Core Idea
Qiran is superior because the Prophet combined Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute regarding which form of Hajj is most excellent. The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the best, followed by Tamattu', then Ifrad. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools prefer Ifrad, while the Hanbali school prefers Tamattu'. The dispute hinges on how to reconcile conflicting hadiths about the Prophet's own Hajj. Let's walk through the evidence and the Hanafi reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of Hajj
State the three valid forms: Qiran, Tamattu', and Ifrad, and briefly define each. This establishes the subject of the dispute.
Refer to key terms in the source.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to the passage, the Hanafi view is that Qiran is afdal (most excellent), then Tamattu', then Ifrad. Confirm this from the source.
The text says: 'تفضيل القرآن ثم التمتع ثم الإفراد'
3
Find the Hanafi proof from the Quran and Sunnah
Locate the Quranic verses cited and the hadith that indicate the Prophet was a Qarin. The passage uses verse 2:196 as evidence for Qiran and multiple hadiths from Ali, Anas, etc.
The hadith of Umar about the command to say 'Umrah in Hajj' is a strong proof.
4
Identify the opposing Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school relies on hadiths from Jabir, Ibn Umar, etc., that the Prophet entered Ihram for Hajj alone (Ifrad). Also, they use verse 3:97 which commands Hajj alone.
The passage mentions: 'ثبت في الصحيح من رواية جابر وابن عمر وابن عباس وعائشة'
5
Apply the Hanafi reconciliation of narrations
The Hanafi scholars reconcile by noting that the Prophet initially intended Ifrad but later added Umrah, becoming a Qarin. This explains why some heard him say 'Labbaik bi-Hajj' and others heard 'Labbaik bi-Hajj wa Umrah'.
The passage quotes al-Nawawi's resolution: 'It is the correct view that he first entered Ihram for Hajj alone, then added Umrah, so he became a Qarin.'
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is which type is recommended. Hanafis recommend Qiran, Shafi'is recommend Ifrad, Hanbalis recommend Tamattu'.
All are valid; the dispute is over afdaliyya (superiority).

ثبت عن ابن عمر وعائشة في الصحيحين وعن ابن عباس فيما رواه الترمذي وحسنه، وعن عمران بن الحصين في الصحيحين، وجمع أئمتنا بين الروايات بأن سبب رواية الإفراد سماع رأى تلبيته بالحج وحده، ورواية التمتع سماع من سمعه يلبي بالعمرة، ورواية القرآن سماع من سمعه يلبي بهما. وهذا لأنه لا مانع من إفراد ذكر نسك في التلبية وعدم ذكر شيء وجهة أخرى مع نية القرآن فهو نظير سبب الاختلاف في تلبيته عليه السلام أكانت الصلاة أو عند استواء ناقته أو حين علا على البيداء فروى كل بحسب ما سمع، ومما يرجح القران أن من روى الإفراد روى التمتع فتناقض بخلاف من روى التمتع وهو بلغة القرآن الكريم وعرف الصحابة أعم من القران وترجح الفرد المسمى بالقران في الاصطلاح بما في الصحيح عن عمر قال : سمعت رسول الله له بوادي العقيق يقول : أتاني الليلة آت من ربي عز وجل فقال : صل في هذا الوادي المبارك ركعتين وقل عمرة في حجة. ولا بد له من امتثال ما أمر به في مقامه الذي هو وحي ولائمتنا ترجيحات كثيرة.
وقال النووي في شرح المهذب : والصواب الذي نعتقده أنه أحرم بالحج أولاً مفرداً ثم أدخل عليه العمرة فصار قارناً، وإدخال العمرة على الحج جائز على أحد القولين عندنا، وعلى الأصح لا يجوز لنا وجاز للنبي ل تلك السنة للحاجة وأمر به في قوله لبيك عمرة وحجة، فمن روى أنه كان مفرداً اعتمد أول الإحرام ومن روى أنه كان قارناً اعتمد آخره، ومن روى أنه كان متمتعاً أراد لتمتع اللغوي وهو الانتفاع بأن كفاه عن النسكين فعل واحد، ويؤيده أنه عليه السلام لم يعتمر تلك السنة عمرة مفردة لا قبل الحج ولا بعده، وقد قدمنا أن القرآن أفضل من إفراد الحج من غير عمرة بلا خلاف ولو جعلت حجته عليه السلام مفردة لزم أن لا يكون اعتمر تلك السنة ولم يقل أحد أن الحج وحده أفضل من القرآن ا هـ. وبهذا تبين صحة ما في النهاية من أن محل الاختلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي إنما هو أن إفراد كل نسك بإحرام في سنة واحدة أفضل أو الجمع بينهما بإحرام واحداً أفضل، وأنه لم يقل أحد بتفضيل الحج وحده على القران وتبين به بطلان ما ذكره الشارح هنا رداً على صاحب النهاية. وما روي عن محمد أنه قال حجة كوفية وعمرة كوفية أفضل عندي من القرآن فليس بموافق لمذهب الشافعي في تفضيل الإفراد فإنه يفضل الإفراد سواء أتى بنسكين في سفرة
فليحرص الحاج مهما أمكنه على صونه عن مثل هذه الأمور لئلا يضيع سعيه وماله ا هـ قوله : (ولو جعلت حجته عليه السلام مفردة (الخ أي من غير إدخال العمرة عليها، وهذا من كلام النووي كما لا يخفى لا كما فهمه الرملي قوله وتبين) به بطلان ما ذكره الشارح حيث قال بعد نقل كلام النهاية ولم ينقل فيه شيئاً وإنما قاله خرراً واستدلالاً بمواضع الاحتجاج، وإطلاقهم أن القرآن أفضل من الإفراد يرده لأن ظاهره يراد به الإفراد بالحج. وأيضاً لو كان كما قاله لكان محمد مع الشافعي وكلهم
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran. From: for the people regarding what is best, not that they consider it invalid while acting upon the noble verse. Interpreting it as meaning dissolving Hajj into Umrah is weak because the context of the hadith in Sahih requires otherwise. It is established by the Book and Sunnah as well. As for the first, His statement 'And to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House' [Al-Imran:97] is evidence for Ifrad. His statement 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' [Al-Baqara:196] is evidence for Qiran. His statement 'And whoever enjoys the Umrah to the Hajj' [Al-Baqara:196] is evidence for Tamattu'. As for the second, what is in the two Sahihs from the hadith of Aisha: she said, 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage. Some of us entered Ihram for Umrah, some for Hajj and Umrah, and some for Hajj. The Messenger of Allah entered Ihram for Hajj.' In a narration by Muslim: 'Some of us entered Ihram for Hajj alone, some for Qiran, and some for Tamattu'.' Second: preferring Qiran, then Tamattu', then Ifrad. Malik and al-Shafi'i preferred Ifrad, and Ahmad preferred Tamattu'. The origin is the difference regarding his (the Prophet's) Hajj. Many people have spoken about it, and the most extensive in that is Imam al-Tahawi, for he spoke about it in over a thousand pages. Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'There is nothing easier than this difference, even though error in it is ugly because it is permissible.' Meaning that since all three are permissible, there is no change of ruling in the disagreement. Since it is one Hajj and they did not agree on its transmission, their difference is ugly from them. What makes it likely that he (peace be upon him) was a Qarin is what Ali narrated in the two Sahihs, Anas in the two Sahihs with many narrations, Imran ibn Husayn in Sahih Muslim, Umar ibn al-Khattab in Sahih al-Bukhari, Abu Dawood, and al-Nasa'i, Hafsah in the two Sahihs, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari in the two Sahihs. What makes it likely that he (peace be upon him) was a Mufrid is what is established in Sahih from the narration of Jabir, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha. And what makes it likely that he was a Mutamatti' is... And with: His saying: 'And Ahmad preferred Tamattu'' said the deceased Sheikh Abd al-Rahman Afandi al-Imadi, Mufti of Damascus, in his ritual book called al-Mustata' min al-Zad: The summary: When I performed Hajj I chose Tamattu' because it is better than Ifrad and easier than Qiran because of the hardship on the Qarin of combining the performance of the two rites and because of the two bloods required for transgression. Also for another reason: Tamattu' is more fitting for the likes of us, and it is possible to preserve the Ihram of Hajj for the Mutamatti' from lewdness, wickedness, and argument. So it is hoped that his Hajj will be accepted because it is interpreted that there is no lewdness, no wickedness, and no argument in it. The Mutamatti' is closer to avoiding that because he does not enter Ihram from the Miqat except for Umrah only, and he enters Ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyya from the Haram. So he can guard himself in those two days, and thus his Hajj is safe. Unlike the Mufrid and Qarin, they remain in Ihram for Hajj for more than ten days, and rarely can a person guard himself over such a period. The teacher of our teachers, Shihab al-Din al-Munini, said in his ritual book: It is valuable speech. He means that Qiran in itself is better than Tamattu', but sometimes something may accompany it that makes it outweighed in comparison to Tamattu'. So if it is a choice between a man performing Hajj as Qarin but his Ihram is not safe from lewdness, wickedness, and argument, and he performs it as Mutamatti' and his Ihram is safe from them, then the better in his case is to perform Hajj as Mutamatti' so his Hajj is safe and accepted, because it is the duty of a lifetime. The matter between: He performs Hajj as Mutamatti'... [Page 627] ...established from Ibn Umar and Aisha in the two Sahihs, from Ibn Abbas in what al-Tirmidhi narrated and deemed good, and from Imran ibn Husayn in the two Sahihs. Our imams reconciled the narrations by saying that the reason for the narration of Ifrad was because he heard his talbiyah with Hajj alone; the narration of Tamattu' was from one who heard him making talbiyah with Umrah; and the narration of Qiran was from one who heard him making talbiyah with both. This is because there is no prohibition of mentioning one rite in the talbiyah and not mentioning something else while having the intention of Qiran. It is similar to the reason for the difference regarding his talbiyah: was it at the time of prayer, or when his she-camel stood up, or when he ascended al-Bayda'? Each narrated according to what he heard. Among the things that support Qiran is that those who narrated Ifrad also narrated Tamattu', so they contradicted themselves, unlike those who narrated Tamattu' (which is the language of the Quran and the custom of the Companions is more general than Qiran) and the preferred individual called Qiran terminologically is supported by what is in Sahih on the authority of Umar who said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah in the valley of al-Aqiq say: 'Last night a visitor came to me from my Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and said: Pray two rak'ahs in this blessed valley and say: Umrah included in Hajj.' And he must obey what he was commanded in his station, which is revelation. Our imams have many preferential proofs. And al-Nawawi said in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: 'The correct view that we believe is that he first entered Ihram for Hajj alone, then he added Umrah to it, so he became a Qarin. Adding Umrah to Hajj is permissible according to one of the two views in our school; according to the most correct, it is not permissible for us, but it was permissible for the Prophet at that time due to necessity, and he was commanded to do so in his saying: 'Labbayk bi-Umrah wa-Hajj.' So whoever narrated that he was a Mufrid relied on the beginning of the Ihram; whoever narrated that he was a Qarin relied on its end; and whoever narrated that he was a Mutamatti' intended the linguistic Tamattu', which is benefit, because performing one act sufficed for both rites. Supporting this is that he did not perform a separate Umrah that year, neither before nor after Hajj. And we have already stated that Qiran is better than Ifrad of Hajj without Umrah without any disagreement. If his Hajj were considered Ifrad alone, it would necessarily mean that he did not perform Umrah that year, and no one has said that Hajj alone is better than Qiran.' And with this, the correctness of what is in al-Nihayah is clear: that the point of difference between us and al-Shafi'i is only whether performing each rite with a separate Ihram in one year is better, or combining them with one Ihram is better. And that no one has said that Hajj alone is better than Qiran. And it clarifies the falsehood of what the commentator mentioned here in refutation of the author of al-Nihayah. And what is narrated from Muhammad that he said: 'A Hajj from Kufa and an Umrah from Kufa are better in my view than Qiran' does not agree with the school of al-Shafi'i in preferring Ifrad, because he prefers Ifrad whether one performs two rites in one journey. So let the pilgrim strive as much as possible to preserve himself from such matters lest his effort and wealth be wasted. End. His saying: 'And if his Hajj were considered Ifrad alone' etc., meaning without including Umrah in it. This is from the words of al-Nawawi, as is not hidden, not as al-Ramli understood. His saying: 'And it clarifies the falsehood of what the commentator mentioned' where he said after quoting the words of al-Nihayah: 'And he did not quote anything in it; rather he said it extemporaneously and by citing places of argument. And their statement that Qiran is better than Ifrad is rejected because its apparent meaning is Ifrad by Hajj. Also, if it were as he said, then Muhammad would be with al-Shafi'i and all of them.'
Source pages p. 626

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the preference (afdaliyya) among the three types of Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj alone), Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram), and Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break of Ihram). The Hanafi position is that Qiran is superior, followed by Tamattu', then Ifrad. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools prefer Ifrad, while the Hanbali school prefers Tamattu'. The passage first presents Quranic evidence for each type: verse 3:97 for Ifrad, verse 2:196 for Qiran, and verse 2:196 for Tamattu'. It then cites a hadith from Aisha in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim showing that Companions did all three types, and the Prophet entered Ihram for Hajj alone, which some interpret as Ifrad. However, other narrations indicate he was a Qarin. The commentator reconciles these by noting that different Companions heard different parts of the talbiyah. The passage also includes a practical consideration from a later scholar, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Imadi, who recommends Tamattu' for ordinary people because it is easier and allows better preservation of Ihram from sins. The passage then refutes the claim that the Prophet's Hajj was purely Ifrad, quoting al-Nawawi's resolution: the Prophet started with Ifrad but later added Umrah, becoming a Qarin. Therefore, Qiran is better than Ifrad. Finally, the commentator defends the Hanafi position against a remark by the original commentator (al-Sharh) who seemed to suggest that 'Qiran is better than Ifrad' actually means 'Ifrad is better than Qiran' because the term 'Ifrad' might mean Hajj alone. This is rebutted, and it is shown that no scholar considers Hajj alone better than Qiran. Even a weak report from Muhammad al-Shaybani that 'a Hajj from Kufa and an Umrah from Kufa' (i.e., separate) is better than Qiran does not align with Shafi'i's view, because Shafi'i prefers Ifrad even when both are done in one journey.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single Ihram with the intention of performing both together.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during the Hajj months, then exiting Ihram and re-entering for Hajj on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah in the same journey; the pilgrim enters Ihram for Hajj only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj is the most excellent?
A) Ifrad (Hajj alone)
B) Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram)
C) Tamattu' (Umrah first then Hajj)
D) All are equally excellent

Key Takeaway
Qiran is the most excellent form of Hajj in the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's example and divine command.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Practical Guidance: Choosing Hajj Type Based on Piety
Practical advice on choosing Hajj type according to personal capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate when Tamattu' might be preferable for an individual pilgrim based on the principles of preserving Ihram sanctity.

Core Idea
The best Hajj is the one that preserves piety, even if Qiran is theoretically superior.

While the Hanafi school holds Qiran as the most excellent type, this passage includes a practical consideration from later scholars: if a person fears they cannot maintain the sanctity of Ihram for the long period required by Qiran or Ifrad, then Tamattu' may be better for them because its Ihram period is shorter. This lesson explores that nuanced application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the theoretical superiority of Qiran
Recall from the previous lesson that Qiran is afdal because it combines both rites in one Ihram. This is the default recommendation.
This is the starting point for the practical consideration.
2
Identify the practical concern
The passage warns that a Qarin or Mufrid remains in Ihram for more than ten days, making it difficult to avoid lewdness (rafath), wickedness (fusuq), and argument (jidal). These invalidate the reward of Hajj.
The hadith: 'There is no lewdness, no wickedness, and no argument in Hajj.'
3
Apply the consideration from al-Imadi
Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Imadi chose Tamattu' because it is easier and safer: the Ihram for Hajj is only two days (from 8th to 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah), so one can guard against sins more easily.
This is a personal choice based on sincerity, not a change in the madhhab ruling.
4
Conclude with the principle
The passage concludes: 'Qiran in itself is better than Tamattu', but if a person cannot maintain piety in Qiran, Tamattu' is better for them.' This shows that individual circumstances matter.
This is an application of the maxim 'Al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions).

ثبت عن ابن عمر وعائشة في الصحيحين وعن ابن عباس فيما رواه الترمذي وحسنه، وعن عمران بن الحصين في الصحيحين، وجمع أئمتنا بين الروايات بأن سبب رواية الإفراد سماع رأى تلبيته بالحج وحده، ورواية التمتع سماع من سمعه يلبي بالعمرة، ورواية القرآن سماع من سمعه يلبي بهما. وهذا لأنه لا مانع من إفراد ذكر نسك في التلبية وعدم ذكر شيء وجهة أخرى مع نية القرآن فهو نظير سبب الاختلاف في تلبيته عليه السلام أكانت الصلاة أو عند استواء ناقته أو حين علا على البيداء فروى كل بحسب ما سمع، ومما يرجح القران أن من روى الإفراد روى التمتع فتناقض بخلاف من روى التمتع وهو بلغة القرآن الكريم وعرف الصحابة أعم من القران وترجح الفرد المسمى بالقران في الاصطلاح بما في الصحيح عن عمر قال : سمعت رسول الله له بوادي العقيق يقول : أتاني الليلة آت من ربي عز وجل فقال : صل في هذا الوادي المبارك ركعتين وقل عمرة في حجة. ولا بد له من امتثال ما أمر به في مقامه الذي هو وحي ولائمتنا ترجيحات كثيرة.
وقال النووي في شرح المهذب : والصواب الذي نعتقده أنه أحرم بالحج أولاً مفرداً ثم أدخل عليه العمرة فصار قارناً، وإدخال العمرة على الحج جائز على أحد القولين عندنا، وعلى الأصح لا يجوز لنا وجاز للنبي ل تلك السنة للحاجة وأمر به في قوله لبيك عمرة وحجة، فمن روى أنه كان مفرداً اعتمد أول الإحرام ومن روى أنه كان قارناً اعتمد آخره، ومن روى أنه كان متمتعاً أراد لتمتع اللغوي وهو الانتفاع بأن كفاه عن النسكين فعل واحد، ويؤيده أنه عليه السلام لم يعتمر تلك السنة عمرة مفردة لا قبل الحج ولا بعده، وقد قدمنا أن القرآن أفضل من إفراد الحج من غير عمرة بلا خلاف ولو جعلت حجته عليه السلام مفردة لزم أن لا يكون اعتمر تلك السنة ولم يقل أحد أن الحج وحده أفضل من القرآن ا هـ. وبهذا تبين صحة ما في النهاية من أن محل الاختلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي إنما هو أن إفراد كل نسك بإحرام في سنة واحدة أفضل أو الجمع بينهما بإحرام واحداً أفضل، وأنه لم يقل أحد بتفضيل الحج وحده على القران وتبين به بطلان ما ذكره الشارح هنا رداً على صاحب النهاية. وما روي عن محمد أنه قال حجة كوفية وعمرة كوفية أفضل عندي من القرآن فليس بموافق لمذهب الشافعي في تفضيل الإفراد فإنه يفضل الإفراد سواء أتى بنسكين في سفرة
فليحرص الحاج مهما أمكنه على صونه عن مثل هذه الأمور لئلا يضيع سعيه وماله ا هـ قوله : (ولو جعلت حجته عليه السلام مفردة (الخ أي من غير إدخال العمرة عليها، وهذا من كلام النووي كما لا يخفى لا كما فهمه الرملي قوله وتبين) به بطلان ما ذكره الشارح حيث قال بعد نقل كلام النهاية ولم ينقل فيه شيئاً وإنما قاله خرراً واستدلالاً بمواضع الاحتجاج، وإطلاقهم أن القرآن أفضل من الإفراد يرده لأن ظاهره يراد به الإفراد بالحج. وأيضاً لو كان كما قاله لكان محمد مع الشافعي وكلهم
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran. From: for the people regarding what is best, not that they consider it invalid while acting upon the noble verse. Interpreting it as meaning dissolving Hajj into Umrah is weak because the context of the hadith in Sahih requires otherwise. It is established by the Book and Sunnah as well. As for the first, His statement 'And to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House' [Al-Imran:97] is evidence for Ifrad. His statement 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' [Al-Baqara:196] is evidence for Qiran. His statement 'And whoever enjoys the Umrah to the Hajj' [Al-Baqara:196] is evidence for Tamattu'. As for the second, what is in the two Sahihs from the hadith of Aisha: she said, 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage. Some of us entered Ihram for Umrah, some for Hajj and Umrah, and some for Hajj. The Messenger of Allah entered Ihram for Hajj.' In a narration by Muslim: 'Some of us entered Ihram for Hajj alone, some for Qiran, and some for Tamattu'.' Second: preferring Qiran, then Tamattu', then Ifrad. Malik and al-Shafi'i preferred Ifrad, and Ahmad preferred Tamattu'. The origin is the difference regarding his (the Prophet's) Hajj. Many people have spoken about it, and the most extensive in that is Imam al-Tahawi, for he spoke about it in over a thousand pages. Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'There is nothing easier than this difference, even though error in it is ugly because it is permissible.' Meaning that since all three are permissible, there is no change of ruling in the disagreement. Since it is one Hajj and they did not agree on its transmission, their difference is ugly from them. What makes it likely that he (peace be upon him) was a Qarin is what Ali narrated in the two Sahihs, Anas in the two Sahihs with many narrations, Imran ibn Husayn in Sahih Muslim, Umar ibn al-Khattab in Sahih al-Bukhari, Abu Dawood, and al-Nasa'i, Hafsah in the two Sahihs, and Abu Musa al-Ash'ari in the two Sahihs. What makes it likely that he (peace be upon him) was a Mufrid is what is established in Sahih from the narration of Jabir, Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, and Aisha. And what makes it likely that he was a Mutamatti' is... And with: His saying: 'And Ahmad preferred Tamattu'' said the deceased Sheikh Abd al-Rahman Afandi al-Imadi, Mufti of Damascus, in his ritual book called al-Mustata' min al-Zad: The summary: When I performed Hajj I chose Tamattu' because it is better than Ifrad and easier than Qiran because of the hardship on the Qarin of combining the performance of the two rites and because of the two bloods required for transgression. Also for another reason: Tamattu' is more fitting for the likes of us, and it is possible to preserve the Ihram of Hajj for the Mutamatti' from lewdness, wickedness, and argument. So it is hoped that his Hajj will be accepted because it is interpreted that there is no lewdness, no wickedness, and no argument in it. The Mutamatti' is closer to avoiding that because he does not enter Ihram from the Miqat except for Umrah only, and he enters Ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyya from the Haram. So he can guard himself in those two days, and thus his Hajj is safe. Unlike the Mufrid and Qarin, they remain in Ihram for Hajj for more than ten days, and rarely can a person guard himself over such a period. The teacher of our teachers, Shihab al-Din al-Munini, said in his ritual book: It is valuable speech. He means that Qiran in itself is better than Tamattu', but sometimes something may accompany it that makes it outweighed in comparison to Tamattu'. So if it is a choice between a man performing Hajj as Qarin but his Ihram is not safe from lewdness, wickedness, and argument, and he performs it as Mutamatti' and his Ihram is safe from them, then the better in his case is to perform Hajj as Mutamatti' so his Hajj is safe and accepted, because it is the duty of a lifetime. The matter between: He performs Hajj as Mutamatti'... [Page 627] ...established from Ibn Umar and Aisha in the two Sahihs, from Ibn Abbas in what al-Tirmidhi narrated and deemed good, and from Imran ibn Husayn in the two Sahihs. Our imams reconciled the narrations by saying that the reason for the narration of Ifrad was because he heard his talbiyah with Hajj alone; the narration of Tamattu' was from one who heard him making talbiyah with Umrah; and the narration of Qiran was from one who heard him making talbiyah with both. This is because there is no prohibition of mentioning one rite in the talbiyah and not mentioning something else while having the intention of Qiran. It is similar to the reason for the difference regarding his talbiyah: was it at the time of prayer, or when his she-camel stood up, or when he ascended al-Bayda'? Each narrated according to what he heard. Among the things that support Qiran is that those who narrated Ifrad also narrated Tamattu', so they contradicted themselves, unlike those who narrated Tamattu' (which is the language of the Quran and the custom of the Companions is more general than Qiran) and the preferred individual called Qiran terminologically is supported by what is in Sahih on the authority of Umar who said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah in the valley of al-Aqiq say: 'Last night a visitor came to me from my Lord, Mighty and Majestic, and said: Pray two rak'ahs in this blessed valley and say: Umrah included in Hajj.' And he must obey what he was commanded in his station, which is revelation. Our imams have many preferential proofs. And al-Nawawi said in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab: 'The correct view that we believe is that he first entered Ihram for Hajj alone, then he added Umrah to it, so he became a Qarin. Adding Umrah to Hajj is permissible according to one of the two views in our school; according to the most correct, it is not permissible for us, but it was permissible for the Prophet at that time due to necessity, and he was commanded to do so in his saying: 'Labbayk bi-Umrah wa-Hajj.' So whoever narrated that he was a Mufrid relied on the beginning of the Ihram; whoever narrated that he was a Qarin relied on its end; and whoever narrated that he was a Mutamatti' intended the linguistic Tamattu', which is benefit, because performing one act sufficed for both rites. Supporting this is that he did not perform a separate Umrah that year, neither before nor after Hajj. And we have already stated that Qiran is better than Ifrad of Hajj without Umrah without any disagreement. If his Hajj were considered Ifrad alone, it would necessarily mean that he did not perform Umrah that year, and no one has said that Hajj alone is better than Qiran.' And with this, the correctness of what is in al-Nihayah is clear: that the point of difference between us and al-Shafi'i is only whether performing each rite with a separate Ihram in one year is better, or combining them with one Ihram is better. And that no one has said that Hajj alone is better than Qiran. And it clarifies the falsehood of what the commentator mentioned here in refutation of the author of al-Nihayah. And what is narrated from Muhammad that he said: 'A Hajj from Kufa and an Umrah from Kufa are better in my view than Qiran' does not agree with the school of al-Shafi'i in preferring Ifrad, because he prefers Ifrad whether one performs two rites in one journey. So let the pilgrim strive as much as possible to preserve himself from such matters lest his effort and wealth be wasted. End. His saying: 'And if his Hajj were considered Ifrad alone' etc., meaning without including Umrah in it. This is from the words of al-Nawawi, as is not hidden, not as al-Ramli understood. His saying: 'And it clarifies the falsehood of what the commentator mentioned' where he said after quoting the words of al-Nihayah: 'And he did not quote anything in it; rather he said it extemporaneously and by citing places of argument. And their statement that Qiran is better than Ifrad is rejected because its apparent meaning is Ifrad by Hajj. Also, if it were as he said, then Muhammad would be with al-Shafi'i and all of them.'
Source pages p. 626

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the preference (afdaliyya) among the three types of Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj alone), Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihram), and Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year with a break of Ihram). The Hanafi position is that Qiran is superior, followed by Tamattu', then Ifrad. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools prefer Ifrad, while the Hanbali school prefers Tamattu'. The passage first presents Quranic evidence for each type: verse 3:97 for Ifrad, verse 2:196 for Qiran, and verse 2:196 for Tamattu'. It then cites a hadith from Aisha in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim showing that Companions did all three types, and the Prophet entered Ihram for Hajj alone, which some interpret as Ifrad. However, other narrations indicate he was a Qarin. The commentator reconciles these by noting that different Companions heard different parts of the talbiyah. The passage also includes a practical consideration from a later scholar, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Imadi, who recommends Tamattu' for ordinary people because it is easier and allows better preservation of Ihram from sins. The passage then refutes the claim that the Prophet's Hajj was purely Ifrad, quoting al-Nawawi's resolution: the Prophet started with Ifrad but later added Umrah, becoming a Qarin. Therefore, Qiran is better than Ifrad. Finally, the commentator defends the Hanafi position against a remark by the original commentator (al-Sharh) who seemed to suggest that 'Qiran is better than Ifrad' actually means 'Ifrad is better than Qiran' because the term 'Ifrad' might mean Hajj alone. This is rebutted, and it is shown that no scholar considers Hajj alone better than Qiran. Even a weak report from Muhammad al-Shaybani that 'a Hajj from Kufa and an Umrah from Kufa' (i.e., separate) is better than Qiran does not align with Shafi'i's view, because Shafi'i prefers Ifrad even when both are done in one journey.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single Ihram with the intention of performing both together.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during the Hajj months, then exiting Ihram and re-entering for Hajj on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah in the same journey; the pilgrim enters Ihram for Hajj only.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason a person might choose Tamattu' over Qiran?
A) Tamattu' is easier and requires fewer rituals.
B) Tamattu' allows the pilgrim to avoid the long Ihram period and preserve purity.
C) Tamattu' is more expensive but more rewarding.
D) Tamattu' is the only valid type for beginners.

Key Takeaway
While Qiran is theoretically best, Tamattu' may be practically better for those who cannot maintain Ihram sanctity for an extended period.

Definition of Qiran and Its Essential Conditions
Defining Qiran and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of qiran and identify its essential conditions (miqat, intention, being afaqi) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qiran is combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram from the miqat; intention, not utterance, is the key.

In this chapter, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the third form of Hajj: Qiran. Unlike ifrad and tamattu', qiran combines both acts in a single ihram from the miqat. Understanding its precise legal definition is essential because it determines the obligation of a dam and distinguishes qiran from mere combination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Qiran is a valid form of Hajj, sunnah but ifrad is superior. The passage focuses on the definition and conditions.
The ruling here is about the definition itself, not the superiority.
2
Parse the definition
The passage defines qiran as raising voice (ihlal) for both Umrah and Hajj from the miqat with a supplication. Note that 'ihlal' indicates recommended loudness.
Ihlal is used to emphasize the sunnah of loud talbiyah.
3
Understand the conditions
The qarin must be an afaqi (coming from outside the miqat). The definition covers literal and effective combination: if one intends one then the other before performing most of the tawaf of the first, it is effective combination.
Effective combination includes cases where the order is reversed, though blameworthy.
4
Distinguish intention from utterance
The phrase 'and say' refers to intention, not literal speech. The niyyah is the essence of ihram.
This is a standard Hanafi principle: intention suffices; verbalization is not required.
5
Recognize what is not a condition
The author did not stipulate that ihram or tawaf must occur within the months of Hajj, contrasting with tamattu'.
This will be elaborated in the next lesson regarding the dam.

باب القرآن وهو أن يهل بالعمرة والحج من الميقات ويقول اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني . وإنما عبر بالإهلال للإشارة إلى أن رفع الصوت بها مستحب . وأراد بالميقات ما ذكرنا وإنما ذكره للإشارة إلى أن القارن لا يكون إلا آفاقياً . وقلنا حقيقة أو حكماً ليدخل ما إذا أحرم بالعمرة ثم أحرم بالحج قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر أو أحرم بالحج ثم أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يطوف له وإن كان مسيئاً في الثاني كما قدمناه لوجود الجمع بينهما في الإحرام حكماً . والمراد من قوله ويقول النية لا التلفظ . ولم يشترط المصنف وقوع الإحرام في أشهر الحج أو طواف العمرة فيها كما هو شرط في التمتع لما روي عن محمد أنه لو طاف لعمرته في رمضان فهو قارن ولا دم عليه إن لم يطف لعمرته في أشهر الحج فتوهم بعضهم في هذه الرواية الفرق بين القران والتمتع فيه وليس كما توهموا فإن القرآن في هذه الرواية بمعنى الجمع لا القران الشرعي المصطلح عليه بدليل أنه نفي لازم القرآن بالمعنى الشرعي وهو لزوم الدم شكراً ونفي اللازم الشرعي نفي للملزوم الشرعي والحاصل أن النسك المستعقب للدم شكراً هو ما تحقق فيه فعل المشروع المرتفق به الناسخ لما كان في الجاهلية وذلك بفعل العمرة في أشهر الحج، فإن كان مع الجمع في الإحرام قبل أكثر طواف العمرة فهو المسمى بالقرآن وإلا فهو التمتع بالمعنى العرفي وكلاهما التمتع بالإطلاق القرآني وعرف الصحابة وهو في الحقيقة إطلاق اللغة الحصول الرفق به هذا كله على أصول المذهب. كذا في فتح القدير.
Chapter of Qiran: It is to raise one's voice with talbiyah for Umrah and Hajj from the miqat and say: O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, make them easy for me and accept them from me. He only expressed 'ihlal' to indicate that raising the voice with it is recommended. By miqat he meant what we mentioned; he mentioned it only to indicate that the qarin must be an afaqi (one coming from outside the miqat). We said 'literally or effectively' to include the case where one enters ihram for Umrah then for Hajj before performing most of her tawaf, or enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah before performing tawaf for it, even if he is blameworthy in the second as we mentioned earlier, because of the existence of combining them in ihram effectively. What he means by 'and say' is intention, not utterance. The author did not stipulate that the ihram occurs in the months of Hajj or that the tawaf of Umrah occurs in them, as is a condition in tamattu', due to what is narrated from Muhammad that if one performs tawaf for his Umrah in Ramadan, he is a qarin and there is no dam (blood sacrifice) upon him if he does not perform tawaf for his Umrah in the months of Hajj. Some misunderstood this narration as a difference between qiran and tamattu', but it is not as they imagined, because qiran in this narration means 'combination' not the technical, conventional qiran; the proof is that he negated a necessary consequence of qiran in the technical sense, which is the obligation of a dam as gratitude, and negating the necessary consequence is negating the necessary precondition. The summary: the rite that necessitates a dam as gratitude is that in which the legislated practice of comfort is realized, i.e., performing Umrah in the months of Hajj. If it is accompanied by combination in ihram before most of the tawaf of Umrah, it is called qiran; otherwise it is tamattu' in the customary sense. Both are tamattu' in the Quranic and sahabi usage, and in reality it is the linguistic usage of achieving ease. All this is according to the principles of the madhhab. This is in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the legal concept of Qiran in Hajj. It opens with the definition: Qiran is performing talbiyah for both Umrah and Hajj from the miqat with the intention expressed in the supplication. The author notes that raising the voice is recommended (mustahabb) and that the qarin must be an afaqi (coming from outside the miqat) because the miqat is the starting point. He then explains that the definition includes both literal and effective combination: if someone first assumes ihram for Umrah and later for Hajj before completing most of the Umrah tawaf, or vice versa, they are still qarin effectively, though the second case is blameworthy (because of breaking the sequence). The definition uses 'says' to mean intention (niyyah), not verbal utterance, because intention is the essence of ihram. The author (i.e., the matn writer of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not require that the ihram or tawaf occur in the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, Dhu al-Hijjah), unlike tamattu'. This is based on a narration from Imam Muhammad: if one performs tawaf for Umrah in Ramadan (i.e., before the months), he is still qarin and no dam is required if he did not perform tawaf in the months. Some scholars misunderstood this as distinguishing qiran from tamattu', but the correct interpretation is that 'qiran' here means simple combination, not the technical qiran that requires a dam. The narrator negates the dam (a necessary consequence of technical qiran), so the combination in such a case is not technical qiran. The dam as gratitude is only due when the act of comfort (i.e., performing Umrah in the months of Hajj) is realized. If there is combination in ihram before most of the Umrah tawaf, and the Umrah is performed in the months, that is technical qiran. Otherwise, it is tamattu'. Both types ultimately are forms of tamattu' in the Quranic sense and in the usage of the Companions, meaning the linguistic sense of achieving ease. This is the settled view of the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram from the miqat, with intention for both.
الميقات (al-miqat): The specific boundary from where ihram must be assumed; for an afaqi, it is the place designated for his region.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah (with tawaf and sa'y) in the months of Hajj, then later performing Hajj with a fresh ihram. This is contrasted with qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the phrase 'and say' (ويقول) in the definition of qiran refer to?
A) Raising the voice
B) The intention
C) The actual recitation of talbiyah
D) The contract of ihram

Key Takeaway
Qiran is defined by intention and ihram from miqat; timing of Umrah tawaf affects the dam, not the definition itself.

The Timing of Umrah Tawaf in Qiran: When is a Dam Required?
Clarifying the dam condition for qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the dam in qiran and distinguish between technical qiran and mere combination based on the narration from Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A qarin only owes a dam if the Umrah tawaf is performed in the months of Hajj; otherwise, the combination is still qiran but without dam.

The previous lesson defined qiran. This lesson delves into a critical nuance: the obligation of the dam (sacrifice) for a qarin. Based on a narration from Imam Muhammad, the Hanafi school clarifies that qiran can be realized in two ways: one that requires a dam (technical qiran) and one that does not (mere combination). Understanding this distinction prevents a common misunderstanding that could lead to incorrect fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of qiran
Qiran is combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram from the miqat with intention.
This was covered in Lesson 1.
2
Present the problematic narration
Imam Muhammad narrates that if one performs tawaf for Umrah in Ramadan (before Hajj months), he is a qarin but no dam is due.
The Arabic text is: 'لو طاف لعمرته في رمضان فهو قارن ولا دم عليه'.
3
Analyze the confusion
Some scholars mistakenly thought this means the months condition is not required for qiran, but that contradicts the usual rule that a qarin owes a dam.
This confusion arises from reading 'qiran' in its technical sense.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The narration uses 'qiran' in the linguistic sense (simple combination), not the technical term. The dam is a necessary consequence of technical qiran; negating the dam means the case is not technical qiran.
The author says: 'فإن القرآن في هذه الرواية بمعنى الجمع لا القران الشرعي'.
5
Conclude with the settled rule
Technical qiran requires both combination in ihram and Umrah tawaf in the months of Hajj. Mere combination without the months does not trigger the dam.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القرآن وهو أن يهل بالعمرة والحج من الميقات ويقول اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني . وإنما عبر بالإهلال للإشارة إلى أن رفع الصوت بها مستحب . وأراد بالميقات ما ذكرنا وإنما ذكره للإشارة إلى أن القارن لا يكون إلا آفاقياً . وقلنا حقيقة أو حكماً ليدخل ما إذا أحرم بالعمرة ثم أحرم بالحج قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر أو أحرم بالحج ثم أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يطوف له وإن كان مسيئاً في الثاني كما قدمناه لوجود الجمع بينهما في الإحرام حكماً . والمراد من قوله ويقول النية لا التلفظ . ولم يشترط المصنف وقوع الإحرام في أشهر الحج أو طواف العمرة فيها كما هو شرط في التمتع لما روي عن محمد أنه لو طاف لعمرته في رمضان فهو قارن ولا دم عليه إن لم يطف لعمرته في أشهر الحج فتوهم بعضهم في هذه الرواية الفرق بين القران والتمتع فيه وليس كما توهموا فإن القرآن في هذه الرواية بمعنى الجمع لا القران الشرعي المصطلح عليه بدليل أنه نفي لازم القرآن بالمعنى الشرعي وهو لزوم الدم شكراً ونفي اللازم الشرعي نفي للملزوم الشرعي والحاصل أن النسك المستعقب للدم شكراً هو ما تحقق فيه فعل المشروع المرتفق به الناسخ لما كان في الجاهلية وذلك بفعل العمرة في أشهر الحج، فإن كان مع الجمع في الإحرام قبل أكثر طواف العمرة فهو المسمى بالقرآن وإلا فهو التمتع بالمعنى العرفي وكلاهما التمتع بالإطلاق القرآني وعرف الصحابة وهو في الحقيقة إطلاق اللغة الحصول الرفق به هذا كله على أصول المذهب. كذا في فتح القدير.

Obligatory Order of Actions for the Qarin: Umrah before Hajj
Ruling on order of actions for qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the order of Umrah and Hajj for the qarin and explain the consequence of reversing the order.

Core Idea
The qarin must perform Umrah actions before Hajj; reversal reassigns the tawaf to Umrah.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the sequence of rituals for a qarin. The author emphasizes that performing Umrah before Hajj is not merely recommended but obligatory (wajib), based on the Quranic verse. Understanding this order is crucial because reversing it has specific consequences for the validity of the intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sequence of performing Umrah tawaf and sa'y before Hajj tawaf and sa'y. Ruling: wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:196: 'So whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj'. The word 'ila' indicates Hajj as the goal.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The preposition 'ila' in Arabic implies that the action before it must be completed before reaching the limit. Thus Umrah must precede Hajj.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub
4
Determine the consequence of violation
If the qarin reverses by doing Hajj tawaf first, that tawaf is repurposed for Umrah, nullifying his intention for Hajj tawaf. He must repeat a tawaf for Hajj.
5
Note the prohibition of shaving before Nahr
The qarin cannot shave between Umrah and Hajj; doing so incurs a penalty (dam).
Shaving violates both ihrams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحج كما مر ) يعني يأتي بأفعال العمرة أولاً من الطواف والسعي بين الصفا والمروة والرمل في الأشواط الثلاثة والسعي بين الميلين الأخضرين وصلاة ركعتي الطواف ثم يأتي بأفعال الحج كلها ثانياً فيبدأ بطواف القدوم ويسعى بعده إن شاء، وهذا الترتيب أعني تقديم العمرة في أفعال الحج واجب لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج جلع الحج غاية وهو شامل للقران والتمتع كما قدمناه فأفاد أنه لو طاف أولاً لحجته وسعى لها ثم طاف لعمرته وسعى لها فطوافه الأول وسعيه يكون اللعمرة ونيته لغو، ولم يذكر الحلق للعمرة لأنه لا يتحلل بينهما بالحلق فلو حلق كان جناية على الإحرامين، أما على إحرام الحج فظاهر لأن أوان التحلل فيه يوم النحر، وأما على إحرام العمرة فكذلك لأن أوان تحلل القارن يوم النحر كما صرح به الإمام محمد. قال الشارح : ويؤيده أن المتمتع إذا ساق الهدي وفرغ من أفعال العمرة وحلق يجب عليه الدم ولا اشتراط فعل أكثر العمرة في أشهر الحج قوله: (لا القران الشرعي الخ قال في شرح اللباب: والذي يظهر لي أنه قارن بالمعنى الشرعي أيضاً كما هو المتبادر من إطلاق قول محمد وغيره أنه قارن، وبدليل أنه إذا ارتكب محظوراً يتعدد عليه الجزاء، وغايته أنه ليس عليه هدى شكر لأن أداءه لم يقع على الوجه المسنون المقرر في الشريعة من إيقاع أكثر العمرة في الأشهر فإنه من وجه في حكم من أفرد بعمرة في غير الأشهر ثم أفرد بالحج فإنه ليس بقارن إجماعاً ا هـ قوله : ( فيبدأ بطواف القدوم) سينص المؤلف على أن المتمتع يرمل في طوافه والظاهر أن القارن كذلك، ثم رأيته في الوالوالجية قال : ولا يرمل القارن والمفرد إلا في طواف التحية ولا يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد طواف الزيارة، أما المتمتع برمل في طواف الزيارة لأنه يسعى بعده بخلاف المفرد والقارن لأنهما لا يسعيان بعده لوجود السعي عقب طواف التحية، والسنة أن يرمل في كل طواف بعده سعي ا هـ.
His saying: (And he performs tawaf and sa'y for it then performs Hajj as mentioned) meaning he performs the actions of Umrah first: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwah, raml in three circuits, brisk walking between the green milestones, and the prayer of two rak'ahs after tawaf, then he performs all the actions of Hajj second, beginning with the tawaf of arrival and then sa'y if he wishes. This order, i.e., precedence of Umrah in the actions of Hajj, is obligatory due to Allah's saying: 'So whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj' making Hajj the goal, and this includes qiran and tamattu' as we mentioned. It follows that if he first performed tawaf for his Hajj and sa'y for it, then performed tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y for it, his first tawaf and sa'y will be for Umrah and his intention is wasted. He did not mention shaving for Umrah because he does not become halal between them by shaving; if he shaves, it is a violation against both ihrams. As for the ihram of Hajj, it is apparent because the time for tahallul is the Day of Nahr. As for the ihram of Umrah, similarly because the time for tahallul of the qarin is the Day of Nahr as stated explicitly by Imam Muhammad. The commentator said: It is supported that if a mutamatti' sends the hady and finishes the actions of Umrah and shaves, dam is obligatory upon him, and there is no condition of performing most of the Umrah in the months of Hajj. His saying: (not the technical qiran) etc. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: It appears to me that he is a qiran in the technical sense as is apparent from the absolute statement of Muhammad and others that he is a qiran, and the proof is that if he commits a prohibited act, the penalty multiplies for him. But the point is that he is not obligated to offer a dam of gratitude because his performance did not occur in the prescribed sunnah form of performing most of the Umrah in the months; thus in one respect he is like one who performed Umrah separately outside the months and then performed Hajj separately, and such a one is not a qarin by consensus. His saying: (he begins with tawaf of arrival) The author will mention that the mutamatti' does raml in his tawaf, and it appears that the qarin is similar. Then I saw in al-Walwaljiyyah: the qarin and the mufrid do not do raml except in the tawaf of greeting, and they do not do sa'y between Safa and Marwah after the tawaf of visit; as for the mutamatti', he does raml in the tawaf of visit because he performs sa'y afterwards, unlike the mufrid and qarin because they do not perform sa'y after it, due to the existence of sa'y after the tawaf of greeting. The sunnah is to do raml in every tawaf after which there is sa'y.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage explains the sequence of actions for a qarin (one performing Hajj with Umrah in one ihram). The qarin must first perform the actions of Umrah: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwah, with raml (quick pace with chest out) in the first three circuits, brisk walking between the two green milestones (on the sides of the Mas'aa), and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. Then he performs the actions of Hajj: tawaf al-qudum (arrival), and sa'y if he wishes. This order is obligatory (wajib) based on the Quranic verse 'So whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj' (2:196). The verse uses 'to' (ila) which makes Hajj the endpoint, implying Umrah must precede. If the qarin reverses the order—doing Hajj's tawaf first—that tawaf will count for Umrah and his original intention is wasted (the tawaf is repurposed). The author does not mention shaving for Umrah because the qarin does not become halal between the two rituals; both ihrams are tied together until the Day of Nahr. Shaving earlier would be a violation (jinayah) on both ihrams. The commentator Al-Burhani clarifies that although the narration from Muhammad indicates no dam for a qarin who performed tawaf in Ramadan, that person is still technically a qarin in the sense that he is liable for multiple penalties if he commits prohibitions (e.g., if he hunts, he must pay for both ihrams). However, he does not owe a dam of gratitude (shukr) because his Umrah was not performed in the months of Hajj as prescribed. The passage then discusses raml: according to Al-Walwaljiyyah, the qarin and the mufrid (one performing only Hajj) do raml only in the tawaf of greeting (tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-tahiyyah), not in the tawaf of visit (tawaf al-ziyarah), because they do not perform sa'y after that tawaf. In contrast, the mutamatti' does raml in the tawaf of visit since he does sa'y after it. The general principle is that raml is sunnah in every tawaf that is followed by sa'y.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-raml): Quick walking with slight jogging, moving the shoulders, in the first three circuits of tawaf. It is a sunnah for the qarin in tawaf followed by sa'y.
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca by the qarin and mufrid; it is sunnah and followed by sa'y.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj performed on the Day of Nahr or after; it is also called tawaf al-ifadah. For the qarin, no sa'y follows this tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a qarin performs tawaf for Hajj first (tawaf al-qudum) and then tawaf for Umrah?
A) His Hajj and Umrah are both valid.
B) His first tawaf counts for Umrah and his intention is null.
C) He must repeat both tawafs.
D) He must offer a dam.

Key Takeaway
The qarin must perform Umrah actions before Hajj actions; reversing the order causes the first Hajj tawaf to be counted for Umrah, nullifying the original intention.

Ruling on Raml for the Qarin: Sunnah in Tawaf Followed by Sa'y
Ruling on raml for qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on raml for the qarin and distinguish between tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-ziyarah.

Core Idea
Raml is sunnah only in tawaf that is followed by sa'y; for the qarin, this is only tawaf al-qudum.

This passage clarifies the sunnah of raml (quick pace with chest out) for the qarin during tawaf. The author cites Al-Walwaljiyyah to establish that the qarin and mufrid do raml only in tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) because they perform sa'y after it, whereas the mutamatti' also does raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because he does sa'y after that. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary ritual actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah status
Raml is a sunnah act in tawaf.
2
Identify the condition for raml
Raml is sunnah in any tawaf that is followed by sa'y (the brisk walking between Safa and Marwah).
3
Apply to qarin
The qarin performs sa'y after tawaf al-qudum, so raml is sunnah in that tawaf. He does not perform sa'y after tawaf al-ziyarah, so raml is not sunnah in that tawaf.
4
Contrast with mutamatti'
The mutamatti' performs sa'y after both tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-ziyarah (since he does Umrah first then Hajj), so raml is sunnah in both.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Some early Hanafi sources held that qarin and mufrid do raml in all tawafs followed by sa'y, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) from Al-Walwaljiyyah is as stated.
The author prefers the view from Al-Walwaljiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحج كما مر ) يعني يأتي بأفعال العمرة أولاً من الطواف والسعي بين الصفا والمروة والرمل في الأشواط الثلاثة والسعي بين الميلين الأخضرين وصلاة ركعتي الطواف ثم يأتي بأفعال الحج كلها ثانياً فيبدأ بطواف القدوم ويسعى بعده إن شاء، وهذا الترتيب أعني تقديم العمرة في أفعال الحج واجب لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج جلع الحج غاية وهو شامل للقران والتمتع كما قدمناه فأفاد أنه لو طاف أولاً لحجته وسعى لها ثم طاف لعمرته وسعى لها فطوافه الأول وسعيه يكون اللعمرة ونيته لغو، ولم يذكر الحلق للعمرة لأنه لا يتحلل بينهما بالحلق فلو حلق كان جناية على الإحرامين، أما على إحرام الحج فظاهر لأن أوان التحلل فيه يوم النحر، وأما على إحرام العمرة فكذلك لأن أوان تحلل القارن يوم النحر كما صرح به الإمام محمد. قال الشارح : ويؤيده أن المتمتع إذا ساق الهدي وفرغ من أفعال العمرة وحلق يجب عليه الدم ولا اشتراط فعل أكثر العمرة في أشهر الحج قوله: (لا القران الشرعي الخ قال في شرح اللباب: والذي يظهر لي أنه قارن بالمعنى الشرعي أيضاً كما هو المتبادر من إطلاق قول محمد وغيره أنه قارن، وبدليل أنه إذا ارتكب محظوراً يتعدد عليه الجزاء، وغايته أنه ليس عليه هدى شكر لأن أداءه لم يقع على الوجه المسنون المقرر في الشريعة من إيقاع أكثر العمرة في الأشهر فإنه من وجه في حكم من أفرد بعمرة في غير الأشهر ثم أفرد بالحج فإنه ليس بقارن إجماعاً ا هـ قوله : ( فيبدأ بطواف القدوم) سينص المؤلف على أن المتمتع يرمل في طوافه والظاهر أن القارن كذلك، ثم رأيته في الوالوالجية قال : ولا يرمل القارن والمفرد إلا في طواف التحية ولا يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد طواف الزيارة، أما المتمتع برمل في طواف الزيارة لأنه يسعى بعده بخلاف المفرد والقارن لأنهما لا يسعيان بعده لوجود السعي عقب طواف التحية، والسنة أن يرمل في كل طواف بعده سعي ا هـ.
His saying: (And he performs tawaf and sa'y for it then performs Hajj as mentioned) meaning he performs the actions of Umrah first: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwah, raml in three circuits, brisk walking between the green milestones, and the prayer of two rak'ahs after tawaf, then he performs all the actions of Hajj second, beginning with the tawaf of arrival and then sa'y if he wishes. This order, i.e., precedence of Umrah in the actions of Hajj, is obligatory due to Allah's saying: 'So whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj' making Hajj the goal, and this includes qiran and tamattu' as we mentioned. It follows that if he first performed tawaf for his Hajj and sa'y for it, then performed tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y for it, his first tawaf and sa'y will be for Umrah and his intention is wasted. He did not mention shaving for Umrah because he does not become halal between them by shaving; if he shaves, it is a violation against both ihrams. As for the ihram of Hajj, it is apparent because the time for tahallul is the Day of Nahr. As for the ihram of Umrah, similarly because the time for tahallul of the qarin is the Day of Nahr as stated explicitly by Imam Muhammad. The commentator said: It is supported that if a mutamatti' sends the hady and finishes the actions of Umrah and shaves, dam is obligatory upon him, and there is no condition of performing most of the Umrah in the months of Hajj. His saying: (not the technical qiran) etc. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: It appears to me that he is a qiran in the technical sense as is apparent from the absolute statement of Muhammad and others that he is a qiran, and the proof is that if he commits a prohibited act, the penalty multiplies for him. But the point is that he is not obligated to offer a dam of gratitude because his performance did not occur in the prescribed sunnah form of performing most of the Umrah in the months; thus in one respect he is like one who performed Umrah separately outside the months and then performed Hajj separately, and such a one is not a qarin by consensus. His saying: (he begins with tawaf of arrival) The author will mention that the mutamatti' does raml in his tawaf, and it appears that the qarin is similar. Then I saw in al-Walwaljiyyah: the qarin and the mufrid do not do raml except in the tawaf of greeting, and they do not do sa'y between Safa and Marwah after the tawaf of visit; as for the mutamatti', he does raml in the tawaf of visit because he performs sa'y afterwards, unlike the mufrid and qarin because they do not perform sa'y after it, due to the existence of sa'y after the tawaf of greeting. The sunnah is to do raml in every tawaf after which there is sa'y.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage explains the sequence of actions for a qarin (one performing Hajj with Umrah in one ihram). The qarin must first perform the actions of Umrah: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwah, with raml (quick pace with chest out) in the first three circuits, brisk walking between the two green milestones (on the sides of the Mas'aa), and the two rak'ahs of tawaf. Then he performs the actions of Hajj: tawaf al-qudum (arrival), and sa'y if he wishes. This order is obligatory (wajib) based on the Quranic verse 'So whoever performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj' (2:196). The verse uses 'to' (ila) which makes Hajj the endpoint, implying Umrah must precede. If the qarin reverses the order—doing Hajj's tawaf first—that tawaf will count for Umrah and his original intention is wasted (the tawaf is repurposed). The author does not mention shaving for Umrah because the qarin does not become halal between the two rituals; both ihrams are tied together until the Day of Nahr. Shaving earlier would be a violation (jinayah) on both ihrams. The commentator Al-Burhani clarifies that although the narration from Muhammad indicates no dam for a qarin who performed tawaf in Ramadan, that person is still technically a qarin in the sense that he is liable for multiple penalties if he commits prohibitions (e.g., if he hunts, he must pay for both ihrams). However, he does not owe a dam of gratitude (shukr) because his Umrah was not performed in the months of Hajj as prescribed. The passage then discusses raml: according to Al-Walwaljiyyah, the qarin and the mufrid (one performing only Hajj) do raml only in the tawaf of greeting (tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-tahiyyah), not in the tawaf of visit (tawaf al-ziyarah), because they do not perform sa'y after that tawaf. In contrast, the mutamatti' does raml in the tawaf of visit since he does sa'y after it. The general principle is that raml is sunnah in every tawaf that is followed by sa'y.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-raml): Quick walking with slight jogging, moving the shoulders, in the first three circuits of tawaf. It is a sunnah for the qarin in tawaf followed by sa'y.
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca by the qarin and mufrid; it is sunnah and followed by sa'y.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj performed on the Day of Nahr or after; it is also called tawaf al-ifadah. For the qarin, no sa'y follows this tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because tawaf al-ziyarah is not followed by sa'y for the qarin.
B) Because the qarin is not required to perform raml at all.
C) Because raml is only for the mutamatti'.
D) Because tawaf al-ziyarah is performed after the Day of Nahr.

Key Takeaway
Raml is sunnah only in tawaf that is followed by sa'y; for the qarin, this means tawaf al-qudum, not tawaf al-ziyarah.
