The Obligatory Order of Actions for the Qārin: Umrah Before Hajj
Ruling on the order of actions for the qārin: proof from Quran and consequence of reversal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wajib order of actions for a qārin, derive the ruling from Quran 2:196, and explain the consequence of reversing the order.

Core Idea
The qārin must perform Umrah actions before Hajj actions; reversal is valid but blameworthy.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq elaborates on the order of rituals for a qārin (one who combines Umrah and Hajj in one ihram). The Hanafi school holds that performing Umrah before Hajj is wajib, based on the Quranic verse that makes Hajj the 'end' (ghayah) of Umrah. The commentary also clarifies what constitutes Qiran versus Tamattu', and addresses a dispute about whether one who performs Umrah outside the Hajj months is still considered a qārin. We will walk through the proof, the obligation, and the practical ruling if the order is violated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing Umrah and Hajj together (Qiran). The ruling is that the qārin must begin with the actions of Umrah (tawaf, sa'y, etc.) before the actions of Hajj (tawaf al-qudum, etc.). This order is wajib.
Wajib, not farḍ, because the proof is zanni in dalāla.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:196: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj...' The word 'ilā' (to) indicates that Hajj is the end-point (ghāyah), implying Umrah must come first.
Qat'i in thubūt but zanni in dalāla.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The Hanafi interpretation: 'ilā' denotes ending/giving precedence. The opposing school (Shāfi‘ī) may interpret 'ilā' as 'along with', so they do not require this order. This is why the Hanafi ruling is wajib not farḍ.
The different interpretation leads to a different ruling.
4
Determine the consequence of reversal
If a qārin reverses the order (tawaf for Hajj first, then for Umrah), his first tawaf counts for Umrah (intention is void) and he has done wrong (asā'a), but the act is valid (jāza). The sa'y of Umrah is valid even if not immediately connected to its tawaf.
The ruling is based on the principle that linking sa'y to its tawaf is not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب القرآن
فإن طاف لهما طوافين وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاة أو بدنة أو سبعها وصام العاجز عنه ثلاثة أيام آخرها يوم عرفة وسبعة إذا فرغ ولو اهل.
وهو لزوم الدم شكراً ونفي اللازم الشرعي نفي للملزوم الشرعي والحاصل أن النسك المستعقب للدم شكراً هو ما تحقق فيه فعل المشروع المرتفق به الناسخ لما كان في الجاهلية وذلك بفعل العمرة في أشهر الحج، فإن كان مع الجمع في الإحرام قبل أكثر طواف العمرة فهو المسمى بالقرآن وإلا فهو التمتع بالمعنى العرفي وكلاهما التمتع بالإطلاق القرآني وعرف الصحابة وهو في الحقيقة إطلاق اللغة الحصول الرفق به هذا كله على أصول المذهب. كذا في فتح القدير.
قوله : (ويطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحج كما مر ) يعني يأتي بأفعال العمرة أولاً من الطواف والسعي بين الصفا والمروة والرمل في الأشواط الثلاثة والسعي بين الميلين الأخضرين وصلاة ركعتي الطواف ثم يأتي بأفعال الحج كلها ثانياً فيبدأ بطواف القدوم ويسعى بعده إن شاء، وهذا الترتيب أعني تقديم العمرة في أفعال الحج واجب لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج جلع الحج غاية وهو شامل للقران والتمتع كما قدمناه فأفاد أنه لو طاف أولاً لحجته وسعى لها ثم طاف لعمرته وسعى لها فطوافه الأول وسعيه يكون اللعمرة ونيته لغو، ولم يذكر الحلق للعمرة لأنه لا يتحلل بينهما بالحلق فلو حلق كان جناية على الإحرامين، أما على إحرام الحج فظاهر لأن أوان التحلل فيه يوم النحر، وأما على إحرام العمرة فكذلك لأن أوان تحلل القارن يوم النحر كما صرح به الإمام محمد. قال الشارح : ويؤيده أن المتمتع إذا ساق الهدي وفرغ من أفعال العمرة وحلق يجب عليه الدم ولا اشتراط فعل أكثر العمرة في أشهر الحج.
قوله: (لا القران الشرعي الخ) قال في شرح اللباب: والذي يظهر لي أنه قارن بالمعنى الشرعي أيضاً كما هو المتبادر من إطلاق قول محمد وغيره أنه قارن، وبدليل أنه إذا ارتكب محظوراً يتعدد عليه الجزاء، وغايته أنه ليس عليه هدى شكر لأن أداءه لم يقع على الوجه المسنون المقرر في الشريعة من إيقاع أكثر العمرة في الأشهر فإنه من وجه في حكم من أفرد بعمرة في غير الأشهر ثم أفرد بالحج فإنه ليس بقارن إجماعاً.
قوله : (فيبدأ بطواف القدوم) سينص المؤلف على أن المتمتع يرمل في طوافه والظاهر أن القارن كذلك، ثم رأيته في الوالوالجية قال : ولا يرمل القارن والمفرد إلا في طواف التحية ولا يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد طواف الزيارة، أما المتمتع برمل في طواف الزيارة لأنه يسعى بعده بخلاف المفرد والقارن لأنهما لا يسعيان بعده لوجود السعي عقب طواف التحية، والسنة أن يرمل في كل طواف بعده سعي ا هـ. وسيأتي في باب الجنايات عن المحيط ما يشير إليه أيضاً وسننبه عليه إن شاء الله تعالى. وإنما لا يرمل المتمتع في طواف التحية لأنه يسن في حقه طواف التحية كما يأتي في بابه نعم لو طاف للتحية وسعى ورمل لم يعدهما في طواف الزيارة لأنهما لا يتكرران كما يأتي أيضاً.
ثم رأيت أيضاً في اللباب قال : فيطوف لها أي للعمرة سبعاً ويضطبع فيه ويرمل في الثلاثة الأول ثم يصلي ركعتيه ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة ثم يطوف للقدوم ويضطبع فيه ويرمل إن قدم السعي ا هـ . قال القاري في شرحه : وهذا ما عليه الجمهور لما قالوا من أن كل طواف بعده سعي فالرمل فيه سنة. وقد نص عليه الكرماني حيث قال : يطوف طواف القدوم ويرمل فيه أيضاً لأنه طواف بعده سعي، وكذا في خزانة الأكمل. وإنما الرمل في طواف العمرة وطواف القدوم مفرداً كان أو قارناً، وأما ما نقله الزيلعي عن الغاية للسروجي من أنه إذا كان قارناً لم يرمل في طواف القدوم إن كان رمل في طواف العمرة فخلاف ما عليه الأكثر.
قوله : بدليل قولهم في جواب المسألة يجزئه قال في النهر : فإن قلت المراد بالإجزاء معناه اللغوي وهو الاكتفاء قلت : يرده التعليل بقوله لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه إذ ظاهره أن المراد المعنى الاصطلاحي . ولقائل أن يقول : معنى قول محمد «يجزئه) أي ما فعله من الإتيان بالسعي الواجب عليه للعمرة وإن قدم طواف الحج عليه لأن وصل سعي طواف العمرة بطوافها غير واجب وهو المعنى بقول صاحب الهداية لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه وهذا لأن محط الفائدة أن سعيه صحيح ا لكنه مسيء بتقديم طواف الحج عليه، وبهذا اكتفينا مؤنة التعبير بالإجزاء فتدبر.
قوله : (وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاة أو بدنة أو سبعها لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج فما استيسر من الهدي والتمتع يشمل القران العرفي والتمتع العرفي كما قدمناه. قيد بالذبح بعد الرمي لأن الذبح قبله لا يجوز لوجوب الترتيب ولم يقيد الذبح بالمحبة كما قيده بها في ذبح المفرد لما أنه واجب على القارن والمتمتع وأطلق البدنة فشملت البعير والبقرة والسبع جزء من سبعة أجزاء، وإنما كان مجزئاً لحديث الصحيحين عن جابر: حججنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة . وأشار بالتخيير بين البدنة وسبعها.
قوله : (ولم يقيد الذبح بالمحبة) قال الرملي : أي بقوله «أن
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran. If he performed two tawafs for them and two sa'ys, it is valid and he does wrong. And if he throws (the stones) on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel or a seventh of it, and if unable, fasts three days the last of which is the Day of Arafa, and seven when he finishes, even if he enters ihram. And it is the obligation of blood as gratitude, and negating the necessary legal consequence is negation of the necessary legal cause. In summary, the ritual that entails blood as gratitude is that in which the legislated action that brings ease and abrogates what was in Jahiliyyah is realized, and that is by performing Umrah in the months of Hajj. If it is combined in the ihram before most of the tawaf of Umrah, then it is called Qiran; otherwise it is Tamattu' in the customary sense, and both are Tamattu' according to the Quranic usage and the usage of the Companions, and in reality it is the linguistic usage of obtaining ease. All this is on the principles of the madhhab. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'And he performs tawaf and sa'y for it, then performs Hajj as mentioned' meaning he first performs the actions of Umrah: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwa, raml in the three circuits, sa'y between the two green pillars, and prayer of two rak'ahs of tawaf; then he performs all the actions of Hajj second: beginning with tawaf al-qudum and then sa'y if he wishes. This order, i.e., giving precedence to Umrah in the actions of Hajj, is obligatory due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj' He made Hajj the end, and it includes Qiran and Tamattu' as we have presented. So it indicates that if he first performed tawaf for his Hajj and sa'y for it, then performed tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y for it, his first tawaf and sa'y would be for Umrah and his intention is null. And he did not mention shaving for Umrah because he does not remove ihram between them by shaving. If he shaves, it would be an offense against both ihrams. As for the ihram of Hajj, it is obvious because the time of removal for it is the Day of Nahr; and as for the ihram of Umrah, likewise, because the time of removal for the qārin is the Day of Nahr, as stated by Imam Muhammad. The commentator said: It supports this that the mutamatti' if he brings a hady and finishes the actions of Umrah and shaves, blood is obligatory upon him, and there is no condition of performing most of Umrah in the months of Hajj. His statement: 'Not the legal Qiran etc.' It was said in Sharh al-Lubab: What appears to me is that he is a qārin in the legal sense as well, as is apparent from the absolute statement of Muhammad and others that he is a qārin, and by the evidence that if he commits a prohibited act, multiple recompense is required of him. Its utmost is that he does not have a gratitude hady because his performance did not occur in the prescribed manner established in the Shariah of performing most of Umrah in the months. So in some respects he is in the ruling of one who performed a separate Umrah outside the months then performed a separate Hajj, for he is not a qārin by consensus. His statement: 'He begins with tawaf al-qudum.' The author will state that the mutamatti' performs raml in his tawaf, and apparently the qārin also does so. Then I saw in al-Walwaljiyyah: The qārin and the mufrid do not perform raml except in tawaf al-tahiyyah, and they do not perform sa'y after tawaf al-ziyarah. As for the mutamatti', he performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because he performs sa'y after it, unlike the mufrid and qārin because they do not perform sa'y after it due to having performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudum. And the sunnah is to perform raml in every tawaf after which there is sa'y. This is from the Walwaljiyyah. And it will come in the chapter on violations from al-Muhit pointing to it as well. And he does not perform raml in tawaf al-tahiyyah because tawaf al-tahiyyah is recommended for him. Yes, if he performed tawaf al-tahiyyah and sa'y and raml, he does not repeat them in tawaf al-ziyarah because they are not repeated. Then I also saw in al-Lubab: He performs tawaf for it, i.e., for Umrah, seven circuits with idtiba' and raml in the first three, then prays two rak'ahs and performs sa'y between Safa and Marwa, then performs tawaf al-qudum with idtiba' and raml if he performs sa'y after it. Al-Qari said in his commentary: This is what the majority are upon, because they said that every tawaf after which there is sa'y, raml is sunnah in it. And al-Kirmani stated it where he said: He performs tawaf al-qudum and performs raml in it because it is a tawaf after which sa'y is performed. And similarly in Khizanat al-Akmal. And raml is only in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum whether one is mufrid or qārin. As for what al-Zayla'i transmitted from al-Ghiyathah of al-Saruji that if he is a qārin, he does not perform raml in tawaf al-qudum if he performed raml in tawaf al-Umrah, this is contrary to what the majority are upon. His statement: 'by the evidence of their saying in answering the issue: it suffices him.' It was said in al-Nahr: If you say that what is meant by 'suffices' is its linguistic meaning, i.e., it is sufficient, I say: it is refuted by the reasoning: 'because he did what was due upon him' since apparently what is meant is the technical meaning. And it can be said: the meaning of Muhammad's statement 'it suffices him' is that what he did of performing the required sa'y for Umrah is sufficient even though he preceded the tawaf of Hajj upon it, because linking the sa'y of Umrah to its tawaf is not obligatory. And this is the meaning of the author of al-Hidayah's statement: 'because he did what was due upon him.' And this is because the point is that his sa'y is valid but he is wrong in preceding the tawaf of Hajj upon it. With this we have dispensed with the trouble of the expression 'suffices', so ponder. His statement: 'And if he throws on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel or a seventh of it' due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then (sacrifice) whatever is easy of the hady' and Tamattu' includes customary Qiran and customary Tamattu' as we have presented. He restricted slaughter to after throwing because slaughter before it is not permissible due to the obligation of order. And he did not restrict slaughter to al-Mahabbah as he did for the mufrid's slaughter because it is obligatory upon the qārin and mutamatti'. And he mentioned camel absolutely, so it includes camel and cow, and a seventh is part of seven parts. And it is valid due to the hadith of the two Sahihs from Jabir: We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and we slaughtered a camel for seven and a cow for seven. And he indicated choice between a camel and a seventh of it. His statement: 'And he did not restrict slaughter to al-Mahabbah' al-Ramli said: i.e., by his saying 'that'.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of Qiran from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses three main rulings:

1. The obligation of order for a qārin: he must perform the actions of Umrah (tawaf, sa'y, raml, etc.) first, then the actions of Hajj (beginning with tawaf al-qudum). This order is wajib based on the Quranic verse 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj' (Quran 2:196). The verse makes Hajj the end (ghayah), indicating that Umrah must precede Hajj. If a qārin reverses the order (tawaf for Hajj first, then for Umrah), his intention is void for the first tawaf; it counts for Umrah, not Hajj.

2. If a qārin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys (i.e., a full set for both Umrah and Hajj but in wrong order), it is valid but he is blameworthy (asa'a). The scholars differ on which tawaf is the second. According to al-Hidayah, the second is tawaf al-qudum; according to Ghiyath al-Bayan, it is tawaf al-ziyarah. The key point is that the sa'y of Umrah must be linked to its tawaf, but postponing sa'y due to other acts (like tawaf al-Hajj) does not invalidate the sa'y; it only makes it makruh.

3. The sacrifice for qārin and mutamatti': they must slaughter a sheep, camel, or cow (or a seventh of a camel/cow) after throwing stones on the Day of Nahr. The timing is important: slaughter before rami is invalid because order is wajib. The evidence is the same Quranic verse and the hadith from Jabir (Sahihayn) about sharing camels and cows. The sacrifice is a gratitude offering (shukr) for the ease of combining Umrah and Hajj.

The passage also discusses raml (quick walking with shoulders thrust): for mutamatti' and qārin, raml is performed in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum (if sa'y follows). A qārin does not perform raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because sa'y has already been done after tawaf al-qudum.

Throughout, the commentator relies on the principles of the Hanafi madhhab, citing Fath al-Qadir, al-Walwaljiyyah, and al-Kirmani. The rulings from this passage are from Zahir al-Riwayah unless noted otherwise, as they come from the core texts of the school.

Key Terms
القرآن (al-qirān): Combining Umrah and Hajj in one ihram from the miqat, with the intention of performing both together, and performing most of Umrah in the months of Hajj.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then removing ihram, then performing Hajj in the same year. In this text, it also includes qiran in a broader sense.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movement in the first three circuits of tawaf; specific to Umrah and tawaf al-qudum if sa'y follows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the source of the ruling that Umrah must precede Hajj for a qārin?
A) A hadith from Jabir
B) Quran 2:196
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy with other acts of worship

Key Takeaway
The qārin must perform Umrah actions before Hajj actions; reversal is valid but blameworthy, and the proof is from Quran 2:196.

Sacrifice (Hady) for Qārin and Mutamatti': Rulings and Timing
Ruling on sacrifice obligation, timing, and permitted animals; also raml details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of sacrifice for qārin and mutamatti', identify the permitted animals and their shares, and explain the requirement of slaughter after rami.

Core Idea
The qārin and mutamatti' must sacrifice a hady after rami on the Day of Nahr; the animal can be a sheep, camel, or cow shared by seven.

This part of the passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the sacrifice obligation for those performing Qiran or Tamattu'. It clarifies that the hady is a gratitude offering (shukr) for the ease of combining Umrah and Hajj. The sacrifice must be performed after the stoning of Jamarat on the Day of Nahr; slaughter before rami is not permissible. The passage also addresses the permissibility of sharing a camel or cow among seven people, based on a hadith. Additionally, it discusses the sunnah of raml (brisk walking) during specific tawafs for the qārin and mutamatti'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation of hady
The hady is wajib upon the qārin and mutamatti' as a gratitude offering. The proof is Quran 2:196 which includes both categories.
The obligation is for making the rituals easier.
2
Determine the timing
The sacrifice must be performed after throwing stones on the Day of Nahr. Slaughter before rami is invalid because order is wajib.
If slaughtered before, it does not count; must be repeated after rami.
3
Identify the permitted animals
A sheep, camel, or cow (or a seventh share) suffices. The evidence is the hadith from Jabir in Sahihayn about sharing a camel or cow among seven.
A seventh means one part of a camel/cow divided into seven shares.
4
Note the raml ruling
Raml is sunnah in every tawaf that is followed by sa'y. For the qārin, raml is performed in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum (if sa'y follows), but not in tawaf al-ziyarah because sa'y has already been performed.
This is based on the principle that raml is for tawaf after which sa'y occurs.

كتاب الحج باب القرآن
فإن طاف لهما طوافين وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاة أو بدنة أو سبعها وصام العاجز عنه ثلاثة أيام آخرها يوم عرفة وسبعة إذا فرغ ولو اهل.
وهو لزوم الدم شكراً ونفي اللازم الشرعي نفي للملزوم الشرعي والحاصل أن النسك المستعقب للدم شكراً هو ما تحقق فيه فعل المشروع المرتفق به الناسخ لما كان في الجاهلية وذلك بفعل العمرة في أشهر الحج، فإن كان مع الجمع في الإحرام قبل أكثر طواف العمرة فهو المسمى بالقرآن وإلا فهو التمتع بالمعنى العرفي وكلاهما التمتع بالإطلاق القرآني وعرف الصحابة وهو في الحقيقة إطلاق اللغة الحصول الرفق به هذا كله على أصول المذهب. كذا في فتح القدير.
قوله : (ويطوف ويسعى لها ثم يحج كما مر ) يعني يأتي بأفعال العمرة أولاً من الطواف والسعي بين الصفا والمروة والرمل في الأشواط الثلاثة والسعي بين الميلين الأخضرين وصلاة ركعتي الطواف ثم يأتي بأفعال الحج كلها ثانياً فيبدأ بطواف القدوم ويسعى بعده إن شاء، وهذا الترتيب أعني تقديم العمرة في أفعال الحج واجب لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج جلع الحج غاية وهو شامل للقران والتمتع كما قدمناه فأفاد أنه لو طاف أولاً لحجته وسعى لها ثم طاف لعمرته وسعى لها فطوافه الأول وسعيه يكون اللعمرة ونيته لغو، ولم يذكر الحلق للعمرة لأنه لا يتحلل بينهما بالحلق فلو حلق كان جناية على الإحرامين، أما على إحرام الحج فظاهر لأن أوان التحلل فيه يوم النحر، وأما على إحرام العمرة فكذلك لأن أوان تحلل القارن يوم النحر كما صرح به الإمام محمد. قال الشارح : ويؤيده أن المتمتع إذا ساق الهدي وفرغ من أفعال العمرة وحلق يجب عليه الدم ولا اشتراط فعل أكثر العمرة في أشهر الحج.
قوله: (لا القران الشرعي الخ) قال في شرح اللباب: والذي يظهر لي أنه قارن بالمعنى الشرعي أيضاً كما هو المتبادر من إطلاق قول محمد وغيره أنه قارن، وبدليل أنه إذا ارتكب محظوراً يتعدد عليه الجزاء، وغايته أنه ليس عليه هدى شكر لأن أداءه لم يقع على الوجه المسنون المقرر في الشريعة من إيقاع أكثر العمرة في الأشهر فإنه من وجه في حكم من أفرد بعمرة في غير الأشهر ثم أفرد بالحج فإنه ليس بقارن إجماعاً.
قوله : (فيبدأ بطواف القدوم) سينص المؤلف على أن المتمتع يرمل في طوافه والظاهر أن القارن كذلك، ثم رأيته في الوالوالجية قال : ولا يرمل القارن والمفرد إلا في طواف التحية ولا يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد طواف الزيارة، أما المتمتع برمل في طواف الزيارة لأنه يسعى بعده بخلاف المفرد والقارن لأنهما لا يسعيان بعده لوجود السعي عقب طواف التحية، والسنة أن يرمل في كل طواف بعده سعي ا هـ. وسيأتي في باب الجنايات عن المحيط ما يشير إليه أيضاً وسننبه عليه إن شاء الله تعالى. وإنما لا يرمل المتمتع في طواف التحية لأنه يسن في حقه طواف التحية كما يأتي في بابه نعم لو طاف للتحية وسعى ورمل لم يعدهما في طواف الزيارة لأنهما لا يتكرران كما يأتي أيضاً.
ثم رأيت أيضاً في اللباب قال : فيطوف لها أي للعمرة سبعاً ويضطبع فيه ويرمل في الثلاثة الأول ثم يصلي ركعتيه ويسعى بين الصفا والمروة ثم يطوف للقدوم ويضطبع فيه ويرمل إن قدم السعي ا هـ . قال القاري في شرحه : وهذا ما عليه الجمهور لما قالوا من أن كل طواف بعده سعي فالرمل فيه سنة. وقد نص عليه الكرماني حيث قال : يطوف طواف القدوم ويرمل فيه أيضاً لأنه طواف بعده سعي، وكذا في خزانة الأكمل. وإنما الرمل في طواف العمرة وطواف القدوم مفرداً كان أو قارناً، وأما ما نقله الزيلعي عن الغاية للسروجي من أنه إذا كان قارناً لم يرمل في طواف القدوم إن كان رمل في طواف العمرة فخلاف ما عليه الأكثر.
قوله : بدليل قولهم في جواب المسألة يجزئه قال في النهر : فإن قلت المراد بالإجزاء معناه اللغوي وهو الاكتفاء قلت : يرده التعليل بقوله لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه إذ ظاهره أن المراد المعنى الاصطلاحي . ولقائل أن يقول : معنى قول محمد «يجزئه) أي ما فعله من الإتيان بالسعي الواجب عليه للعمرة وإن قدم طواف الحج عليه لأن وصل سعي طواف العمرة بطوافها غير واجب وهو المعنى بقول صاحب الهداية لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه وهذا لأن محط الفائدة أن سعيه صحيح ا لكنه مسيء بتقديم طواف الحج عليه، وبهذا اكتفينا مؤنة التعبير بالإجزاء فتدبر.
قوله : (وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاة أو بدنة أو سبعها لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج فما استيسر من الهدي والتمتع يشمل القران العرفي والتمتع العرفي كما قدمناه. قيد بالذبح بعد الرمي لأن الذبح قبله لا يجوز لوجوب الترتيب ولم يقيد الذبح بالمحبة كما قيده بها في ذبح المفرد لما أنه واجب على القارن والمتمتع وأطلق البدنة فشملت البعير والبقرة والسبع جزء من سبعة أجزاء، وإنما كان مجزئاً لحديث الصحيحين عن جابر: حججنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة . وأشار بالتخيير بين البدنة وسبعها.
قوله : (ولم يقيد الذبح بالمحبة) قال الرملي : أي بقوله «أن
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran. If he performed two tawafs for them and two sa'ys, it is valid and he does wrong. And if he throws (the stones) on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel or a seventh of it, and if unable, fasts three days the last of which is the Day of Arafa, and seven when he finishes, even if he enters ihram. And it is the obligation of blood as gratitude, and negating the necessary legal consequence is negation of the necessary legal cause. In summary, the ritual that entails blood as gratitude is that in which the legislated action that brings ease and abrogates what was in Jahiliyyah is realized, and that is by performing Umrah in the months of Hajj. If it is combined in the ihram before most of the tawaf of Umrah, then it is called Qiran; otherwise it is Tamattu' in the customary sense, and both are Tamattu' according to the Quranic usage and the usage of the Companions, and in reality it is the linguistic usage of obtaining ease. All this is on the principles of the madhhab. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'And he performs tawaf and sa'y for it, then performs Hajj as mentioned' meaning he first performs the actions of Umrah: tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwa, raml in the three circuits, sa'y between the two green pillars, and prayer of two rak'ahs of tawaf; then he performs all the actions of Hajj second: beginning with tawaf al-qudum and then sa'y if he wishes. This order, i.e., giving precedence to Umrah in the actions of Hajj, is obligatory due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj' He made Hajj the end, and it includes Qiran and Tamattu' as we have presented. So it indicates that if he first performed tawaf for his Hajj and sa'y for it, then performed tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y for it, his first tawaf and sa'y would be for Umrah and his intention is null. And he did not mention shaving for Umrah because he does not remove ihram between them by shaving. If he shaves, it would be an offense against both ihrams. As for the ihram of Hajj, it is obvious because the time of removal for it is the Day of Nahr; and as for the ihram of Umrah, likewise, because the time of removal for the qārin is the Day of Nahr, as stated by Imam Muhammad. The commentator said: It supports this that the mutamatti' if he brings a hady and finishes the actions of Umrah and shaves, blood is obligatory upon him, and there is no condition of performing most of Umrah in the months of Hajj. His statement: 'Not the legal Qiran etc.' It was said in Sharh al-Lubab: What appears to me is that he is a qārin in the legal sense as well, as is apparent from the absolute statement of Muhammad and others that he is a qārin, and by the evidence that if he commits a prohibited act, multiple recompense is required of him. Its utmost is that he does not have a gratitude hady because his performance did not occur in the prescribed manner established in the Shariah of performing most of Umrah in the months. So in some respects he is in the ruling of one who performed a separate Umrah outside the months then performed a separate Hajj, for he is not a qārin by consensus. His statement: 'He begins with tawaf al-qudum.' The author will state that the mutamatti' performs raml in his tawaf, and apparently the qārin also does so. Then I saw in al-Walwaljiyyah: The qārin and the mufrid do not perform raml except in tawaf al-tahiyyah, and they do not perform sa'y after tawaf al-ziyarah. As for the mutamatti', he performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because he performs sa'y after it, unlike the mufrid and qārin because they do not perform sa'y after it due to having performed sa'y after tawaf al-qudum. And the sunnah is to perform raml in every tawaf after which there is sa'y. This is from the Walwaljiyyah. And it will come in the chapter on violations from al-Muhit pointing to it as well. And he does not perform raml in tawaf al-tahiyyah because tawaf al-tahiyyah is recommended for him. Yes, if he performed tawaf al-tahiyyah and sa'y and raml, he does not repeat them in tawaf al-ziyarah because they are not repeated. Then I also saw in al-Lubab: He performs tawaf for it, i.e., for Umrah, seven circuits with idtiba' and raml in the first three, then prays two rak'ahs and performs sa'y between Safa and Marwa, then performs tawaf al-qudum with idtiba' and raml if he performs sa'y after it. Al-Qari said in his commentary: This is what the majority are upon, because they said that every tawaf after which there is sa'y, raml is sunnah in it. And al-Kirmani stated it where he said: He performs tawaf al-qudum and performs raml in it because it is a tawaf after which sa'y is performed. And similarly in Khizanat al-Akmal. And raml is only in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum whether one is mufrid or qārin. As for what al-Zayla'i transmitted from al-Ghiyathah of al-Saruji that if he is a qārin, he does not perform raml in tawaf al-qudum if he performed raml in tawaf al-Umrah, this is contrary to what the majority are upon. His statement: 'by the evidence of their saying in answering the issue: it suffices him.' It was said in al-Nahr: If you say that what is meant by 'suffices' is its linguistic meaning, i.e., it is sufficient, I say: it is refuted by the reasoning: 'because he did what was due upon him' since apparently what is meant is the technical meaning. And it can be said: the meaning of Muhammad's statement 'it suffices him' is that what he did of performing the required sa'y for Umrah is sufficient even though he preceded the tawaf of Hajj upon it, because linking the sa'y of Umrah to its tawaf is not obligatory. And this is the meaning of the author of al-Hidayah's statement: 'because he did what was due upon him.' And this is because the point is that his sa'y is valid but he is wrong in preceding the tawaf of Hajj upon it. With this we have dispensed with the trouble of the expression 'suffices', so ponder. His statement: 'And if he throws on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel or a seventh of it' due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then (sacrifice) whatever is easy of the hady' and Tamattu' includes customary Qiran and customary Tamattu' as we have presented. He restricted slaughter to after throwing because slaughter before it is not permissible due to the obligation of order. And he did not restrict slaughter to al-Mahabbah as he did for the mufrid's slaughter because it is obligatory upon the qārin and mutamatti'. And he mentioned camel absolutely, so it includes camel and cow, and a seventh is part of seven parts. And it is valid due to the hadith of the two Sahihs from Jabir: We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and we slaughtered a camel for seven and a cow for seven. And he indicated choice between a camel and a seventh of it. His statement: 'And he did not restrict slaughter to al-Mahabbah' al-Ramli said: i.e., by his saying 'that'.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of Qiran from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses three main rulings:

1. The obligation of order for a qārin: he must perform the actions of Umrah (tawaf, sa'y, raml, etc.) first, then the actions of Hajj (beginning with tawaf al-qudum). This order is wajib based on the Quranic verse 'So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj' (Quran 2:196). The verse makes Hajj the end (ghayah), indicating that Umrah must precede Hajj. If a qārin reverses the order (tawaf for Hajj first, then for Umrah), his intention is void for the first tawaf; it counts for Umrah, not Hajj.

2. If a qārin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys (i.e., a full set for both Umrah and Hajj but in wrong order), it is valid but he is blameworthy (asa'a). The scholars differ on which tawaf is the second. According to al-Hidayah, the second is tawaf al-qudum; according to Ghiyath al-Bayan, it is tawaf al-ziyarah. The key point is that the sa'y of Umrah must be linked to its tawaf, but postponing sa'y due to other acts (like tawaf al-Hajj) does not invalidate the sa'y; it only makes it makruh.

3. The sacrifice for qārin and mutamatti': they must slaughter a sheep, camel, or cow (or a seventh of a camel/cow) after throwing stones on the Day of Nahr. The timing is important: slaughter before rami is invalid because order is wajib. The evidence is the same Quranic verse and the hadith from Jabir (Sahihayn) about sharing camels and cows. The sacrifice is a gratitude offering (shukr) for the ease of combining Umrah and Hajj.

The passage also discusses raml (quick walking with shoulders thrust): for mutamatti' and qārin, raml is performed in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum (if sa'y follows). A qārin does not perform raml in tawaf al-ziyarah because sa'y has already been done after tawaf al-qudum.

Throughout, the commentator relies on the principles of the Hanafi madhhab, citing Fath al-Qadir, al-Walwaljiyyah, and al-Kirmani. The rulings from this passage are from Zahir al-Riwayah unless noted otherwise, as they come from the core texts of the school.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal obligated upon a qārin or mutamatti' as gratitude for the ease of combining Umrah and Hajj.
الرمل (al-raml): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movement in the first three circuits of tawaf; specific to Umrah and tawaf al-qudum if sa'y follows.
البدنة (al-badana): A camel used for sacrifice; in the passage it is used generally to include both camel and cow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of people that can share a camel or cow for the hady according to the hadith cited in the passage?
A) 7
B) 2
C) 10
D) 1

Key Takeaway
The qārin and mutamatti' must sacrifice a hady after rami on the Day of Nahr; the animal can be a sheep, camel, or cow shared by seven.

The Ruling on Two Tawafs and Two Sa'ys in Qiran
Explains ruling and disputes about two tawafs and sa'y in Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys, and explain the differing views on the identity of the second tawaf within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A qarin's extra tawafs and sa'ys are valid but blameworthy; no dam required, but the second tawaf's identity is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a specific scenario: a qarin who performs two complete tawafs and two sa'ys. The matn declares the action valid but blameworthy, yet later commentators debate the identity of the second tawaf. Is it tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-ziyarah? The answer affects the ruling on ramal and the understanding of 'ijza'. Let's walk through the dispute step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling from the matn
Identify that the action is valid (jaza) but blameworthy (asa'a). This is the starting point.
The matn uses 'jaza wa asa'a'.
2
Understand the intended sequence
Notice that the conjunction 'wa' in 'tawafain wa sa'yain' here means 'thumma' or 'fa', indicating that the two tawafs are performed first, then the two sa'ys.
This is clarified by the commentator and the reference to al-Jami' al-Saghir.
3
Identify the first view on the second tawaf
The author of al-Hidayah and the commentators following al-Mabsut hold that the second tawaf is tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf). Thus, the person delayed the sa'y of Umrah by performing a sunnah tawaf first.
This view results in no dam requirement according to the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa.
4
Identify the second view on the second tawaf
The author of Ghayat al-Bayan holds that the second tawaf is tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj), after having performed tawaf al-Umrah earlier. He argues that only the obligatory tawaf can be described as 'mujzi' (sufficing).
This view implies a different sequence: Umrah tawaf, then Arafah, then ziyarah tawaf, then sa'y.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The majority (al-Mabsut, al-Hidayah) is followed: the second tawaf is tawaf al-qudum, no dam is required, and the action is valid but blameworthy.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن طاف لهما طوافين وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء بأن طاف للعمرة والحج أربعة عشر شوطاً . وسعی كذلك. وأراد بالواو معنى «ثم» أو الفاء لأن المسألة مفروضة فيما إذا أتى بالسعي بعد الطوافين ولا يفهم هذا من الواو لأنها لمطلق الجمع ولهذا أتى في الجامع الصغير بـ«ثم واختلفوا في ثاني الطوافين في قولهم طاف طوافين فذهب صاحب الهداية والشارحون تبعاً للمبسوط إلى أنه طواف القدوم ولهذا قال في الهداية : وقد أساء بتأخير سعي العمرة وتقديم طواف التحية عليه ولا يلزمه شيء، أما عندهما فظاهر لأن التقديم والتأخير في المناسك لا يوجب الدم عندهما، وعنده طواف التحية سنة وتركه لا يوجب الدم فتقديمه أولى والسعي بتأخيره بالاشتغال بعمل آخر لا يوجب الدم فكذا بالاشتغال بالطواف وذهب صاحب غاية البيان إلى أن المراد بأحدهما طواف العمرة وبالآخر طواف الزيارة بأن أتى بطواف العمرة ثم اشتغل بالوقوف ثم طاف للزيارة يوم النحر ثم سعى أربعة عشر شوطاً بدليل قولهم في جواب المسألة يجزئه والمجزئ عبارة عما يكون كافياً في الخروج عن عهدة الفرض، ولا يحصل الإجزاء بترك الفرض والإتيان بالسنة وبدليل قولهم إن القارن يطوف طوافين ويسعى سعيين عندنا ليس المراد بهما إلا طواف العمرة وطواف الزيارة يطوف طواف القدوم ويرمل فيه أيضاً لأنه طواف بعده سعي، وكذا في خزانة الأكمل. وإنما الرمل في طواف العمرة وطواف القدوم مفرداً كان أو قارناً، وأما ما نقله الزيلعي عن الغاية للسروجي من أنه إذا كان قارناً لم يرمل في طواف القدوم إن كان رمل في طواف العمرة فخلاف ما عليه الأكثر ا هـ قوله : بدليل قولهم في جواب المسألة يجزئه قال في النهر : فإن قلت المراد بالإجزاء معناه اللغوي وهو الاكتفاء قلت : يرده التعليل بقوله لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه إذ ظاهره أن المراد المعنى الاصطلاحي . ولقائل أن يقول : معنى قول محمد «يجزئه) أي ما فعله من الإتيان بالسعي الواجب عليه للعمرة وإن قدم طواف الحج عليه لأن وصل سعي طواف العمرة بطوافها غير واجب وهو المعنى بقول صاحب الهداية لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه وهذا لأن محط الفائدة أن سعيه صحيح ا لكنه مسيء بتقديم طواف الحج عليه، وبهذا اكتفينا مؤنة التعبير بالإجزاء فتدبر
He said: (If he performs two tawafs and two sa'ys for both, it is valid but he did badly) meaning he performed for Umrah and Hajj fourteen circuits and performed sa'y similarly. The waw in 'tawafain wa sa'yain' here means 'thumma' or 'fa' because the case is assumed to have performed sa'y after the two tawafs; this is not understood from the waw because it indicates mere conjunction, hence in al-Jami' al-Saghir he used 'thumma'. They differed on the second tawaf in their statement 'he performed two tawafs'. The author of al-Hidayah and the commentators following al-Mabsut held it to be tawaf al-qudum, therefore he said in al-Hidayah: He acted badly by delaying the sa'y of Umrah and advancing tawaf al-tahiyyah, but nothing is required of him. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is clear because precedence and delay in rituals do not require blood atonement according to them. According to him (Abu Hanifa), tawaf al-tahiyyah is sunnah and its omission does not require blood, so performing it first is better, and delaying sa'y by engaging in another act does not require blood, similarly engaging in tawaf. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan held that the intended meaning is one tawaf for Umrah and the other for ziyarah: he performed tawaf for Umrah, then busied himself with standing (at Arafah), then performed tawaf al-ziyarah on the day of Nahr, then performed sa'y of fourteen circuits, as evidence for their answer that it suffices him. The term 'mujzi' refers to what is sufficient to discharge the obligation, and discharge is not achieved by omitting the obligatory and performing the sunnah. And by their statement that the qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys according to us, meaning only tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-ziyarah. He performs tawaf al-qudum and ramal in it as well because it is a tawaf after which there is sa'y, similarly in Khizanat al-Akmal. Ramal is only in tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-qudum, whether for a mufrid or qarin. As for what al-Zayla'i narrated from al-Ghayyah of al-Saruji, that if he is a qarin he does not do ramal in tawaf al-qudum if he did ramal in tawaf al-Umrah, it is contrary to what the majority are upon. End. He said: As evidence for their answer that it suffices him. He said in al-Nahr: If you say that by 'ijza' the linguistic meaning is intended, which is sufficiency, I say: It is refuted by the reasoning that 'he performed what was due upon him', apparently intended is the technical meaning. And it can be said: The meaning of Muhammad's statement 'it suffices him' is that what he did of performing the obligatory sa'y for Umrah is valid even if he advanced the tawaf of Hajj upon it because linking the sa'y of Umrah to its tawaf is not obligatory. This is the meaning of the author of al-Hidayah: 'he performed what was due upon him'. This is because the benefit is that his sa'y is valid but he is blameworthy for advancing the tawaf of Hajj upon it. With this we dispense with the burden of the expression 'ijza'. So ponder.
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a qarin who performs two tawafs and two sa'ys. The text first explains the matn: if a qarin performs two tawafs (for Umrah and Hajj) and two sa'ys, the action is valid (jaza) but blameworthy (asa'a). The commentator clarifies that the conjunction 'wa' in the matn actually means 'thumma' or 'fa', indicating sequence: first both tawafs, then both sa'ys. The main dispute concerns the identity of the second tawaf. The author of al-Hidayah and others following al-Mabsut hold it to be tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), so the person delayed the sa'y of Umrah and advanced a sunnah tawaf, which is blameworthy but no blood atonement is required. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), sequence in rituals does not require dam. According to Abu Hanifa, advancing a sunnah does not require dam, so it is better to do it. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan, however, interprets the two tawafs as tawaf al-Umrah and tawaf al-ziyarah, with a sequence of Umrah tawaf, then standing at Arafah, then ziyarah tawaf, then sa'y. Evidence for this is that the term 'mujzi' (sufficing) is used: it must refer to fulfilling the obligatory, not sunnah. Additionally, the qarin is known to perform two tawafs and two sa'ys — these are Umrah and Hajj tawafs. The passage also discusses the ramal (quick pace) in tawaf al-qudum, affirming that a qarin should also do ramal because it is a tawaf followed by sa'y, except for a minority view. Finally, a discussion on the technical vs. linguistic meaning of 'ijza' is provided, concluding that the sa'y is valid but the person is blameworthy.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arriving in Mecca, before the stay at Arafah, for those entering Ihram.
سعي العمرة (sa'y al-umrah): The sa'y performed for Umrah, which is obligatory.
طواف التحية (tawaf al-tahiyyah): The greeting tawaf performed upon entering the Masjid al-Haram as a sunnah.
قارن (qarin): One who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The Hajj is invalid and he must perform it again.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who performs two tawafs and two sa'ys has a valid Hajj but is blameworthy; no dam is required, and the majority view is that the second tawaf is tawaf al-qudum.

The Hadi for Qiran and Tamattu': Obligation, Timing, and Sharing
Ruling on slaughtering hadi after ramy with Quran and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the hadi for qiran and tamattu', explain its required timing (after ramy), and identify the proof from Quran and Sunnah, including the permissibility of sharing a camel or cow among seven.

Core Idea
The hadi for qiran and tamattu' is wajib, must be after ramy, and can be a seventh of a camel or cow.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rai'iq explains the ruling on the sacrificial animal (hadi) required from those performing Hajj as qiran or tamattu'. It clarifies when the slaughter must occur, what qualifies as a valid sacrifice, and the conditions for sharing a single animal. Understanding these details ensures the hajj rituals are performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering a hadi by the qarin or mutamatti after stoning on the day of Nahr. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) based on the Quranic command and the Hanafi principle that an imperative indicates obligation.
The matn uses the imperative form, and the commentator confirms it is wajib, not mustahabb.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: Quran 2:196 (فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج فما استيسر من الهدي) and the hadith of Jabir from Sahihayn about sharing a camel or cow among seven.
The Quranic verse provides the basis for obligation; the hadith provides the basis for permissibility of sharing.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Quranic verse commands 'fima istaysara min al-hady' – an imperative that in Hanafi usul indicates wujub. The hadith directly shows the Prophet's practice of sharing one animal among seven, proving the sufficiency of a seventh part.
The commentator emphasizes that the hadith is from the two Sahihs, indicating strong authentication.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds the hadi is wajib for tamattu' but not for qiran; Hanafis consider it wajib for both. The basis is whether qiran is included in the Quranic term 'tamattu'. Hanafis include it linguistically and by analogy.
The passage incidentally mentions the difference but does not fully argue it.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school, relying on the apparent meaning of the verse and the practice of the Companions. The permissibility of sharing is firmly established by the hadith.
The text also clarifies that if a qarin sends money for two animals but only one is available, slaughtering one does not release both ihrams – unless it is a dam ihsar (blockage).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإذا رمى يوم النحر ذبح شاة أو بدنة أو سبعها لقوله تعالى فمن تمتع بالعمرة إلى الحج فما استيسر من الهدي والتمتع يشمل القران العرفي والتمتع العرفي كما قدمناه. قيد بالذبح بعد الرمي لأن الذبح قبله لا يجوز لوجوب الترتيب ولم يقيد الذبح بالمحبة كما قيده بها في ذبح المفرد لما أنه واجب على القارن والمتمتع وأطلق البدنة فشملت البعير والبقرة والسبع جزء من سبعة أجزاء، وإنما كان مجزئاً لحديث الصحيحين عن جابر: حججنا مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة . وأشار بالتخيير بين البدنة وسبعها إلى أنه دم عبادة لا دم جناية فيأكل منه كما سيأتي، وسيأتي في الأضحية أنه لا بد أن يكون الكل مريداً للقربة وإن اختلفت جهة القربة فلو أراد أحد السبعة لحماً لأهله لا يجزئهم، واستدل له بعض شارحي المصابيح بقوله الا الله وأنا أغني الشركاء عن الشرك من عمل عملاً أشرك فيه معي غيري تركته وشركه (۱) وما في المبتغى ولو بعث القارن بثمن هديين فلم يوجد بذلك بمكة إلا هدي واحد فبذبحه لا يتحلل عن الإحرامين ولا عن : محمول على هدي الإحصار لأن التحلل موقوف عليه لا على ذبح دم الشكر. وفي الظهيرية والخانية: والاشتراك في البقرة أفضل من الشاة والجزور أفضل من البقرة كما في الأضحية فإن كان القارن ساق الهدي . مع نفسه كان أفضل . أحدهما اهـ .
He said: (And when he stones on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel or a seventh of it) due to His statement 'Then whoever enjoys Umrah until Hajj, then what is easy from the hadi' and tamattu includes both the common qiran and common tamattu as we have presented. He restricted slaughter after stoning because slaughter before it is not permissible due to the requirement of sequence. He did not restrict slaughter to love as he restricted it in the slaughter of the mufrid because it is obligatory for the qarin and mutamatti. He gave absolute permission for the badanah, so it includes camel and cow, and a seventh is part of seven portions. It was only sufficient due to the hadith of the two Sahihs from Jabir: We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and we slaughtered the camel on behalf of seven and the cow on behalf of seven. And he indicated by the choice between the badanah and its seventh that it is a blood of worship, not a blood of crime, so he eats from it as will come. And it will come in Udhiyah that all must intend the devotion even if the direction of devotion differs; if one of the seven intends meat for his family, it does not suffice them. And some commentators of al-Masabih used as evidence his statement: 'except Allah and I make partners free from partnership. Whoever performs an act in which he associates someone other than Me with Me, I leave him and his partner.' And what is in al-Mubtagha: If the qarin sends the price of two animals but only one animal is found in Mecca, by slaughtering it he does not become free from either Ihram. This is understood as the hady of ihsar (blockage), because release depends on it, not on slaughter of gratitude. And in al-Zahiriyyah and al-Khaniyyah: Sharing in the cow is better than the sheep, and the camel is better than the cow, as in Udhiyah. If the qarin drives the hadi with himself, it is better. 'One of them, end.'
Source pages p. 630

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Quran and Sunnah about the hadi (sacrificial animal) required from the qarin and mutamatti. The matn states that after stoning on the day of Nahr, one slaughters a sheep, a camel, or a seventh of a camel/cow. The commentator explains that the restriction to after stoning is because sequence is obligatory: slaughter before ramy is invalid. He also notes that unlike the mufrid (who does only Hajj), the qarin and mutamatti must slaughter; the mufrid's slaughter is recommended (mahabba) but not obligatory. The matn's allowance of a seventh part is proven by the authentic hadith of Jabir about sharing the sacrificial animal among seven. The text further explains that this hadi is a 'dam 'ibadah' (blood of worship), not a 'dam jinayah' (blood of crime), so the owner may eat from it. The condition for sharing is that all participants intend the devotion (qurbah); if one intends meat for his family, it does not suffice. A hadith is cited: 'Whoever performs an act associating others with Me, I desert him and his partner.' The passage also clarifies a case: if a qarin sends money for two animals but only one is available, slaughtering one does not release him from both ihrams because the hadi of gratitude (shukr) is not the cause of tahlil; rather, it is the hadi of ihsar (blockage) that causes tahlil. Finally, some fiqh works state that sharing in a cow is better than a sheep, and a camel is better than a cow, and it is best if the qarin drives his own hadi.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal required from the qarin and mutamatti during Hajj.
دم عبادة (dam 'ibadah): A blood sacrifice that is an act of worship, from which the sacrificer may eat.
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial camel or cow; the term includes both.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Analogy (qiyas) to udhiyah.
B) The Quranic verse on hadi.
C) The hadith of Jabir from Sahihayn.
D) Consensus of the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
The hadi for qiran and tamattu' is a wajib sacrifice that must be performed after stoning, and a seventh of a camel or cow suffices based on the authentic Sunnah, provided all participants intend devotion.

Defining 'Ajiz: When Can a Qarin Fast Instead of Hadi?
States the Hanafi ruling on fasting for the qarin and defines inability through multiple scholarly views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a qarin may fast instead of slaughtering a hadi, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the definition of 'ajiz (wealth threshold).

Core Idea
A qarin can only fast if truly unable to find a hadi; the Hanafis differ on how much wealth makes one able.

The Quran grants an alternative to sacrificing a hadi: fasting. But who qualifies as unable to find a hadi? The Hanafi school has multiple definitions, each affecting whether the qarin must slaughter or may fast. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the intra-Hanafi dispute on the threshold of wealth (ghina) that determines inability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The qarin who cannot find a hadi must fast three days during Hajj and seven after. This is based on Quran 2:196.
The obligation is conditional on inability ('ajz).
2
Locate the dispute
The term 'ajiz (unable) is not defined in the Quran. Hanafi scholars differ on what constitutes enough wealth to render one able.
3
List the opposing views
Some say one month's food, some one day's food, some surplus of 200 dirhams, etc. These are attributed to different Hanafi authorities.
Refer to Ibn Muqatil, Abu Yusuf, al-Kirmani, etc.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Each view changes whether a particular pilgrim must slaughter or may fast. The mufta bihi (relied upon) view is the surplus of 200 dirhams.
Consequence: thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Apply the preferred view
If a qarin has surplus wealth of 200 dirhams or more after basic needs, he is not 'ajiz and must slaughter. Otherwise, he may fast.
This is the position of Abu Yusuf and a narration from Abu Hanifa.

He said: (And the one unable to do so fasts three days, the last of which is the day of Arafah, and seven when he returns, even in Mecca) meaning the one unable to obtain the hadi fasts due to His statement 'Then whoever cannot find, then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; those are complete.' And his statement 'as he restricted it in slaughter of the mufrid' is a negligence from him because he did not restrict it there either; rather he said: 'Then slaughter, then shave or shorten, and shaving is better.' His statement: (And he indicated by the choice between the badanah and its seventh that it is a blood of worship etc.) Its requirement is that if it were a blood of crime, he would not have choice. And in Udhiyah of al-Wiqayah and its commentary by al-Qahistani: like a cow that three people slaughter for Udhiyah, tamattu', and qiran in Hajj, it is valid. Similarly, if seven slaughter for those purposes and for ihsar and penalty of hunting or shaving and aqiqah and voluntary, it is valid in the apparent principles. According to Abu Yusuf, it is better that they be of the same type; if they are different and each one is drawing near, it is permissible. According to Abu Hanifa, it is disliked, as in al-Nazm. And it will be mentioned in al-Hady that sharing in a badanah is permissible as in Udhiyah with the condition that all intend devotion, even if their types of blood are different. End. The author's statement: (And the one unable to do so fasts) Our companions differed in defining the limit of wealth in the chapter of expiations. Some said: maintenance of a month; if he has less than that, it is permissible for him to fast. Ibn Muqatil said: Whoever has maintenance of a day and night, it is not permissible for him to fast if the food he has is the amount that is obligatory upon him. This agrees with what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf that if he has enough to buy what is obligatory and he has nothing else, fasting does not suffice him. Some said regarding the one who works with his hand, i.e., the earner: he keeps the maintenance of his day and expiates with the rest. And the one who does not work keeps maintenance of a month, according to what al-Kirmani mentioned, and this is a good detail, except that this applies when he does not possess the specific [textually defined] property; otherwise, fasting is not permissible for him as stated in al-Khulasah and al-Bada'i'. Even if he has debt, as some mentioned. And from Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa: if he has surplus beyond his dwelling and clothing and basic needs, and the surplus is two hundred dirhams or more, fasting does not suffice him. Thus in Sharh al-Lubab. In the marginalia of al-Madani from al-Mansak al-Kabir of al-Sindi: It is understood from the wording of al-Zahiriyyah that if one is insolvent in Mecca but wealthy in his own country, fasting is permissible for him because the place of the blood [hadi] is Mecca. (1) Narrated by Muslim in Kitab al-Zuhd, hadith 46.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on fasting as an alternative for those unable to obtain a hadi, and includes a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of wealth (ghina) that determines eligibility for fasting. The matn states: the one who is 'ajiz (unable) fasts three days during Hajj (last day being Arafah) and seven after returning, even if he remains in Mecca. The commentary clarifies that the Quranic verse (2:196) is the basis: 'If you cannot find a hadi, then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return.' The discussion then digresses into a note about sharing animals, reiterating that sharing is valid as long as all intend devotion, and that Abu Yusuf prefers same type while Abu Hanifa dislikes differing types. The main legal dispute is on the definition of 'ajiz: when is a person considered able to obtain a hadi? The Hanafi scholars differ: some say if one has enough food for a month, he is not 'ajiz; Ibn Muqatil says if he has food for a day and night, he cannot fast; others distinguish between a wage earner (who keeps one day's food) and a non-worker (who keeps one month). A narration from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa: if he has surplus over basic needs amounting to 200 dirhams or more, fasting is invalid. A useful rule from al-Zahiriyyah: if a person is poor in Mecca but wealthy in his homeland, he may still fast because the hadi is required in Mecca. This is supported by a hadith in Muslim about sincerity.

Key Terms
عاجز ('ajiz): One who is unable to obtain a hadi due to lack of wealth.
الغنى في باب الكفارات (al-ghina fi bab al-kafarat): The state of being wealthy in the context of expiations; determines whether one may fast or must make sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to one Hanafi view mentioned in the text, if a person has a surplus of 200 dirhams after basic needs, can he fast instead of slaughtering a hadi?
A) Yes, because he is still not wealthy.
B) No, his fasting is not acceptable.
C) Yes, but only if he is in Mecca.
D) No, unless he has debt.

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'ajiz in the hadi ruling is a matter of scholarly interpretation; the later Hanafi reliance on the 200 dirham surplus standard provides a clear criterion for fatwa.

Sharing in Sacrifice for Qarin and Mutamatti'
Explains ruling on sharing in sacrifice for qarin and mutamatti'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing a single sacrificial animal among multiple persons for different types of hady, identify the condition of intention for validity, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
All participants must intend qurbah, even if their types of sacrifice differ.

This lesson examines the ruling on sharing a sacrificial animal (cow or camel) among pilgrims with different obligations – such as tamattu', qiran, or ihsar. The Hanafi school permits sharing under specific conditions, but there is a known internal disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his student Abu Yusuf. We will explore the textual evidence, the condition of intention, and the preferred position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the hady
The passage first clarifies that the hady of qiran and tamattu' is a 'blood of worship' (dam ibadah), meaning the owner may eat from it. Distinguish this from 'blood of penalty' (dam jinaya) where eating is not permitted.
2
State the condition for sharing
For a shared sacrifice to be valid, every participant must intend qurbah (drawing near to Allah). If even one person intends mere family meat, the sacrifice does not count for any of them.
The intention (niyya) is a core condition – the act must be purely for Allah.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Abu Hanifa considers sharing (with different types of hady) as makruh, while Abu Yusuf permits it as long as each intends qurbah. Abu Yusuf's view is supported by a hadith cited in the passage.
The hadith: 'I free partners from shirk…' indicates that sincerity is key.
4
Understand the proof
The commentator uses a hadith (from some sharh of Masabih) to argue that if everyone seeks Allah's reward, their intentions are compatible even if the specific obligations differ. This is a dalil naqli.
The hadith text: 'Allah, and I am free from partners… whoever does a deed in which he associates another with Me, I leave him and his partner.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later Hanafi authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin) prefer the permissive view of Abu Yusuf because it is easier and aligns with the hadith. Thus, sharing is permissible but it is better if all participants have the same type of hady.
The passage mentions that sharing in a cow is better than a sheep, and a camel better than a cow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى أنه دم عبادة لا دم جناية فيأكل منه كما سيأتي، وسيأتي في الأضحية أنه لا بد أن يكون الكل مريداً للقربة وإن اختلفت جهة القربة فلو أراد أحد السبعة لحماً لأهله لا يجزئهم، واستدل له بعض شارحي المصابيح بقوله الا الله وأنا أغني الشركاء عن الشرك من عمل عملاً أشرك فيه معي غيري تركته وشركه (۱) وما في المبتغى ولو بعث القارن بثمن هديين فلم يوجد بذلك بمكة إلا هدي واحد فبذبحه لا يتحلل عن الإحرامين ولا عن : محمول على هدي الإحصار لأن التحلل موقوف عليه لا على ذبح دم الشكر. وفي الظهيرية والخانية: والاشتراك في البقرة أفضل من الشاة والجزور أفضل من البقرة كما في الأضحية فإن كان القارن ساق الهدي . مع نفسه كان أفضل . . أحدهما اهـ .
That it is a blood of worship not a blood of penalty, so one may eat from it as will come. And it will come in Adahi that it is necessary that everyone intends proximity (qurbah) even if the direction of proximity differs. So if one of the seven intended meat for his family, it does not suffice them. And some commentators of Masabih deduced for it by his saying: 'Allah, and I am free from partners, from shirk: whoever does a deed in which he associates another with Me, I leave him and his partner.' And what is in al-Mubtagha: if the qarin sent the price of two hadys and only one hady was found in Mecca, then by slaughtering it he is not released from the two ihrams, nor from... it is carried on the hady of ihsar because the release depends on it, not on slaughtering the blood of thanksgiving. And in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya: and sharing in a cow is better than a sheep, and a camel is better than a cow as in Adahi. If the qarin drove the hady with himself, it is better. 'One of them' end.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of sharing in the sacrificial animal for the qarin and mutamatti'. It first establishes that the hady of Qiran and Tamattu' is a 'blood of worship' (dam ibadah) not a 'blood of penalty' (dam jinaya), so the sacrificer may eat from it. It then discusses the condition for validity: all participants must intend qurbah (drawing near to Allah), even if their specific intentions differ (e.g., one for tamattu', another for ihsar). If one intends solely for family meat, the sacrifice does not count for the required hady. The commentator cites a hadith (quoted by some sharh of Masabih) to support that sharing is permissible if all seek Allah's reward. The passage then discusses the preference: a camel is better than a cow, a cow better than a sheep. Abu Yusuf allows participation even if the participants have different types of hady (tamattu', ihsar, etc.) as long as each intends qurbah, while Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked). The relied-upon position is that it is permissible but it is better for all to be of the same type (e.g., all for tamattu').

Key Terms
دم عبادة (dam ibadah): Blood of worship: the sacrificial animal for Qiran or Tamattu', which is an act of worship and thus the sacrificer may eat from it.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): Sharing: multiple persons contributing to one sacrificial animal, each receiving a share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum condition for multiple persons to share a single sacrificial animal (e.g., cow) for hady?
A) All must have the same type of hady (e.g., all tamattu').
B) All must intend qurbah, even if their types differ.
C) The animal must be a camel.
D) At least seven persons must participate.

Key Takeaway
Sharing a sacrificial animal in Hajj is permissible in the Hanafi school as long as every participant intends qurbah; Abu Yusuf's permissive view is the relied-upon position.

When Finding Hady Invalidates the Substitute Fast: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of later finding hady on substitute fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when finding a hady after completing the substitute fast invalidates the fast, and evaluate the competing opinions within the school.

Core Idea
The substitute fast for the hady falls only if the hady becomes available before shaving — after shaving, the fast is final.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the Quranic ruling that one unable to offer a hady may fast instead. The commentators delve into the crucial question: what if he later becomes able? The answer hinges on the timing of shaving. The passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute, with some scholars arguing that finding the hady any time during the days of sacrifice invalidates the fast, while the majority holds that the fast remains valid if he has already shaved. We will unpack the proofs and identify the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling: the substitute fast for the hady
Based on Quran 2:196, one who cannot find a hady must fast three days during Hajj (last day Arafah) and seven after returning. This fast is a substitute (khalaf) for the hady, allowing one to shave and exit ihram.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because it is a replacement.
2
Identify the condition for the fast to be valid: inability to find the hady
The fast is only valid if one is truly unable to afford the hady. Various Hanafi definitions of 'inability' are discussed, with the relied-upon view being that one is able if he has the price of the hady or surplus wealth beyond basic needs.
This is a separate issue; the main dispute focuses on what happens if ability arises later.
3
The problem: finding the hady after fasting
The central issue: if a pilgrim fasts the three days (and possibly the seven as well), but then becomes able to offer a hady during the days of slaughter (10th–13th Dhul Hijjah), does the fast become invalid?
The answer depends on whether he has already shaved or not.
4
Follow the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Kamal and others argue that the fast is invalidated if the hady is found at any time during the days of Nahr, even after shaving. The majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) respond that the purpose of the hady is to permit shaving; if shaving already occurred, the substitute is fulfilled and cannot be undone. They analogize to tayammum: finding water after prayer does not invalidate the prayer.
The phrase 'al-'ibrah li-ayyam al-nahr' is interpreted differently: for Al-Kamal, it means the days are critical; for the majority, it means ability is considered before the purpose is achieved.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text concludes that the view of al-Fath and the majority is correct: the fast remains valid if shaving occurs before finding the hady. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The dispute is legitimate, but the majority view is stronger in evidence and practicality.
