عن الإجرام لغير المحصر إنما هو الحلق أو التقصير، وللمحصر ذبح الهدي في محله وذكر أن الهدي وجب شكراً على القارن والمتمتع وأنه أصل والصوم خلف عنه، وأن شرط بدليته تقديم الثلاثة على يوم النحر، ثم حقق أن العبرة لوجود الهدي في أيام النحر وأنه لا بدلية لين الهدي والحلق حتى يقال وجود الهدي بعد الحلق لا يعتبر الحصول المقصود بالخلف وهو الحلق كما وقع في عدة . من المعتبرات إذ لا دخل للحلق قبل وجوده فيها فوجوده فيها يبطل حكم الصوم فيلزمه ذبحه وإن تحلل قبله لموجب اطلاق النص، ولقول المحققين العبرة لأيام النحر وجوداً وعدماً للهدي. قال الكمال: فإن قدر على الهدي في خلال الثلاثة أو بعدها قبل يوم النحر لزمه الهدي وسقط الصوم لأنه خلف، وإذا قدر على الأصل. قبل تأدي الحكم بالخلف بطل الخلف ا.هـ. فقد نص على أن الصوم خلف عن الهدي والهدي لا يتحلل به ولا بخلفه بل بالحلق أو التقصير وهذا عين الصواب. وأما قوله «وإن قدر على الهدي بعد الحلق قبل أن يصوم السبعة في أيام الذبح أو بعدها لم يلزمه الهدي لأن التحلل قد حصل بالحلق فوجود الأصل بعده لا ينقض الخلف» ا هـ. ففيه تدافع وتقييد لمطلق الكتاب كما تقدم، وذلك لأنه أفاد أنه يتحلل بالهدي أصلاً وبالحلق خلفاً، فإذا وجد الهدي لا يبطل خلفه الذي هو الحلق على كلامه الأخير، والصواب كلامه الأول. ثم نقل نحوه عن المحيط وغيره ومنها ما في هذا الشرح، ونازعهم بما مر. وحاصل كلامه وجوب الهدي بوجوده في أيام النحر سواء حلق أو لا، وأنه لا يسقط الهدي إلا بوجوده بعدها مخالفاً لما هو المنصوص عليه في كثير من المعتبرات. أقول: لا يخفى عليك أن الواجب اتباع المنقول ووجهه أن المقصود من الذبح إباحة التحلل بالحلق أو التقصير، فإذا عجز عن الذبح جعل الصوم خلفاً عنه في إباحة التحلل بالحلق، فإذا قدر على الذبح في أيام النحر قبل الحلق وجب الذبح لعدم حصول المقصود بالخلف فبطل الخلف كما لو وجد المتيمم الماء قبل الصلاة، أما لو قدر عليه بعد الحلق لا يبطل الصوم كما لو وجد الماء بعد الصلاة لحصول المقصود به وهو التحلل بالحلق، وحينئذ فحصول الأصل الذي هو الذبح بعد تحقق المقصود الذي هو الحلق أو التقصير لا ينقض الخلف الذي هو الصوم . ، هذا معنى ما في الفتح وغيره، وليس في كلام الفتح ولا في غيره جعل الحلق خلفاً عن الذبح، وقولهم العبرة لأيام النحر » يعني قبل حصول المقصود فافهم قوله : (ويدل على أنه لو صام في وقته انظر ما هذه الدلالة وما وجهها وليس هذا في الفتح
His saying: (and he fasts who is unable to [offer] it, three days the last of which is the day of Arafah, and seven when he returns, even if in Makkah) means: he fasts who is unable to offer the hady, due to His saying: 'But if you cannot find [the animal], then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return' [Quran 2:196]. And his saying: 'as he restricted it in slaughtering the mufrid' is an oversight because he did not restrict it also, rather he said: 'then slaughter, then shave or shorten, and shaving is better.' His saying: (and he indicated by the choice between a camel and a seventh of it that it is a blood of worship etc.) its implication is that if it were a blood of penalty, he would not have choice. And in Udhiya of al-Wiqaya and its commentary by al-Qahistani: like a cow slaughtered by three for udhiya, tamattu', and qiran in Hajj, it is valid. Likewise, if seven slaughter for those and for ihsar and compensation for hunting or shaving and aqiqah and voluntary, it is valid according to apparent principles. And from Abu Yusuf: the best is that they be of one type. So if they are different and each approaches [Allah], it is permissible. And from Abu Hanifa: that it is disliked, as in al-Nazm. And it will be mentioned in al-Hady that partnership in a camel is like in udhiya, provided all intend qurbah even if their types of blood are different. End. Tamattu', ihsar, compensation for hunting, etc. End. His saying: (and sharing in a cow is better than a sheep). Al-Sharnaballali said: it is restricted to when his share of the cow is more valuable than a sheep, as in the poem of Ibn Wahban. The author's saying: (and he fasts who is unable to about it) our companions differed in defining the limit of wealth in the chapter of expiations. Some said: provision of a month; if he has less than that, fasting is permissible for him. Ibn Muqatil said: whoever has provision of a day and night, fasting is not permissible for him if the food he has is the amount that is obligatory upon him, and this agrees with what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf: that if he has the amount with which to buy what is obligatory and has nothing else, fasting is not permissible for him. And some said regarding the one who works with his hands, i.e., the earner: he retains his day's provision and expiates with the rest, and the one who does not work retains a month's provision as mentioned by al-Kirmani, and it is a good detail except that this is when there is no specific property in his possession, otherwise fasting is not permissible for him as clarified in al-Khulasa and al-Bada'i'. And if he has a debt as mentioned by some. And from Abu Yusuf, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa: if he has surplus beyond his dwelling and clothing beyond sufficiency and that surplus is two hundred dirhams or more, fasting is not permissible for him. Thus in Sharh al-Lubab. In the footnote of al-Madani from al-Mansak al-Kabir of al-Sindi: it is understood from the expression of al-Zahiriyya that one who is in Makkah poor but in his country wealthy, fasting is permissible for him because the place of the blood is Makka. (1) Narrated by Muslim in the Book of Renunciation, Hadith 46. [PAGE_632] 632 Book of Hajj, Chapter of Qiran: he fasts ten complete days [Quran 2:196]. And consideration is given to the days of Nahr in terms of inability and ability. Likewise, if he becomes able to offer the hady before completing the three-day fast, or after completing it before shaving and becoming halal while it is still the days of slaughter, his fast is invalidated and he is not released except by the hady. And if he found the hady after shaving and becoming halal before... his fast is valid and he does not have to slaughter the hady. And if he fasted three days and did not shave or become halal until the days of slaughter passed, then he found the hady, his fast is valid and nothing is upon him. Thus mentioned al-Asbijabi. And it indicates that if he fasted in its time while the hady existed, it is considered: if he remains until the Day of Nahr, it does not suffice him due to ability on the original; and if... so his ease and hardship are considered by it. End. His saying: (and consideration is given to the days of Nahr in inability and ability). Al-Sharnaballali mentioned in a treatise he called Badi'at al-Hady limā istaysara min al-Hady and mentioned that the analyzer of the restrictions for the non-muhsar is only shaving or shortening, and for the muhsar slaughtering the hady in its place. And he mentioned that the hady is obligatory as gratitude upon the qarin and mutamatti', and that it is the original and the fast is a substitute for it, and that the condition of its substitution is the presentation of the three [days] before the Day of Nahr. Then he verified that consideration is for the existence of the hady during the days of Nahr, and that there is no substitution for the hady and shaving such that it could be said that existence of the hady after shaving does not affect: the intended goal is achieved by the substitute, which is shaving, as occurs in several reliable texts, because shaving has no role before its existence, so its existence during them invalidates the ruling of the fast and necessitates his slaughtering it, even if he became released before it due to the generality of the text, and due to the saying of the verifiers: consideration is for the days of Nahr, existence and non-existence of the hady. Al-Kamal said: if he becomes able to offer the hady during the three [fasting days] or after them before the Day of Nahr, the hady becomes incumbent and the fast falls, because it is a substitute, and if he becomes able from the original before the execution of the ruling by the substitute, the substitute is invalidated. End. So he stated that the fast is a substitute for the hady, and one does not become released by the hady nor by its substitute but by shaving or shortening, and this is exactly correct. As for his saying: 'And if he becomes able to offer the hady after shaving before he fasts the seven during the days of slaughter or after them, the hady does not become incumbent because the release has already occurred by shaving, so the existence of the original after it does not invalidate the substitute.' End. There is contradiction and restriction of the absolute of the book as advanced, because he implied that one becomes released by the hady originally and by shaving as a substitute, so if he finds the hady, it does not invalidate his substitute which is shaving according to his latter statement, but the correct is his former statement. Then he transmitted similar from al-Muhit and others, and from what is in this commentary, and he disputed them with what passed. The summary of his statement is: the hady becomes obligatory by its existence during the days of Nahr whether he shaves or not, and that the hady is not dropped except by its existence after them, contrary to what is stated in many reliable texts. I say: it is not hidden from you that it is obligatory to follow the transmitted; and its justification is that the purpose of slaughtering is to permit release by shaving or shortening. So if he is unable to slaughter, the fast is made a substitute for him in permitting release by shaving. So if he becomes able to slaughter during the days of Nahr before shaving, slaughtering becomes obligatory because the purpose has not been achieved by the substitute, so the substitute becomes invalid, just like if a person who performs tayammum finds water before prayer. As for if he becomes able after shaving, the fast is not invalidated, just like if he finds water after prayer, because the purpose has been achieved, namely release by shaving. Therefore, the occurrence of the original, which is slaughter, after the achievement of the purpose, which is shaving or shortening, does not invalidate the substitute, which is the fast. This is the meaning in al-Fath and others, and in the speech of al-Fath nor others is making shaving a substitute for slaughter. And their saying 'consideration is for the days of Nahr' means before the achievement of the purpose, so understand. His saying: (and it indicates that if he fasts in its time, look) what this indication is and what its face is, and this is not in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of fasting for the qarin or mutamatti' who cannot afford the hady. It begins by stating the condition: the person must be 'ajiz (unable) to find or afford the hady. The fast is three days during Hajj (the last being the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, Arafah) and seven days after returning home (or in Makkah if staying). The evidence is the Quranic verse (2:196). The commentary then discusses the definition of 'inability' (al-ajz), presenting several opinions from Hanafi scholars: some say one must lack a month's provision; others say a day's provision; yet others that one must have no surplus beyond basic needs and debt. The relied-upon position is that one is considered able if he has the price of the hady or enough wealth (nisab) beyond his needs. The main focus then shifts to the effect of later acquiring the hady. If he becomes able to afford the hady during the days of slaughter (10th-13th of Dhul Hijjah) before he shaves (halq or taqsir), his fast becomes invalid and he must slaughter. If he becomes able after shaving (i.e., after he has already become halal via the substitute fast), his fast remains valid and no slaughter is required. The commentator discusses a subtle ikhtilaf: some (like Al-Kamal) hold that finding the hady before the Day of Nahr invalidates the fast even if after shaving, but the majority (and the view adopted in al-Fath) is that it does not, because the purpose (release) was already achieved by shaving, analogous to tayammum after prayer. The passage concludes by affirming that the fast is a substitute (khalaf) for the hady, and the hady does not release one; release is only by shaving. Therefore, if one finds the hady after shaving, the substitute (fast) is not invalidated.

Key Terms
العجز (al-'ajz): Inability to afford the hady; defined by various opinions as lacking a month's provision, or a day's, or having no surplus beyond essential needs.
الخلف (al-khalaf): Substitute: the fast is a substitute (khalaf) for the hady in permitting release by shaving.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): Days of sacrifice: the 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mutamatti' fasts three days during Hajj but finds a hady on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah after shaving his head. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) He must slaughter the hady and his fast is invalid.
B) His fast remains valid and he does not need to slaughter.
C) He must fast an additional seven days.
D) He must both slaughter and repeat the fast.

Key Takeaway
The substitute fast for the hady is invalidated only if the pilgrim becomes able to slaughter before shaving during the days of Nahr; after shaving, the fast is final.

Validity of Substitute Fast When Able to Offer Hady in Hajj
Ruling with proof on invalidity of substitute fast when ability to offer hady arises before halq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of the substitute fast when the pilgrim becomes able to offer hady during the days of Nahr, and distinguish between cases before and after halq.

Core Idea
Ability to offer hady before halq invalidates the substitute fast; after halq, the fast stands.

In this lesson, we examine a key issue in Hajj fiqh: the interaction between the sacrificial animal (hady) and its substitute, fasting. Using the Quranic verse (2:196) and qiyas with tayammum, the Hanafi school establishes a precise timeline for when the substitute remains valid. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the relied-upon position and addresses an intra-madhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is fasting as a substitute (badal) for hady for a qarin or mutamatti'. The ruling depends on timing: if ability to offer hady arises before halq, the fast is invalid (batil); if after halq, the fast is valid (sahih).
The days of Nahr (10-12 Dhul Hijjah) are the critical period for determining ability.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 2:196, which makes fasting a substitute when one cannot find hady. The passage also uses qiyas to tayammum: just as finding water before prayer invalidates tayammum, finding hady before halq invalidates the substitute fast.
The thubut of the Quranic verse is qati, but its dalala is zanni regarding the exact timing, hence the ikhtilaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse conditions fasting on the inability to find hady. 'Finding' is interpreted as having the ability to offer it during the days of Nahr. The purpose of the substitute is to permit tahlul via halq. If the original becomes available before halq, the substitute is no longer needed.
The analogy to tayammum reinforces that the substitute is only valid until the original is attainable before the goal (prayer/halq) is achieved.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih
Some later Hanafi scholars argued that even finding hady after halq invalidates the fast. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), supported by al-Kamal ibn al-Humam and others, is that after halq the fast is valid because the goal of tahlul is already attained.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq prefers the position that halq is the decisive factor, not the days of Nahr alone.

هلك قبل الذبح جاز للعجز عن الأصل فكان المعتبر وقت التحلل. كذا في فتح القدير.
Chapter of Qiran: He fasts the seven (and) ten complete [Al-Baqarah 2:196]. And the consideration is for the days of Nahr in inability and ability. Similarly, if he becomes able to offer hady before completing the fast of three days, or after completing but before he shaves and becomes lawful, while it is in the days of slaughter, his fast is invalidated and he does not become lawful except with hady. And if he finds hady after he has shaved and become lawful before... his fast is valid and he is not obliged to slaughter the hady. And if he fasted three days and did not shave or become lawful until the days of slaughter passed, then he finds hady, his fast is valid and nothing is due upon him. Thus mentioned al-Asbijaabi. And it indicates that if he fasts in its time while having hady, consider: if he remains until the day of Nahr, it does not suffice him due to ability over the original; and if... so his ease and hardship are considered by it. End quote. His statement: (And the consideration is for the days of Nahr in inability and ability). Al-Shurunbulali mentioned in a treatise named Badi'at al-Hady lima Istarasa min al-Hady, and mentioned that the analyser for one not under constraint (muhsar) is shaving or trimming, and for the muhsar slaughtering hady in its place, and mentioned that hady is obligatory as gratitude for the qarin and mutamatti', and it is the original and fast is a substitute for it, and that the condition of its substitution is advancing the three before the day of Nahr. Then he verified that the consideration is for the existence of hady in the days of Nahr, and that there is no substitution for hady and shaving such that it is said existence of hady after shaving does not consider the attainment of the goal by the substitute which is shaving, as occurred in several reliable texts, because shaving has no impact before its existence, so its existence in them invalidates the ruling of the fast, so he must slaughter it, even if he became lawful before it due to the requirement of the absolute text, and due to the saying of the verifiers: the consideration is for the days of Nahr, existence and non-existence of hady. Al-Kamal said: If he becomes able to offer hady during the three or after them before the day of Nahr, hady is due upon him and the fast falls because it is a substitute, and if he becomes able over the original before the performance of the ruling by the substitute, the substitute is invalidated. End quote. So he stated that the fast is a substitute for hady, and one does not become lawful by hady nor by its substitute, but rather by shaving or trimming, and this is correct. As for his statement: 'And if he becomes able to offer hady after shaving before he fasts the seven in the days of slaughter or after, hady is not due upon him because the tahlul has occurred by shaving, so the existence of the original after it does not overturn the substitute' End quote. There is conflict and restriction of the absolute of the book as preceded, because he indicated that one becomes lawful by hady originally and by shaving as a substitute, so if hady appears, it does not invalidate its substitute which is shaving according to his last statement, and the correct is his first statement. Then he transmitted similar from al-Muheet and others, and from what is in this Sharh, and he disputed with them by what has passed. The summary of his saying is the obligation of hady by its existence in the days of Nahr, whether he shaved or not, and that hady is not dropped except by its existence after them, contrary to what is stipulated in many reliable books. I say: It is not hidden from you that the obligatory is to follow the transmitted, and its face is that the purpose of slaughter is to permit tahlul by shaving or trimming. So if he is unable to slaughter, fasting is made a substitute for it in permitting tahlul by shaving. So if he becomes able to slaughter in the days of Nahr before shaving, slaughter becomes obligatory due to the non-attainment of the purpose by the substitute, so the substitute is invalidated, just as if one who performs tayammum finds water before prayer. But if he becomes able after shaving, the fast is not invalidated, just as if one finds water after prayer, because the purpose has been attained, which is tahlul by shaving. So the occurrence of the original, which is slaughter, after the attainment of the purpose, which is shaving or trimming, does not overturn the substitute, which is fasting. This is the meaning in al-Fath and others. And there is not in the speech of al-Fath nor others making shaving a substitute for slaughter. And their saying: the consideration is for the days of Nahr means before attainment of the purpose. So understand. His statement: (And it indicates that if he fasts in its time... look what this indication is and what its face is, and this is not in al-Fath). It became destroyed before slaughter, it is permitted due to inability over the original, so the consideration is the time of tahlul. Thus in Fath al-Qadeer.
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Qiran in Hajj. It begins by stating the general principle: the consideration for ability or inability to offer the hady (sacrificial animal) is the days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah). If a mutamatti' or qarin becomes able to offer the hady during these days before he shaves his head (halq) and becomes lawful from ihram, his substitute fast (the three days or seven days) becomes invalid and he must slaughter the hady. However, if he finds the hady after he has already shaved and become lawful, his fast remains valid and no hady is required. The author supports this with the Quranic verse (2:196) and cites al-Asbijaabi. The passage then delves into a scholarly dispute: some argue that the existence of hady even after halq invalidates the fast, but the correct Hanafi position, as clarified by al-Kamal and others, is that the fast is a substitute for the hady, and the goal is the tahlul achieved by halq. Once halq has occurred, the purpose is fulfilled, so finding the hady later does not affect the fast. The analogy to tayammum is drawn: finding water after prayer does not invalidate the prayer, similarly, finding hady after halq does not invalidate the fast. The commentary emphasizes that the reliance is on the transmitted texts, and the proper understanding is that the days of Nahr are the criterion for capability only before the attainment of the goal (halq). The passage ends with a note about the evidence and a reference to Fath al-Qadeer regarding a case where the hady dies before slaughter.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal offered by a qarin or mutamatti' as an act of gratitude and expiation.
خلاف (khilaf): Substitute; here, the fast stands in place of the hady when one is unable to offer it.
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days of sacrifice: the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head to exit ihram; it is a required action for tahlul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mutamatti' fasts three days as a substitute for hady. After completing the fast but before shaving his head, he receives a gift of a sheep sufficient for hady. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) His fast is valid and he does not need to slaughter the sheep.
B) His fast becomes invalid and he must slaughter the sheep as hady.
C) He may choose to either continue with the fast or slaughter the sheep.
D) He must repeat both the fast and slaughter the sheep.

Key Takeaway
The substitute fast for hady is valid only if the ability to offer hady arises after halq; if it arises before halq, the substitute is void and hady becomes obligatory.

The Meaning of 'Return' in Hajj Fasting: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on interpreting 'return' in the fasting verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of 'return' (الرجوع) in verse 2:196 and explain why the Hanafi school permits fasting the seven days in Makkah before returning home.

Core Idea
To avoid hardship, Hanafis interpret 'return' as completing Hajj rituals, not physically going home.

The Quran commands those performing tamattu' to fast three days during Hajj and seven upon 'return'. But what does 'return' mean? A difference between Hanafis and Shafi'is arises: should the seven-day fast be delayed until one reaches home, or can it be done in Makkah after the rituals? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi metaphorical interpretation of 'return' and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Term
Locate the word 'return' (الرجوع) in the Quranic verse (2:196) and note the two possible interpretations: literal (physical return to homeland) and metaphorical (completion of Hajj rituals).
The Hanafi school chooses the metaphorical meaning.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Evidence
The Hanafi position: the seven-day fast may be performed after the days of Tashriq in Makkah, before traveling home. Evidence: the case of a person with no homeland, whose only 'return' is from the rituals; also, the word 'return' is broad enough to include this meaning.
The source cites ijma' on the case of a homeless traveler.
3
State the Shafi'i Position and Its Evidence
The Shafi'i position: the seven-day fast must be performed after returning to one's family. Evidence: the literal meaning of the verse and a hadith in Bukhari: 'and seven when you return to your families.'
This is the apparent (zahir) reading.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Why do Hanafis depart from the literal? Because the literal leads to impossibility for some (e.g., a traveler without a fixed home). Necessity (darura) and the principle of avoiding hardship justify the metaphorical interpretation.
The response is based on the agreed-upon branch of a homeless person.
5
Identify the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The difference is clear: Hanafis allow fasting in Makkah immediately after the Hajj rituals; Shafi'is require postponement until return home. This affects pilgrims from faraway lands or those who stay in Makkah after Hajj.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text

And his statement: 'Its last is the day of 'Arafah' is an explanation of the superior (afdal), otherwise its time is the time of Hajj after ihram for 'umrah, because what is meant by 'Hajj' in the verse is its time, since it itself is not suitable as a time. And the reason the delay is superior is because the fast is a substitute for the hady, so it is recommended to delay it to its last time hoping to be able to [offer] the original. Thus in al-Hidayah. And he indicated by his statement 'when you return' that what is meant by 'return' in the verse is being free from the actions of Hajj metaphorically, since being free is the cause of returning to one's family. And al-Shafi'i acted upon the literal meaning, so he did not permit fasting them in Makkah. The hadith of al-Bukhari, raised, supports him: 'and seven when you return to your families.' Rather, our imams turned from the literal to the metaphorical for a branch that is agreed upon: if one has no homeland to return to but is continuously traveling, it is obligatory upon him to fast them by this text; and only the return from the rituals is realized as a return. Similarly, if he returns to Makkah not intending to reside there, even if his return to other than his family and homeland is realized, then it occurs to him to make it his homeland, he may fast there even though his return to his homeland is not realized. Thus in Fath al-Qadeer. And he meant by 'being free' being free from the obligatory and mandatory actions of Hajj, which is with the passing of the days of Tashriq, because the third day is for the obligatory stoning for those who stay until dawn. It follows that if he fasts the seven and some of the days of Tashriq, it is not permissible. And since he mentioned the prohibition of fasting on them absolutely in the discussion of fasting, he did not restrict it here. Rather, what is in it is... (and if he fasts etc.) His statement: (an explanation) (of the superior). Al-Nahr said: He stated by his statement 'its last is the day of 'Arafah' that fasting after it is not permissible, so what is in al-Bahr is questionable. End quote. It was answered that his statement 'an explanation of the superior' refers to delaying the fast to the day of 'Arafah, not to it being before the days of Nahr. End quote. I say: It appears that this was not hidden from the author of al-Nahr, so that he might answer his criticism with this, because the author's expression is explicit in that. Perhaps his intention is that... the books of Manasik interpret the author's speech as explaining what is more important, which is the impermissibility of delay, and then it contains an indication of what is superior, not a separate explanation of the superior while neglecting the important, as the author did. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of the three-day substitute fast for the mutamatti' and the interpretation of the word 'return' in the Quranic verse. The author (likely the commentator) explains that the statement 'its last is the day of 'Arafah' is a recommendation (afdal), not a condition. The proper time for this fast is the period of Hajj after ihram for 'umrah, but the best time is delayed to the day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) in hopes of being able to offer the hady. The Hanafi school interprets 'return' (idha raja'tum) in the verse metaphorically as 'completion of the Hajj rituals', while Imam al-Shafi'i takes it literally as returning to one's homeland. The proof is the hadith in Bukhari: 'and seven when you return to your families.' However, Hanafis offer a practical case: if a person has no homeland (e.g., a perpetual traveler), he can only 'return' from the rituals, so the metaphor must hold. The passage concludes with a discussion of the exact meaning of 'return' and a refutation of a critique by al-Nahr, asserting that the author's intent is clear.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): In this passage, the 'return' mentioned in the Quranic verse; Hanafis interpret it metaphorically as completion of Hajj rituals, Shafi'is as literal return to homeland.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the day of Nahr (11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah); fasting during these days is generally prohibited, and the seven-day fast must be completed after them.
المجاز (al-majaz): Metaphorical interpretation; Hanafis employ it to resolve apparent contradictions in legal texts.
الفراغ (al-faragh): Being free from the obligatory and wajib acts of Hajj; this occurs after the days of Tashriq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Returning to one's homeland after Hajj.
B) Completing the rituals of Hajj and being free to leave.
C) Returning to ihram for 'umrah.
D) Returning to Mina for the stoning.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis interpret 'return' in 2:196 as completion of Hajj rituals, allowing the seven-day substitute fast to be performed in Makkah, while Shafi'is require returning home, based on literal reading.

Condition of Ihram for the Three-Day Substitute Fast
Intra-Hanafi explanation of ihram condition for substitute fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of the three-day fast for a mutamatti' and a qarin, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ihram condition for the mutamatti'.

Core Idea
For the qarin, ihram for both Hajj and 'Umrah is required; for the mutamatti', only after ihram for 'Umrah suffices.

This passage addresses the conditions for the substitute fast required from a mutamatti' or qarin who cannot afford the hady. While both must fast after entering ihram, the precise requirement for the mutamatti' is debated: must he be in a state of ihram during the fast, or is it sufficient to have entered ihram previously? The majority Hanafi position resolves this dispute, and we will examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of Hajj performers
Define mutamatti' (performs 'Umrah then Hajj separately) and qarin (performs both with a single ihram). Note their different obligations regarding the substitute fast.
For the qarin, the fast compensates for both Hajj and 'Umrah; for the mutamatti', only for Hajj after 'Umrah.
2
Extract the conditions for the fast from the text
From the passage: the qarin must fast after ihram for both Hajj and 'Umrah. The mutamatti' must fast after ihram for 'Umrah. These are agreed upon (bila khilaf).
The text uses 'after ihram' (بعد الإحرام) as the key phrase.
3
Identify the disputed point
The dispute is whether the mutamatti' must be in a state of ihram (i.e., not yet performed tahlul) at the time of fasting, or whether it is sufficient that he has entered ihram at some earlier time.
The passage says 'هل يشترط صومها في المتمتع حالة وجود الإحرام أم يجوز حال كونه حلالاً'
4
Locate the majority position and the dissenting view
The majority (zahir al-riwayah) hold that ihram for Hajj is not a condition; only that the fast be after ihram for 'Umrah. A minority view (possibly in al-Bada'i') might require the ihram to be intact.
The text says 'فإنه ليس بشرط لصحة صوم المتمتع في ظاهر المذهب على قول الأكثر'
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the mutamatti' fasts after coming out of ihram (halal), the majority consider it valid; the other view would require him to be in ihram during the fast.
This affects when and how the mutamatti' can fulfil his obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (بعد الإحرام بالعمرة) هذا بالنسبة للتمتع ، أما القارن فلا بد أن يكون بعد الإحرام بالحج والعمرة فقد ذكر في اللباب من شرائط صحة صيام الثلاثة أن يصومها بعد الإحرام بهما في القارن وبعد إحرام العمرة في المتمتع . لكن هل يشترط صومها في المتمتع حالة وجود الإحرام أم يجوز حال كونه حلالاً أي بعد ما أحل من إحرام العمرة فيه كلام قال في شرح اللباب ثم اعلم أن كل ما هو شرط في صوم القارن فهو شرط في صوم المتمتع بلا خلاف إلا إحرام الحج فإنه ليس بشرط لصحة صوم المتمتع في ظاهر المذهب على قول الأكثر ، بل يشترط أن يكون بعد إحرام العمرة فقط، فلو صام المتمتع في أشهر الحج بعد ما أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يحرم بالحج جاز إلا أن وجود الإحرام حالة . شرط في جواز صوم القرآن، وأما صوم المتمتع فالأكثر على عدم اشتراط ذلك، ففي البدائع: وهل . ا هـ . صوم الثلاثة
His statement: (after ihram for 'umrah) this is regarding the mutamatti'. As for the qarin, it must be after ihram for Hajj and 'umrah. It is mentioned in al-Lubab among the conditions for the validity of the three-day fast that he fasts them after ihram for both in the case of the qarin, and after ihram for 'umrah in the case of the mutamatti'. But is it required for the mutamatti' to fast while in a state of ihram, or is it permissible while being halal (i.e., after coming out of the ihram for 'umrah)? There is discussion. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: Then know that everything that is a condition for the fast of the qarin is a condition for the fast of the mutamatti' without dispute, except ihram for Hajj, for it is not a condition for the validity of the mutamatti's fast in the apparent school according to the majority. Rather, the condition is only that it be after ihram for 'umrah. So if the mutamatti' fasts in the months of Hajj after he has assumed ihram for 'umrah before he assumes ihram for Hajj, it is permissible. However, the existence of ihram at the time is a condition for the permissibility of the fast of the qarin. As for the fast of the mutamatti', the majority hold that this condition is not required. In al-Bada'i: 'And is...' End quote. The fast of the three.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions for the validity of the three-day substitute fast. It clarifies that for the qarin (one who combines Hajj and 'Umrah), the fast must be performed after entering ihram for both. For the mutamatti', the fast must be after ihram for 'Umrah. The point of dispute is whether the mutamatti' must be in a state of ihram (i.e., not having performed tahlul) at the time of fasting. According to the majority in the school, ihram for Hajj is not a condition for the mutamatti's fast; it is sufficient that he has entered ihram for 'Umrah, even if he later becomes halal before fasting. However, some authorities, as referenced in al-Bada'i', might have required the ihram to be intact. The relied-upon position is that the fast is valid as long as it is performed after the ihram for 'Umrah, even if the person has already come out of ihram. The passage ends abruptly with a reference to al-Bada'i' for further detail.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs 'Umrah during the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year without returning home between them.
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and 'Umrah together with a single ihram.
شرط (shart): Condition necessary for the validity of the substitute fast.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' may fast the three substitute days after entering ihram for 'Umrah, even if he later becomes halal; the majority Hanafi position does not require him to be in ihram during the fast.

Timing of the Three-Day Fast for Tamattu' and Qiran
Explains the ruling on when to fast the three days and the Shafi'i dispute on the verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the three days of fasting for tamattu' and qiran and explain the Hanafi metaphorical interpretation of 'idha raj'atum' in contrast to the Shafi'i literal interpretation.

Core Idea
The three fasts must be completed by the Day of Arafah; 'return' means completion of rituals, not literal homecoming.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when the three days of fasting for tamattu' and qiran must be performed, and addresses a key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'idha raj'atum'. We will see how the Hanafi school uses metaphorical interpretation (majaz) to resolve a practical impossibility that arises from the literal reading.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on timing
The three days must be fasted during the Hajj period after entering ihram for Umrah (for tamattu') or for both Umrah and Hajj (for qiran). The last preferred day is the Day of Arafah, but the entire period from the start of Hajj until Arafah is valid.
The time is not limited to Arafah; delaying to Arafah is recommended.
2
Identify the preferred time and reason
The preferred time is the Day of Arafah because fasting is a substitute for the hady (sacrificial animal), so one hopes to be able to perform the original sacrifice. Thus delay is recommended.
This is based on the principle of preferring the original over the substitute.
3
Explain the Shafi'i literal interpretation
Imam al-Shafi'i interprets the word 'return' (raj'ah) in the verse literally as returning to one's family and homeland. Therefore, he holds that the seven days of fasting (after the three) must be performed after returning home, and not in Makkah.
This is supported by the hadith 'and seven when you return to your families' (Bukhari).
4
Present the Hanafi metaphorical interpretation
The Hanafis interpret 'return' metaphorically as 'completion of Hajj rituals'. This is based on a unanimously agreed branch: if a person has no homeland or returns to Makkah without intending to settle, he must still fast, which would be impossible under the literal reading. Thus the metaphorical interpretation is necessary.
The Hanafis do not reject the hadith but reconcile it through interpretation.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The Shafi'i school requires the seven days to be fasted after returning home, while the Hanafi school permits fasting them in Makkah immediately after completing the Hajj rituals. This affects pilgrims who cannot easily go home or have no fixed home.
The Hanafi view is more flexible for many modern pilgrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب القرآن
٦٣٣
هلك قبل الذبح جاز للعجز عن الأصل فكان المعتبر وقت التحلل. كذا في فتح القدير. وقوله «آخرها يوم عرفة» بيان للأفضل وإلا فوقته وقت الحج بعد الإحرام بالعمرة لأن المراد بالحج في الآية وقته لأن نفسه لا يصلح ظرفاً. وإنما كان الأفضل التأخير لأن الصوم بدل عن الهدي فيستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته رجاء أن يقدر على الأصل كذا في الهداية. وأشار بقوله «إذا فرغ إلى أن المراد بالرجوع في الآية الفراغ من أعمال الحج مجازاً إذ الفراغ سبب للرجوع إلى أهله، وقد عمل الشافعي بالحقيقة فلم يجوز صومها بمكة ويشهد له حديث البخاري مرفوعاً
وسبعة إذا رجعتم إلى أهليكم وإنما عدل أئمتنا عن الحقيقة إلى المجاز لفرع مجمع عليه وهو لو لم يكن له وطن أصلاً ليرجع إليه بل مستمر على السياحة وجب عليه صومها بهذا النص ولا يتحقق في حقه سوى الرجوع عن الأعمال، وكذا لو رجع إلى مكة غير قاصد للإقامة بها حتى تحقق رجوعه إلى غير أهله ووطنه ثم بدا له أن يتخذها وطناً كان له أن يصوم بها مع أنه لم يتحقق منه الرجوع إلى وطنه. كذا في فتح القدير. وأراد بالفراغ الفراغ من فرضاً وواجباً من أعمال الحج وهو بمضي أيام التشريق لأن اليوم الثالث منها يوم للرمي الواجب على من أقام به حتى طلع الفجر فيفيد أنه لو صام السبعة وبعضها من أيام التشريق فإنه لا يجوز ولما قدمه في بحث الصوم من النهي عن الصوم فيها مطلقاً فلذا لم يقيد ههنا.
بل الذي فيه ولو صام الخ) قوله : (بيان) (للأفضل قال في النهر : وأفاد بقوله «آخرها يوم عرفة» أن صومها بعده لا يجوز فما في البحر فيه نظر ا.هـ. وأجيب عنه بأن قوله «بيان للأفضل» راجع إلى تأخير الصوم إلى يوم عرفة لا إلى كونه قبل أيام النحر ا.هـ. قلت والذي يظهر أن هذا لم يخف على صاحب النهر حتى يجاب عن نظره به لأن عبارة المؤلف صريحة في ذلك، ولعل مراده أن المناسك حمل كلام المصنف على بيان ما هو الأهم وهو عدم جواز التأخير ويكون حينئذ فيه إشارة إلى ما هو الأفضل لا على بيان الأفضل وترك الأهم كما فعل المؤلف تأمل. لكن لا يخفي أن قول المصنف الآتي فإن لم يصم الثلاثة إلى يوم النحر تعين الدم صريح في بيان عدم جواز التأخير فلذا جعل المؤلف قول المصنف هنا «آخرها يوم عرفة» بياناً للأفضل لئلا يتكرر كلامه فتأمل قوله : (بعد الإحرام بالعمرة) هذا بالنسبة للتمتع، أما القارن فلا بد أن يكون بعد الإحرام بالحج والعمرة فقد ذكر في اللباب من شرائط صحة صيام الثلاثة أن يصومها بعد الإحرام بهما في القارن وبعد إحرام العمرة في المتمتع. لكن هل يشترط صومها في المتمتع حالة وجود الإحرام أم يجوز حال كونه حلالاً أي بعد ما أحل من إحرام العمرة فيه كلام قال في شرح اللباب ثم اعلم أن كل ما هو شرط في صوم القارن فهو شرط في صوم المتمتع بلا خلاف إلا إحرام الحج فإنه ليس بشرط لصحة صوم المتمتع في ظاهر المذهب على قول الأكثر، بل يشترط أن يكون بعد إحرام العمرة فقط، فلو صام المتمتع في أشهر الحج بعد ما أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يحرم بالحج جاز إلا أن وجود الإحرام حالة شرط في جواز صوم القرآن، وأما صوم المتمتع فالأكثر على عدم اشتراط ذلك، ففي البدائع: وهل ا.هـ. صوم الثلاثة
Book of Hajj: Chapter on Qiran. If it perishes before slaughter, it is permissible due to inability to perform the original, so the consideration is the time of tahlul. So in Fath al-Qadir. His statement 'Its last is the Day of Arafah' is a clarification of the preferred, otherwise its time is the time of Hajj after ihram for Umrah because what is meant by Hajj in the verse is its time, because the essence itself is not suitable as a time. And the preference is to delay because fasting is a substitute for the hady, so it is recommended to delay it to the end of its time hoping to be able to perform the original. So in al-Hidayah. And he indicated by his statement 'when you have finished' that what is meant by 'return' in the verse is metaphorically the completion of the rituals of Hajj, since completion is the cause of returning to one's family. Al-Shafi'i acted on the literal meaning and did not permit fasting them in Makkah, and the hadith of Bukhari raised supports him: 'and seven when you return to your families.' Our imams departed from the literal to the metaphorical due to a unanimously agreed upon branch: if one has no homeland at all to return to, but is continuously traveling, then fasting them is obligatory by this text, and in his case only the return from the rituals is realized. Likewise, if he returned to Makkah not intending to stay there, so his return to other than his family and homeland is realized, then he decides to take it as a homeland, he may fast there even though he has not realized return to his homeland. So in Fath al-Qadir. He intended by 'finishing' the completion of the obligatory and necessary acts of Hajj, which is the passing of the days of tashriq, because the third day is for the obligatory stoning for one who remains there until dawn, so it indicates that if he fasts the seven and some of the days of tashriq, it is not permissible. And since he presented in the discussion of fasting the prohibition of fasting on those days absolutely, he did not qualify it here. Rather, in which is 'and if he fasted etc.' His statement: 'clarification' of the preferred. He said in al-Nahr: And what he said 'its last is the Day of Arafah' indicates that fasting after it is not permissible, so what is in al-Bahr is questionable. It was answered that his statement 'clarification of the preferred' refers to delaying the fast to the Day of Arafah, not to it being before the days of Nahr. I say: It appears that this was not hidden from the author of al-Nahr such that it is answered by this, because the author's expression is explicit in that. Perhaps his intent is that the rituals carry the author's speech to an explanation of what is more important, which is the impermissibility of delay, and then there is in it an indication of what is preferred, not an explanation of the preferred and leaving the more important as the author did, reflect. But it is not hidden that the author's later statement 'if he does not fast the three until Yawm al-Nahr, the blood becomes due' is explicit in showing the impermissibility of delay, so the author made his statement here 'its last is the Day of Arafah' a clarification of the preferred so that his speech is not repeated, reflect. His statement: 'after ihram for Umrah' this is for tamattu'. As for the qarin, it must be after ihram for Hajj and Umrah. It was mentioned in al-Lubab that among the conditions for the validity of fasting the three is that he fasts them after ihram for both in the qarin and after ihram for Umrah in the mutamatti'. But is it required to fast them in the state of ihram in the mutamatti', or is it permissible while he is halal (after leaving ihram of Umrah)? There is discussion. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: 'Then know that every condition for the fast of the qarin is a condition for the fast of the mutamatti' without exception except ihram for Hajj, for it is not a condition for the validity of the mutamatti's fast in the apparent madhhab according to the majority. Rather, it is required only that it be after ihram for Umrah. So if the mutamatti' fasts in the months of Hajj after he has entered ihram for Umrah before he enters ihram for Hajj, it is permissible, except that the existence of ihram for Hajj is a condition for the permissibility of the qiran fast. As for the mutamatti's fast, the majority do not require that. In al-Bada'i': 'Is...' end. Fasting the three.
Source pages p. 633

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the timing of the three days of fasting required for tamattu' and qiran. The author begins by stating that the last permissible day for these fasts is the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), but this is for preference; technically the time is the entire Hajj period after entering ihram for Umrah. The preferred position is to delay the fast to the Day of Arafah because it is a substitute for the sacrificial animal (hady), so one hopes to be able to perform the original sacrifice. The text then addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the Quranic verse 'and seven when you return' (2:196). Al-Shafi'i takes the literal meaning of 'return' as returning to one's homeland, so he does not permit fasting the seven days in Makkah. The Hanafis interpret 'return' metaphorically as 'completion of the Hajj rituals,' based on a unanimously agreed branch: a person with no homeland or one who returns to Makkah without intending to settle must still fast, so the literal meaning cannot apply. The Hanafi position is supported by the ḥadīth in Bukhari, but they reconcile it through metaphorical interpretation. The passage also discusses that the condition for fasting in tamattu' is after ihram for Umrah only, not necessarily during ihram for Hajj, unlike the qarin who must fast after ihram for both. This is the apparent madhhab. Overall, the passage clarifies the timing, the preferred delay, and defends the Hanafi interpretation against Shafi'i.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah during the months of Hajj followed by Hajj in the same year with a break (tahlul) in between.
القارن (al-qarin): One who enters ihram for both Umrah and Hajj together without a break.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal (camel, cow, or sheep) required for tamattu' and qiran as a compensaton.
الدم (al-dam): Blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) due as compensation for various omissions or violations during Hajj/Umrah.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): In the context of the verse, interpreted metaphorically as completion of Hajj rituals, not physical return to home.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is meant by 'idha raj'atum' in the verse about fasting seven days?
A) When you physically return to your families
B) When you have completed the Hajj rituals
C) When you return to the state of halal
D) When you return to Makkah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits fasting the seven days in Makkah because 'return' in the verse means completion of Hajj rituals, not literal homecoming.

Obligation of Blood (Dam) if Fasting Not Completed by Yawm al-Nahr
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a tamattu' or qarin must complete the three days of fasting by Yawm al-Nahr, explain why failure makes blood (dam) obligatory, and distinguish between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn on multiple dams for shaving before sacrificing.

Core Idea
Fasting for tamattu' is a substitute for sacrifice; if not completed by Yawm al-Nahr, the original obligation of dam becomes wajib.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical timing issue in Hajj. A mutamatti' or qarin must fast three days during Hajj; if these fasts are not completed by Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), the fast becomes invalid and a blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory. The text also delves into an intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a qarin shaves before sacrificing, does he owe one dam or two? We will follow the reasoning and the resolution provided by the commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting three days for a mutamatti' or qarin. The ruling: if not completed by Yawm al-Nahr, the fast is invalid and dam becomes wajib.
This is the core ruling from the passage.
2
Understand the legal rationale
The fast is a substitute (badal) for the hady. Substitutes are only valid within the time specified by the Law. Once the time expires, the original obligation (dam) revives.
The text states: 'because the fast is a substitute, and a substitute is only established by the Law.'
3
Examine the proof
The proof is the command of Ibn Umar (RA) to slaughter a sheep in such a case. In Hanafi usul, the action of a Companion is considered a proof (hujjah).
The dalil is a qawl sahabi, which is zanni al-thubut but accepted as evidence.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on shaving
If a qarin shaves before sacrificing: Abu Hanifah says two dams (one for shaving at wrong time, one for delaying sacrifice); Sahibayn say one dam. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends Abu Hanifah, explaining that the number depends on whether the delay was due to inability (excused) or transgression.
This resolves the apparent contradiction between sections in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يصم إلى يوم النحر تعين الدم أي إن لم يصم الثلاثة حتى دخل يوم النحر لم يجزه الصوم أصلاً وصار الدم متعيناً لأن الصوم بدل وإلا بدال لا تنصب إلا شرعاً والنص خصه بوقت الحج وجواز الدم على الأصل، وعن ابن عمر أنه أمر في مثله بذبح الشاة فلو لم يقدر على الهدي تحلل وعليه دمان دم التمتع ودم التحلل قبل الهدي. كذا في الهداية هنا. وقال فيما يأتي في آخر الجنايات : فإن حلق القارن قبل أن يذبح فعليه دمان عند أبي حنيفة دم بالحلق في غير أوانه لأن أوانه بعد الذبح ودم بتأخير الذبح عن الحلق. وعندهما يجب عليه دم واحد وهو الأول فنسبه صاحب غاية البيان إلى التخليط لكونه جعل أحد الدمين هنا دم الشكر والآخر دم الجناية وهو صواب وفيما يأتي أثبت عند أبي حنيفة دمين آخرين سوى دم الشكر ونسبه في فتح القدير أيضاً في باب الجنايات إلى السهو وليس كما قالا بل كلامه صواب في الموضعين فهنا لما لم يكن جانياً بالتأخير لأنه لعجزه لم يلزمه لأجله دم ولزمه دم للحلق في غير أوانه، وفي باب الجنايات لما كان جانياً بحلقه قبل الذبح لزمه دمان كما قرره ولم يذكر دم الشكر لأنه قدمه في باب القران وليس الكلام إلا في الجناية وسيأتي تمامه هناك بأزيد من هذا إن شاء الله تعالى
If he does not fast until Yawm al-Nahr, the blood becomes determined; meaning if he does not fast the three until Yawm al-Nahr enters, the fast is not valid at all and the blood becomes determined because the fast is a substitute, and a substitute is only established by the Law, and the text specifies it for the time of Hajj, and the blood (sacrifice) is permissible on the original. And from Ibn 'Umar that he commanded in such a case to slaughter a sheep. So if he cannot afford the hady, he may exit ihram (tahlul) and upon him are two dams: dam for tamattu' and dam for tahlul before the hady. So in al-Hidayah here. And he said later in the last chapter of Jinayat: If the qarin shaves before sacrificing, upon him are two dams according to Abu Hanifah: a dam for shaving at an improper time because its proper time is after the slaughter, and a dam for delaying the slaughter from the shaving. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), only one dam is due, which is the former. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan attributed confusion to him for making one of the two dams here the dam of gratitude and the other the dam of transgression, but it is correct. And later he affirmed for Abu Hanifah two other dams besides the dam of gratitude, and in Fath al-Qadir also in the chapter of Jinayat he attributed it to forgetfulness, but it is not as they said; rather his speech is correct in both places. Here, since he was not a transgressor by delaying because of his inability, no dam is obligated on him for that, and a dam is obligated for shaving at an improper time. And in the chapter of Jinayat, since he was a transgressor by shaving before the slaughter, two dams are obligated as he determined, and he did not mention the dam of gratitude because he already presented it in the chapter of Qiran, and the discussion there is only about transgression. Its completion will come there with more than this, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the statement of Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). It establishes that if a mutamatti' or qarin does not fast the three days before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah), then the fast becomes invalid and the blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory instead. The reason is that fasting is only a substitute for the hady, and the Law only permits it at the time of Hajj. Once that time passes, the original obligation (the sacrifice) takes effect. The text then enters an intra-Hanafi discussion about a qarin who shaves his head before sacrificing. According to Abu Hanifah, two dams are due: one for shaving before the proper time (which is after slaughter), and one for delaying the slaughter due to the shaving. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), only one dam is due (the first). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends the apparent contradiction between the ruling in this chapter and the later chapter in al-Hidayah, explaining that here the person is excused due to inability, so only the dam for shaving at the wrong time is due, whereas in the Jinayat chapter the person is a transgressor, so two dams are due. This resolves the confusion attributed by some commentators.

Key Terms
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice, marking the end of the time for fasting the three days.
الدم (al-dam): The obligatory blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) that becomes due as compensation.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head, which is a ritual act of leaving ihram, but must be done after sacrifice; doing it earlier is a violation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what happens if a mutamatti' does not fast the three days by Yawm al-Nahr?
A) He may still fast after Yawm al-Nahr
B) The blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory
C) He must sacrifice a camel
D) He must repeat the Umrah

Key Takeaway
If the tamattu' fast is not completed by Yawm al-Nahr, the fast becomes invalid and a blood sacrifice is wajib; if a qarin shaves before sacrificing, the number of dams depends on whether he was excused or a transgressor.

The Dam for a Qarin Who Fails to Perform Umrah Tawaf Before Arafat
Ruling that a qarin who stands at Arafat without Umrah tawaf owes a dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a qarin who stands at Arafat without having performed Umrah tawaf and explain why a dam is owed.

Core Idea
A qarin who stands at Arafat without Umrah tawaf owes a dam because the Umrah becomes impossible after Hajj actions begin.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim who enters ihram for both Umrah and Hajj (qiran) but, for whatever reason, reaches Arafat without having performed the tawaf of Umrah. The classical Hanafi texts rule that such a person owes a dam (blood sacrifice) as compensation for abandoning the Umrah. We'll examine the reasoning and the conditions that trigger this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act in question is a qarin standing at Arafat without having performed the tawaf of Umrah. The ruling is that a dam becomes wajib.
The dam is not for missing tawaf per se but for abandoning the Umrah entirely, as it becomes impossible to complete after wuquf.
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
The passage explains that once a person stands at Arafat, the actions of Hajj begin. If he then tries to perform Umrah tawaf, he would be building Umrah actions on Hajj actions, which is contrary to the legislated order (khilaf al-mashru'). Therefore, the Umrah is considered abandoned, and a dam is due.
The key phrase is 'تعذر عليه أداؤها' (it became impossible for him to perform it).
3
Clarify what constitutes 'not performing tawaf'
The passage notes that 'not entering Makkah' is a metaphor for not performing tawaf. However, if a pilgrim completes four or more circuits of tawaf before standing at Arafat, it is as if he performed tawaf, and no dam is due. The ruling applies only if he did not complete at least four circuits.
The four circuits threshold is mentioned in the text: 'حتى لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط ثم وقف بعرفة يجوز'.
4
Consider exceptions and variations
The passage also discusses the number of dams in more complex scenarios, such as when the qarin also shaves before sacrificing or delays the slaughter. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, there might be up to three dams in some cases, but the core ruling remains that at least one dam is due for abandoning the Umrah.
This step introduces the intra-Hanafi discussion about the number of dams, which depends on whether the pilgrim is a transgressor or excused due to inability.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical case
Take a scenario: A qarin enters Makkah but due to extreme crowd, he does not perform tawaf and proceeds to Arafat. He owes a dam. If he had performed four circuits before leaving for Arafat, no dam is due.
This step solidifies the understanding by applying the rule to a concrete example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يدخل مكة ووقف بعرفة فعليه دم لرفض العمرة وقضاؤها يعني إن لم يأت القارن بالعمرة حتى أتى بالوقوف فعليه دم لترك العمرة لأنه تعذر عليه أداؤها لأنه يصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج، وذلك خلاف المشروع فعدم دخول مكة كناية عن عدم طواف العمرة لأن الدخول وعدمه سواء إذا لم يطف لها والمراد أكثر أشواطه حتى لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط ثم وقف بعرفة يجوز له بعد ما أحرم بالعمرة في أشهر الحج قبل أن يحرم بالحج ؟ قال أصحابنا، يجوز، سواء طاف لعمرته أو لم يطف ا.هـ. وهو ظاهر في هذا المعنى لكن ليس بصريح في المدعى إذ يمكن حمله على المتمتع الذي ساق الهدي، وكذا ما في المدارك وشرح الكنز من أن وقته أشهر الحج الإحرامين في حق المتمتع لكنه أنه لا يصح بعد إحرام الحج وليس كذلك، بل بعده هو المستحب أو المتعين. اهـ ملخصاً وتمامه فيه قوله : بل كلامه صواب في الموضعين (الخ حاصله أنه يجب عليه عند الإمام ثلاثة دماء : دم القرآن ودم الجناية على الإحرام بالحلق في غير أوانه ودم تأخير الذبح. ولما كان فرض المسألة هنا فيمن عجز عن الهدي لم يكن جانباً بتأخيره وإنما الجناية حصلت بالحلق في غير أوانه فلزمه دم له ودم للقران وأما ما في الجنايات فهو في غير العاجز فلزمه دمان. ولم يذكر دم الشكر لذكره له هنا لكن لزوم الدمين هناك خلاف المذهب وساغ حمل كلام الهداية عليه لتصحيحه وإخراجه عن الخطأ والسهو. هذا وقد يقال إنه إذا لم يكن جانباً بالتأخير لم يكن جانباً أيضاً بالحلق في غير أوانه فينبغي أن لا يلزمه إلا دم القرآن لأن العجز عذر، وقد نقل الشرنبلالي في رسالته عن شرح مختصر الطحاوي للإمام الأسبيجابي ما نصه : ولو لم يصم الثلاثة لم يجز الصوم بعد ذلك ولا يجزئه إلا
And if he does not enter Makkah and stands at Arafat, upon him is a dam for abandoning the Umrah and its completion. Meaning if the qarin did not perform Umrah until he performed the standing (at Arafat), upon him is a dam for leaving the Umrah because it became impossible for him to perform it, since he would be building the actions of Umrah on the actions of Hajj, and that is contrary to what is legislated. So not entering Makkah is a metaphor for not performing tawaf for Umrah, because entering or not is the same if he does not perform tawaf for it, and what is meant is the majority of its circuits, so that if he performed four circuits for it then stood at Arafat... Is it permissible for him after he enters ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj before he enters ihram for Hajj? Our companions said: It is permissible, whether he performed tawaf for his Umrah or not. End. And it is apparent in this meaning but not explicit in the claim, because it can be carried upon the mutamatti' who drove the hady. Likewise what is in al-Madarik and Sharh al-Kanz that its time is the months of Hajj for the two ihrams for the mutamatti', but it is that it is not valid after ihram for Hajj, and it is not so; rather, after it is the preferred or the determined. End summarized. And its completion is in his statement: Rather, his speech is correct in both places. The summary is that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, three dams are due: dam for qiran, dam for transgression on ihram by shaving at an improper time, and dam for delaying the slaughter. Since the assumption of the issue here is about one who is unable to afford the hady, he is not a transgressor by delaying, but the transgression occurred by shaving at an improper time, so one dam for that and one for qiran are due. As for what is in the Jinayat chapter, it is about one who is not unable, so two dams are due. And he did not mention the dam of gratitude because he already mentioned it here, but the requirement of two dams there is contrary to the madhhab, and it was allowed to carry the speech of al-Hidayah upon it to correct it and remove it from error and forgetfulness. This: It may be said that if he is not a transgressor by delay, he is also not a transgressor by shaving at an improper time, so only the dam for qiran should be due because inability is an excuse. And al-Shurunbulali transmitted in his treatise from Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi by Imam al-Usbijabi: 'If he does not fast the three, the fast is not valid after that, and nothing suffices him except...'
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that a qarin who does not enter Makkah (i.e., does not perform the Umrah tawaf) and proceeds to stand at Arafat owes a dam (blood sacrifice) for abandoning the Umrah. The reason is that once he stands at Arafat, the Umrah becomes impossible because he would be building Umrah actions on Hajj actions, which is not how it is legislated. The text then discusses the number of dams due: according to Imam Abu Hanifah, in the case of a qarin who is unable to afford the hady and shaves before sacrificing, three dams may be due in some contexts, but here only two (one for qiran and one for shaving). The passage resolves apparent contradictions with other parts of al-Hidayah and other works, explaining that differences arise based on whether the person is a transgressor or excused due to inability. Finally, it mentions a transmission from Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi confirming that if the three days are not fasted, fasting is invalid afterward. The passage emphasizes that the ruling applies specifically when no tawaf has been performed; if four or more circuits of tawaf were done before Arafat, it may be valid.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qarin): One who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.
طواف العمرة (tawaf al-umrah): The circumambulation of the Kaaba that is a pillar (rukn) of Umrah.
الوقوف بعرفة (al-wuquf bi 'Arafah): Standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the greatest pillar of Hajj.
الدم (al-dam): The blood sacrifice due as compensation for abandoning or violating a ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a qarin owe a dam if he stands at Arafat without having performed Umrah tawaf?
A) Because he missed the tawaf due to laziness
B) Because it becomes impossible to perform Umrah properly after standing at Arafat
C) Because he didn't enter Makkah
D) Because he combined both ihrams incorrectly

Key Takeaway
A qarin who stands at Arafat without having performed at least four circuits of Umrah tawaf owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah.

Ruling on a Qarin Who Fails to Fast Before Nahr
Expansion of a matn ruling with proof and reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Qarin misses fasting before the Day of Nahr and explain why blood becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Fasting after Nahr is invalid; blood is the only option.

This passage expands on a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses a specific scenario: a pilgrim performing Hajj as a Qarin who fails to fast the three days before the Day of Nahr. The commentator clarifies that fasting after that day is invalid, and blood becomes mandatory. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that fasting is a substitute (badal) for the blood sacrifice, and substitutes are only valid when prescribed by divine law within a specific time frame. The passage also cites a narration from Ibn Umar to support the obligation of blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the Qarin who fails to fast three days before the Day of Nahr. The ruling: fasting is invalid after Nahr, and blood (dam) becomes obligatory.
The ruling is mandatory (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a narration from Ibn Umar (a Companion) who ordered a sheep to be slaughtered in a similar case. In Hanafi usul, the action of a Companion can be a proof.
The dalil is a Qawl Sahabi, which is considered a proof in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the narration prove the ruling? The Companion's order to slaughter indicates that blood is the required act when fasting is missed. The passage also reasons that fasting is a substitute (badal) and a substitute is only valid within the time specified by the text; after that time, the original obligation (blood) reverts.
The reasoning is based on the nature of a badal (substitute).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that if one cannot afford the sacrificial animal, he exits ihram and owes two bloods: one for Tamattu' and one for exiting before sacrifice. This reflects a difference within the Hanafi school? Actually, it's a sub-ruling. The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may allow fasting after Nahr with compensation.
The Hanafi position is clear: fasting after Nahr is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمكة فإن لم يصم إلى يوم النحر تعين الدم وإن لم يدخل مكة ووقف بعرفة فعليه دم قوله : (فإن لم يصم إلى يوم النحر تعين الدم أي إن لم يصم الثلاثة حتى دخل يوم النحر لم يجزه الصوم أصلاً وصار الدم متعيناً لأن الصوم بدل وإلا بدال لا تنصب إلا شرعاً والنص خصه بوقت الحج وجواز الدم على الأصل، وعن ابن عمر أنه أمر في مثله بذبح الشاة فلو لم يقدر على الهدي تحلل وعليه دمان دم التمتع ودم التحلل قبل الهدي. كذا في الهداية هنا.
In Makkah: if he does not fast until the Day of Nahr, the blood becomes obligatory. And if he does not enter Makkah and stands at Arafah, upon him is blood. His saying: (if he does not fast until the Day of Nahr the blood becomes obligatory) meaning if he did not fast the three days until the Day of Nahr entered, fasting does not suffice him at all and blood becomes obligatory because fasting is a substitute, and a substitute is not established except by divine law, and the text specifies it for the time of Hajj, and blood is permissible on the basis of the original. And from Ibn Umar that he ordered in a similar case the slaughter of a sheep, so if he could not find a sacrificial animal, he would exit Ihram and upon him are two bloods: blood of Tamattu' and blood of exiting Ihram before the sacrificial animal. Thus in Al-Hidayah here.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn ruling. The commentator explains that if a Qarin fails to fast three days before the Day of Nahr, fasting is no longer valid and blood becomes mandatory. The reasoning (talil) is that fasting is a substitute (badal) for the blood sacrifice, and a substitute can only be established by divine law (shar'). The text (Quran or Sunnah) specifically confines the fasting to the time of Hajj, so after that time, the original obligation (blood) reverts. A narration from Ibn Umar is cited: he ordered a sheep to be slaughtered in a similar case, and if one cannot find a sacrificial animal, he exits ihram and owes two bloods: one for Tamattu' and one for exiting before sacrifice. This is from Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute – here, fasting is a substitute for the blood sacrifice.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice obligatory for certain violations in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He may do nothing.

Key Takeaway
Fasting is a time-bound substitute; if missed before Nahr, blood becomes wajib.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Bloods for a Qarin Who Shaves Before Sacrificing
Resolution of an intra-Hanafi dispute through contextual analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the number of bloods required for a Qarin who shaves before sacrificing, and explain the resolution of the apparent contradiction in Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
A Qarin who shaves before sacrificing owes two bloods only if he was able to sacrifice; if unable, only one.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the required bloods for a Qarin who shaves his head before slaughtering the sacrificial animal. Abu Hanifa and his two companions disagree on whether one or two bloods are due. The commentator defends the author of Al-Hidayah against accusations of inconsistency by highlighting the key factor of ability versus inability to sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a Qarin shaving his head before slaughtering the sacrificial animal. Determine what the point of disagreement is: the number of bloods required.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, two bloods are due: one for shaving at an improper time (before slaughter) and one for delaying the slaughter after shaving.
The proper time for shaving is after slaughter.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, only one blood is required, which is for shaving at the wrong time.
They consider delaying the slaughter as not a separate violation.
4
Understand the commentator's defense of consistency
The commentator argues that the apparent contradiction in Al-Hidayah is resolved by context: in Bab al-Qiran, the Qarin was unable to sacrifice, so no blood for delay; in Bab al-Jinayat, he was able, so two bloods apply.
5
Apply the distinction
Identify the practical consequence: only one blood is owed when the Qarin cannot sacrifice (e.g., due to lack of means), but two when he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال فيما يأتي في آخر الجنايات : فإن حلق القارن قبل أن يذبح فعليه دمان عند أبي حنيفة دم بالحلق في غير أوانه لأن أوانه بعد الذبح ودم بتأخير الذبح عن الحلق. وعندهما يجب عليه دم واحد وهو الأول فنسبه صاحب غاية البيان إلى التخليط لكونه جعل أحد الدمين هنا دم الشكر والآخر دم الجناية وهو صواب وفيما يأتي أثبت عند أبي حنيفة دمين آخرين سوى دم الشكر ونسبه في فتح القدير أيضاً في باب الجنايات إلى السهو وليس كما قالا بل كلامه صواب في الموضعين فهنا لما لم يكن جانياً بالتأخير لأنه لعجزه لم يلزمه لأجله دم ولزمه دم للحلق في غير أوانه، وفي باب الجنايات لما كان جانياً بحلقه قبل الذبح لزمه دمان كما قرره ولم يذكر دم الشكر لأنه قدمه في باب القران وليس الكلام إلا في الجناية وسيأتي تمامه هناك بأزيد من هذا إن شاء الله تعالى
And he said later in the end of the chapter on violations: If the Qarin shaves before he slaughters, then upon him are two bloods according to Abu Hanifa: a blood for shaving at an improper time because its proper time is after slaughter, and a blood for delaying the slaughter from the shaving. According to the two companions, only one blood is required, and it is the first. So the author of Ghayat al-Bayan attributed it to confusion because he made one of the two bloods here the blood of gratitude and the other the blood of violation, and that is correct. And later he established for Abu Hanifa two other bloods besides the blood of gratitude, and the author of Fath al-Qadir also attributed it in the chapter on violations to forgetfulness, but it is not as they said; rather his speech is correct in both places. For here, since he was not a violator by delaying because of his inability, no blood was required for that, and a blood was required for shaving at an improper time. And in the chapter on violations, since he was a violator by shaving before slaughter, two bloods were required as he stated. And he did not mention the blood of gratitude because he had already presented it in the chapter on Qiran, and the discussion is only about violations. And its completion will come there with more than this, God willing.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the number of bloods (dams) required for a Qarin who shaves before sacrificing. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, two bloods are due: one for shaving before its proper time and one for delaying the sacrifice after shaving. However, according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), only one blood is due, which is the first. The commentator then defends the author of Al-Hidayah against criticisms from the authors of Ghayat al-Bayan and Fath al-Qadir, who claimed inconsistency. The defense is that in the earlier discussion (in Bab al-Qiran), the person was unable to sacrifice, so he was not a violator for delaying; thus only one blood was needed for shaving. In the later discussion (in Bab al-Jinayat), the person was able but shaved early, so two bloods were due. The blood of gratitude (dam al-shukr) is not mentioned in the violations chapter because it had already been discussed.

Key Terms
دم الشكر (dam al-shukr): Blood of gratitude for successfully performing Qiran.
دم الجناية (dam al-jinayah): Blood for a violation (jinayah) of ihram, such as shaving before the proper time.
قارن (qarin): A person performing Hajj Qiran, combining Umrah and Hajj in one ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's resolution, in which situation does a Qarin owe two bloods after shaving before sacrificing?
A) When he is unable to sacrifice
B) When he is able to sacrifice
C) In all cases
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The number of bloods for a Qarin who shaves before sacrificing depends on whether he is able or unable to sacrifice; Abu Hanifa requires two when able, while the Sahibayn require one regardless.
