Abandonment of Umrah in Qiran: Standing Triggers Dam and Qada
Explains the obligation of blood and qada for abandoning Umrah by standing at Arafah without performing it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Qarin who stands at Arafah without performing Umrah, identify the conditions for rafd, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of rafd.

Core Idea
Standing at Arafah without Umrah makes one a rafid, obligating dam and qada — the relied-upon view is that rafd occurs upon standing, not merely heading.

Hajj al-Qiran requires the pilgrim to perform both Umrah and Hajj in one ihram, with Umrah coming first. But what if the pilgrim proceeds directly to Arafah without completing the Umrah rituals? This lesson explains the Hanafi position: he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of Umrah, must sacrifice a blood, and later make up the Umrah. We also explore an important intra-madhhab dispute about the exact moment rafd occurs — upon heading to Arafah or upon standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The Qarin stands at Arafah without having performed tawaf for Umrah. The ruling: dam (blood) is wajib and qada (makeup) of Umrah is wajib.
The blood is not the blood of Qiran; it is a separate dam for abandoning Umrah.
2
Understand the definition of rafd
Rafd occurs when the Qarin stands at Arafah without having performed at least four circuits (the rukn) of tawaf for Umrah. If he performed four or more, he does not become rafid; he completes the remaining wajibat later.
Any tawaf performed, even if intended for Hajj, is redirected to Umrah if done in the Umrah ihram state.
3
Locate the proof: istihsan vs. qiyas
The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is based on istihsan: standing, not heading, triggers rafd. The qiyas position (narration of Hasan and Tahawi) says heading does.
The key distinction: heading to Arafah is not prohibited in Qiran as it is in the Friday prayer analogy.
4
Analyze the dispute and its practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a Qarin heads to Arafah but returns before standing, performs Umrah, then later stands — according to the apparent narration he is a Qarin; according to the qiyas narration he is rafid and must offer two dams (one for abandonment, one for Qiran).
This scenario is the critical test case.
5
Apply the conditions for rafd
The conditions: no prior tawaf for Umrah (or less than four circuits), and standing at Arafah (after its time). Intention is irrelevant — rafd occurs whether he intended to abandon or not.
The obligation of qada is because entering ihram makes Umrah binding like a vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن لم يدخل مكة ووقف بعرفة فعليه دم لرفض العمرة وقضاؤها يعني إن لم يأت القارن بالعمرة حتى أتى بالوقوف فعليه دم لترك العمرة لأنه تعذر عليه أداؤها لأنه يصير بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج، وذلك خلاف المشروع فعدم دخول مكة كناية عن عدم طواف العمرة لأن الدخول وعدمه سواء إذا لم يطف لها والمراد أكثر أشواطه حتى لو طاف لها أربعة أشواط ثم وقف بعرفة فإنه لا يصير رافضاً لها إذ قد أتى بركنها ولم يبق إلا واجباتها من الأقل والسعي ويأتي بها يوم النحر وهو قارن على حاله بخلاف ما إذا طاف الأقل ثم وقف فإنه كالعدم فيصير رافضاً . والمراد بعدم الطواف للعمرة عدم الطواف أصلاً فإنه لو طاف طوافاً ما ولو قصد به طواف القدوم للحج فإنه ينصرف إلى طواف العمرة ولم يكن رافضاً لها بالوقوف لأن الأصل أن المأتي به من جنس ما هو متلبس به في وقت يصلح له ينصرف إلى ما هو متلبس به، وعن هذا قلنا لو طاف طاف وسعى للحج ثم . وسعى للعمرة كان الأول لها والثاني له ولا شيء عليه كمن سجد بعد الركوع ينوي سجدة تلاوة انصرف إلى سجدة الصلاة ولم يقيد الوقوف بعرفة بكونه بعد الزوال كما وقع في كافي الحاكم لأنه لا حاجة إليه لأن الوقوف قبل وقته لا اعتبار به، وقيد بالوقوف لأنه لا يكون رافضاً لها بمجرد التوجه إلى عرفات هو الصحيح. والفرق بينه وبين مصلي الظهر يوم الجمعة إذا توجه إليها أن الأمر هناك بالتوجه متوجه بعد أداء الظهر، والتوجه في القران والتمتع منهي عنه قبل أداء العمرة فافترقا وأطلق في رفضها فشمل ما إذا قصده أو لا، وأشار به إلى سقوط دم القرآن عنه لعدمه وإنما وجب دم لرفضها لأن كل من تحلل بغير طواف يجب عليه دم كالمحصر ووجب قضاؤها لأن الشروع ملزم كالنذر والله أعلم قوله : (هو الصحيح) صححه صاحب الهداية والكافي وهو ظاهر الرواية وهو الاستحسان، وفي رواية الحسن والطحاوي عن أبي حنيفة يصير رافضاً بمجرد التوجه إلى عرفات وهو القياس، وفي الفتح والصحيح ظاهر الرواية. أقول : ويمكن الجمع بأن يكون الرفض بالتوجه والارتفاض بالوقوف وثمرة الخلاف فيما إذا توجه إلى عرفة ثم بدا له فرجع عن الطريق قبل الوقوف بعرفة وطاف لعمرته وسعى لها ثم وقف بعرفة هل يكون قارناً؟ جواب ظاهر الرواية يكون قارناً. كذا في شرح اللباب، وكان ينبغي أن يذكر الجمع بعد ذكر ثمرة الخلاف تأمل .
His saying: (And if he does not enter Makkah and stands at Arafah, then upon him is blood for abandoning the Umrah and its makeup) meaning if the Qarin did not perform the Umrah until he performed the standing, then upon him is blood for leaving the Umrah because its performance became impossible for him, since he becomes one who builds the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj, and that is contrary to the legislated. So not entering Makkah is a metaphor for not performing the tawaf of Umrah, because entering and not entering are the same if he does not perform tawaf for it. And what is meant is most of its circuits, such that if he performed four circuits for it and then stood at Arafah, he does not become an abandoner of it, since he has performed its pillar and nothing remains but its obligatory parts like the less and the sa'y, and he performs them on the Day of Nahr and he remains a Qarin as he was. Unlike if he performed less than four and then stood, then it is like nothing and he becomes an abandoner. And what is meant by not performing tawaf for Umrah is not performing it at all, because if he performed any tawaf, even if he intended it as tawaf of arrival for Hajj, it is redirected to the tawaf of Umrah and he is not an abandoner by standing, because the principle is that what is performed of the same type as what one is engaged in at a time suitable for it is redirected to what he is engaged in. And for this reason we said: if he performed tawaf and sa'y for Hajj and then performed sa'y for Umrah, the first is for Umrah and the second for Hajj and nothing is upon him, like one who prostrates after bowing intending a prostration of recitation, it is redirected to the prostration of prayer. And the standing at Arafah is not restricted to after noon as occurred in Kafi al-Hakim, because there is no need for it, since standing before its time is not considered. And it is restricted to standing because he does not become an abandoner merely by heading to Arafat; that is the correct view. And the difference between him and one who prays Zuhr on Friday when he heads to it is that the command there to head to it is after performing Zuhr, while heading in Qiran and Tamattu' is prohibited before performing Umrah, so they differ. And he made it absolute in his abandonment, so it includes whether he intended it or not. And he indicated by it the falling away of the blood of Qiran from him due to its non-existence, and only blood is obligatory for his abandonment, because everyone who ends Ihram without tawaf must offer blood, like the muhsar. And it is necessary to make it up because entering makes it binding like a vow. And God knows best. His saying: (It is the correct view) authenticated by the author of Al-Hidayah and Al-Kafi, and it is the apparent narration and it is istihsan. And in the narration of Hasan and Tahawi from Abu Hanifa, he becomes an abandoner merely by heading to Arafat, and that is qiyas. And in Fath al-Qadir, the correct is the apparent narration. I say: It is possible to reconcile by saying that abandonment occurs by heading and the state of being an abandoner by standing, and the fruit of the difference appears when he heads to Arafa then changes his mind and returns before standing at Arafah, performs tawaf for his Umrah and sa'y for it, then stands at Arafah: is he a Qarin? The answer according to the apparent narration is that he is a Qarin. Thus in Sharh al-Lubab. It would have been better to mention the reconciliation after mentioning the fruit of the difference; reflect.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This long passage explains the ruling for a Qarin who does not perform the Umrah rituals before standing at Arafah. The Hanafi position is that if he stands at Arafah without having done any tawaf for Umrah, he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of the Umrah, and must offer a blood sacrifice (dam) and later make up the Umrah (qada). The reason is that he has made the actions of Umrah dependent on Hajj, which is against the prescribed order. The text clarifies what counts as 'not performing tawaf': if he performed four or more circuits of tawaf for Umrah (the pillar), then standing at Arafah does not make him rafid; he can complete the remaining wajibat later. But if he performed less than four, it is as if he did nothing and he becomes rafid. Also, any tawaf performed during the state of ihram for Umrah is considered for Umrah, even if intended for Hajj. The ruling is that the moment of becoming rafid is upon standing at Arafah, not merely heading towards it, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) which is istihsan. However, a narration from Hasan and Tahawi from Abu Hanifa says that merely heading to Arafah makes one rafid, based on qiyas. The commentator reconciles by saying that abandonment occurs upon heading, but the actual state of being rafid occurs upon standing, and the practical difference is in a scenario where one heads towards Arafah but turns back before standing, performs Umrah, then later stands—according to the apparent narration, he remains a Qarin. The passage also analogizes to the muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) who must offer blood. Thus, the blood here is not the blood of Qiran but a blood for abandoning the Umrah.

Key Terms
رفض العمرة (rafd al-umrah): Abandonment of Umrah by the Qarin when he proceeds to Arafah without performing its tawaf and sa'y.
قضاء العمرة (qada' al-umrah): The obligation to perform a makeup Umrah after having abandoned it in the current Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what constitutes rafd (abandonment of Umrah) for a Qarin?
A) Heading towards Arafah
B) Standing at Arafah without having performed at least four circuits of Umrah tawaf
C) Standing at Arafah without having performed any tawaf at all
D) Intending to skip Umrah

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who stands at Arafah without having performed the rukn of Umrah tawaf (four circuits) becomes rafid, obligating a blood sacrifice and a makeup Umrah.

Definition and Ruling of Tamattu' in Hajj
Defines Tamattu' and states the ruling for the mutamatti' regarding the dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tamattu' and state the wajib ruling for the mutamatti' regarding the dam and its fasting alternative.

Core Idea
Tamattu' combines Umrah and Hajj in one journey; a sacrifice (dam) is wajib, but fasting substitutes when unable.

This lesson clarifies what tamattu' means in both language and Islamic law, and then explains the obligatory sacrifice (dam al-tamattu') that a mutamatti' must offer. Understanding this definition and ruling is essential for every pilgrim performing Hajj tamattu', as it affects their obligations during the pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic and legal definitions
Note that tamattu' linguistically means 'enjoyment' and legally refers to performing Umrah during the Hajj months, then Hajj in the same year, with a break of ihram in between.
The definition includes the sequence: ihram for Umrah from miqat, tawaf, sa'y, halq or taqsir, then ihram for Hajj.
2
Identify the wajib ruling for the mutamatti'
The mutamatti' must offer a dam (blood sacrifice) as thanks for the convenience of combining the two pilgrimages. This is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
The dam is not a pillar but a wajib; omitting it without excuse incurs sin.
3
Learn the substitute ruling if unable to find a sacrificial animal
If the pilgrim cannot find or afford a dam, they must fast three days during the Hajj period and seven days after returning home.
The fasting is a direct replacement for the dam; one does not owe both.
4
Distinguish tamattu' from other types of Hajj
Tamattu' differs from ifrad (Hajj only) and qiran (combined Umrah and Hajj with one ihram). In tamattu', there is a full break between Umrah and Hajj.
The mutamatti' is required to be non-resident of Makkah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of Tamattu'. He delayed it after Qiran because it is after it in rank, as he presented it. It is linguistically from 'mataa' or 'mut'a', and it is that one enters into ihram for Umrah from the miqat, performs tawaf for it, sa'y, shaves or shortens, and then becomes halal, then he raises his voice for Hajj from the same year or from his place. It is one type of tamattu'. And in the divine law, it is blood. So if he does not find a sacrificial animal, he becomes halal and upon him is the blood of Tamattu'. And there is no blood upon him for his becoming halal it is said that he should slaughter, and no blood upon him for leaving the fast. End.

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Tamattu' in Hajj. It defines Tamattu' linguistically and legally. Legally, a mutamatti' performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, then after completing it, he begins Hajj in the same year. The definition includes the actions: ihram from the miqat, tawaf, sa'y, shaving or shortening, then resolving ihram, and later ihram for Hajj. The ruling: the mutamatti' must offer a blood sacrifice (dam) for combining Umrah and Hajj. If he cannot find a sacrificial animal, he must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning. The text mentions that there is no additional blood for becoming halal (i.e., for the Umrah itself) nor for leaving the fast if he could not fast? The phrase 'ولا دم عليه لترك الصوم' may be ambiguous; the intended meaning is that if one omits the fast (due to inability?), no blood is due? However, the standard ruling is that if one cannot fast, he must offer blood. This passage is a brief summary.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Tamattu', i.e., performs Umrah first in the Hajj months then Hajj in the same year.
دم المتعة (dam al-tamattu'): Blood sacrifice obligatory for the mutamatti' in thanks for the ability to combine Umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Definition and Rulings of Tamattu' and Rafd al-'Umrah
Commentary defining tamattu' and ruling on rafd al-'umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tamattu', identify the conditions for a valid tamattu', and explain when a person becomes a rafid (rejecter) of the 'umrah.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is 'umrah then hajj in one journey; rafd occurs only by standing at 'Arafat with incomplete tawaf.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi commentary on tamattu'—the combined performance of 'umrah and hajj in one journey with a break. We will define tamattu', examine its conditions (like performing most of the 'umrah tawaf in hajj months), and then focus on a key ruling: when does a pilgrim become a 'rafid' (rejecter) of the 'umrah? The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies an intra-Hanafi dispute and establishes the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of tamattu'
Find the sentence beginning with 'هو أن يحرم' and note the sequence: ihram for 'umrah from miqat, tawaf, sa'y, shaving, then ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah.
The definition includes both actions and a spatial restriction ('from miqat').
2
Identify the conditions for a valid tamattu'
The commentator points out that most of the 'umrah tawaf must occur in hajj months, and that ilmaam (returning home) can invalidate tamattu' if valid. List these conditions.
Note the distinction between conditions for tamattu' itself and conditions for avoiding the need for dam.
3
Understand the concept of rafd (rejecting the 'umrah)
Rafd occurs when a pilgrim performs hajj actions (standing at 'Arafat) before completing the 'umrah tawaf. The text specifies that standing, not merely heading, triggers rafd.
The ḥukm of rafd: the pilgrim becomes a qārin (if tawaf incomplete) or must offer dam and make up the 'umrah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
One narration (from Hasan and al-Ṭaḥāwī) says mere heading to 'Arafat constitutes rafd. The relied-upon view (ẓāhir al-riwāya) requires actual standing. Compare the proofs.
The Ḥanafī response to the qiyās with Friday prayer shows the use of istiḥsān.

أهله بعد العمرة ولا يكون العود إلى العمرة مستحقاً عليه، وعن هذا قلنا لا تمتع لأهل مكة وأهل المواقيت ا هـ. وهذا ما ذكره المؤلف، والظاهر أن التفسير الأول إنما هو في حق الآفاقي، والثاني أعم منه يدلك على The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Tamattu', concerning the rejection of 'umrah and its performance. It is that one enters ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, performs tawaf for it, sa'y, shaves or shortens hair, and becomes free from it, and stops the talbiyah at the beginning of tawaf, then enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah from the Haram and performs hajj. So his statement 'from the miqat' is to exclude Mecca: there is no tamattu' or qiran for its inhabitants, not to exclude passing by his family or other things as we explained in qiran. He did not restrict its ihram to the months of hajj because it is not a condition, but performing most of its tawaf during them is a condition. So if one performed the lesser part of tawaf in Ramadan, for example, then completed the rest in Shawwal, then performed hajj in that year, he is mutamatti'. He did not restrict tawaf to this because it will be clarified in this chapter. He mentioned shaving to indicate completion of the actions of 'umrah, not because it is a condition for tamattu', because he has a choice between it and remaining in ihram until he enters ihram for hajj. It is not objected that the mutamatti' who drives hady cannot shave for 'umrah, for if he shaves, he owes dam because driving hady prevents him from tahallul contrary to the original. His statement 'then enters ihram for hajj' indicates that his ihram is after qiran. He did not restrict hajj to that year because it is known: the meaning of tamattu' is to perform the two rites in one journey with ease, and it is not required that it be in the year of ihram for 'umrah, but rather the year of its performance. So if one entered ihram for 'umrah in Ramadan and remained in ihram until Shawwal of the next year, then performed tawaf for his 'umrah in that month, then performed hajj in that same year, he is mutamatti'. This is unlike someone who was obligated to exit from hajj through 'umrah, like one who missed hajj and delayed it to the next year, then exited through 'umrah in Shawwal and performed hajj that same year; he is not mutamatti', because he performed these actions for exit from hajj, not from 'umrah, so these actions are not considered 'umrah, so he is not mutamatti'. His statement 'day of Tarwiyah' indicates permissibility, otherwise it is better before it for hastening to good. His statement 'from the Haram' indicates the spatial restriction for the people of Mecca. He did not restrict with absence of ilmaam (staying with family) between them—a valid ilmaam—as will be clarified shortly. The summary: if he stays with his family between them in a valid ilmaam, his tamattu' is invalidated; otherwise not. The valid ilmaam is that the return not be obligatory upon him. It is said 'he stayed with his family' according to what is suitable, so it includes the Meccan. His statement: (and the valid of it, i.e. ilmaam). In al-'Inayah: it is said 'he stayed with his family' if he settles, and it is of two types: valid and invalid. The first is settling in his homeland without remaining in the state of ihram. This only occurs for the mutamatti' who did not drive hady. The second is the opposite, and it occurs for one who drove hady. In al-Mi'raj after what preceded, and in al-Muhit: the valid ilmaam is that he returns to his family after 'umrah and the return to 'umrah is not obligatory upon him. For this reason we say: there is no tamattu' for the people of Mecca and the people of the miqat. This is what the author mentioned. The apparent is that the first interpretation concerns the afaqi, and the second is more general. This is indicated by what is in al-Hidayah: if he drove hady, his ilmaam is not valid, unlike the Meccan who went to Kufa and entered ihram for 'umrah and drove hady; he is not mutamatti' because the return there is not obligatory, so his ilmaam with his family is valid. In al-'Inayah: because the return meant is from the homeland to the Haram or to Mecca, and that is not here.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the definition of tamattu' and its related rulings, particularly the issue of rejecting (rafd) the 'umrah. The commentator begins by presenting the definition of tamattu' as per the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: entering ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, performing tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or shortening, then exiting ihram, later entering ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah from the Haram. He explains that the phrase 'from the miqat' excludes the people of Mecca, who cannot perform tamattu' or qiran. The ihram for 'umrah is not restricted to the months of hajj, but most of its tawaf must occur during those months. The commentator then addresses a key issue: if a mutamatti' performs part of the 'umrah tawaf, then goes to 'Arafat and stands there before completing the tawaf, he becomes a rafid (rejecter) of the 'umrah and must offer a dam and make up the 'umrah later. However, if he has completed the essential parts of tawaf (four circuits according to the Hanafi view), his going to 'Arafat does not make him a rafid; he remains a qarin. The text then discusses the concept of ilmaam (staying with family) between 'umrah and hajj: a valid ilmaam, where one returns to his homeland without remaining in ihram, invalidates tamattu'. For those who drive hady, ilmaam is not valid. The passage also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute: the zahir al-riwaya holds that only actual standing at 'Arafat constitutes rafd, not merely heading towards it, while a narration from Hasan and Tahawi states that mere heading suffices. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the zahir al-riwaya.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'umrah in the months of hajj and then performing hajj in the same year, with a break in between (tahallul).
رفض (rafd): Rejecting or abandoning the 'umrah by performing hajj actions before completing the 'umrah, necessitating dam and qada'.
إلمام (ilmaam): Returning to one's hometown and staying there without remaining in ihram; if valid, it breaks tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he merely intends to go to 'Arafat.
B) When he heads towards 'Arafat.
C) When he stands at 'Arafat after performing less than four circuits of 'umrah tawaf.
D) When he completes the 'umrah tawaf and then goes to 'Arafat.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires completing the 'umrah with most of its tawaf in hajj months; rejecting the 'umrah occurs only by standing at 'Arafat after less than four tawaf circuits.

Definition of Tamattu' and Its Required Acts
Defines tamattu' with its acts and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of tamattu' and identify each of its required acts (arkan) and conditions (shurut) as derived from the text.

Core Idea
Tamattu' is performing 'umrah first then Hajj in the same year with a break (tahlil) between them.

This lesson unpacks the precise definition of tamattu' as given in Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary in Al-Bahr al-Raiq. Understanding its constituent acts and conditions is essential for both performing Hajj correctly for those undertaking tamattu', and for distinguishing it from other types of Hajj like ifrad and qiran. The passage clarifies subtle conditions such as the timing of tawaf and the prohibition on returning home (ilmaam sahih).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being defined
Recognize that the passage defines tamattu', a type of Hajj where 'umrah is performed first, then Hajj later in the same year, with a release from ihram in between.
Contrast with ifrad (Hajj only) and qiran ('umrah and Hajj combined in one ihram).
2
List the required sequential acts (arkan)
Extract the sequence from the definition: ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, tawaf, sa'y, shaving or shortening (halq/taqsir), cutting the talbiyah at the start of tawaf, then ihram for Hajj from the Haram on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah).
The text emphasizes that cutting talbiyah occurs at the beginning of tawaf of 'umrah.
3
Determine the conditions (shurut) for validity
Identify conditions: the pilgrim must be from outside Makkah (not a Makkan), most of the 'umrah tawaf must be performed during the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, Dhul Hijjah), and they must not have returned to their family in a valid return (ilmaam sahih) between 'umrah and Hajj.
The condition about tawaf timing is subtle: the start of 'umrah outside Hajj months is allowed, as long as most tawaf falls within them.
4
Note the optional elements (sunan) and exceptions
Performing the entire 'umrah within the months of Hajj is recommended but not required. An exception is the one who drives a hadiy (sacrificial animal) – they are not permitted to shave for 'umrah; doing so would incur a dam.
5
Understand the effect of invalid return (ilmaam)
The passage notes that a valid return to one's family after completing 'umrah invalidates tamattu'. This will be explained further in the text.
This condition ensures that the pilgrim remains in a state of connection to the Hajj journey.

Source Text

أفعالها فخرج الانتفاع أو النفع وفي الشريعة ما ذكره بقوله : (وهو) أن يحرم بعمرة من الميقات فيطوف لها ويسعى ويحلق أو يقصر وقد حل منها ويقطع التلبية بأول الطواف ثم يحرم بالحج يوم التروية من الحرم ويحج) فقوله من الميقات للاحتراز عن مكة فإنه ليس لأهلها تمتع ولا قرآن لا للاحتراز عن دوبرة أهله أو غيرها كما بيناه في القرآن، ولم يقيد إحرامها بأشهر الحج لأنه ليس بشرط لكن أداء أكثر طوافها فيها شرط، فلو طاف الأقل في رمضان مثلاً ثم طاف الباقي في شوال ثم حج من عامة كان متمتعاً. وإنما لم يقيد الطواف به لما يصرح به في هذا الباب. وإنما ذكر الحلق لبيان تمام أفعال العمرة لا لأنه شرط في التمتع لأنه مخير بينه وبين بقائه محرماً بها إلى أن يدخل إحرام الحج ولا يرد عليه المتمتع الذي ساق الهدي فإنه لا يجوز له الحلق للعمرة حتى لو حلق لها لزمه دم لأن سوق الهدي عارض منعه من التحلل على خلاف الأصل. وفي قوله ثم يحرم بالحج دلالة على تراخي إحرامه عن القرآن، ولم يقيد الحج بأن يكون من عامه للعلم به لأن معنى التمتع الترفق بأداء النسكين في سفرة واحدة ولا يشترط أن يكون من عام الإحرام العمرة بل من عام فعلها حتى لو أحرم بعمرة في رمضان وأقام على إحرامه إلى شوال من العام القابل ثم طاف لعمرته من القابل ثم حج من عامه ذلك كان متمتعاً بخلاف من وجب عليه أن يتحلل من الحج بعمرة كفائت الحج فأخر إلى قابل فتحلل بها في شوال وحج من عامه ذلك لا يكون متمتعاً لأنه ما أتى بأفعالها عن إحرام عمرة بل للتحلل عن إحرام الحج فلم تقع هذه الأفعال معتداً بها عن العمرة فلم يكن متمتعاً. وقوله يوم التروية بيان للجواز وإلا فالأفضل أن يكون قبله للمسارعة إلى الخير، وقوله من الحرم بيان للميقات المكاني لأهل مكة ولم يقيد بعدم الإلمام بأهله فيما بينهما إلماماً صحيحاً لما يصرح به قريباً.
Its actions, so excluded is 'intifa'' or 'naf' (linguistic meanings), and in Shari'ah is what he mentioned by his saying: (And it) is that he enters ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, then performs tawaf for it, and sa'y, and shaves or shortens, and he has become free from it, and he cuts the talbiyah at the beginning of the tawaf, then he enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah from the Haram and performs Hajj. His saying 'from the miqat' is to exclude Makkah, for its residents have no tamattu' or qiran, not to exclude the area of his family or others as we explained in qiran. He did not restrict its ihram to the months of Hajj because it is not a condition, but performing most of its tawaf in them is a condition. So if he performed the lesser part of tawaf in Ramadan, for example, then performed the remainder in Shawwal, then performed Hajj that same year, he would be a mutamatti'. He only did not restrict tawaf to it because of what will be stated in this chapter. He only mentioned shaving to indicate the completion of the acts of 'umrah, not because it is a condition for tamattu', because he is given a choice between it and remaining in ihram for it until he enters ihram for Hajj. It is not objected to regarding the mutamatti' who drove the hadiy, for he is not allowed to shave for 'umrah, such that if he shaved for it he would be liable for a dam, because the driving of the hadiy is an obstacle preventing him from tahlil contrary to the principle. In his saying 'then he enters ihram for Hajj' is an indication of the tardiness of his ihram from qiran. He did not restrict Hajj to being in the same year, because of the knowledge that the meaning of tamattu' is comfort in performing the two rites in one journey, and it is not a condition that it be from the year of the ihram of 'umrah, but rather from the year of its performance. So even if he entered ihram for 'umrah in Ramadan and remained in his ihram until Shawwal of the following year, then performed tawaf for his 'umrah in the following year, then performed Hajj in that same year, he would be a mutamatti', contrary to one who was obligated to free himself from Hajj by an 'umrah, like one who missed Hajj, so he delayed it to the following year and freed himself by it in Shawwal and performed Hajj in that same year: he is not a mutamatti' because he performed its acts not from the ihram of 'umrah but to free himself from the ihram of Hajj, so these acts are not considered valid as 'umrah, so he is not a mutamatti'. His saying 'day of Tarwiyah' is an explanation of permissibility, otherwise it is better to be before it for hastening to good. His saying 'from the Haram' is an explanation of the spatial miqat for the people of Makkah, and he did not restrict it to not returning to his family between them in a valid return, because it will be stated shortly.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage is a definition of tamattu' (the legal type of Hajj performed by doing 'umrah first, then Hajj in the same year). The author, explaining the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, defines it as a sequence of acts: ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or trimming (halq or taqsir), then cutting the talbiyah at the start of tawaf, then entering ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) from the Haram, and performing Hajj. The commentary clarifies that the miqat is required for non-Makkans; Makkans do not have tamattu' or qiran. The 'umrah does not necessarily have to be in the months of Hajj, but most of its tawaf must be in those months for the tamattu' to be valid. If someone performs a partial tawaf in Ramadan and completes it in Shawwal, then performs Hajj the same year, they are mutamatti'. Shaving is mentioned only to indicate completion of 'umrah, not as a condition; one may choose to stay in ihram for 'umrah until beginning Hajj. However, if one has driven a sacrificial animal (hadiy), they may not shave for 'umrah; doing so would require a dam (penalty). The phrase 'then he enters ihram for Hajj' indicates that the ihram for Hajj occurs after completing 'umrah, distinct from qiran. The Hajj need not be in the same calendar year as the 'umrah; rather, it must be in the year the 'umrah is performed. For example, if one starts 'umrah in Ramadan of one year, completes it in Shawwal of the next year, and then performs Hajj in that latter year, they are mutamatti'. The exception is someone who missed Hajj and uses an 'umrah to exit the state of ihram: that does not count as tamattu'. The day of Tarwiyah is the permissibility time for ihram of Hajj, though earlier is better. The 'from the Haram' specifies the spatial miqat for Makkans. The passage ends by noting that returning to one's family between 'umrah and Hajj (ilmaam) is not mentioned as a condition here, but will be discussed shortly.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'umrah first in the months of Hajj, then Hajj in the same year, with tahlil between them.
إلمام (ilmaam): Returning to one's family between 'umrah and Hajj after tahlil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person enters ihram for 'umrah in Ramadan, performs part of the tawaf in Ramadan and completes it in Shawwal, then performs Hajj later that year. Is this valid tamattu' according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because most of the tawaf was in the months of Hajj.
B) No, because the 'umrah must start in the months of Hajj.
C) No, because the 'umrah was not from the miqat.
D) Yes, because he performed Hajj in the same year.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is defined by a specific sequence of acts with conditions; the most subtle condition is that most of the 'umrah tawaf must occur in the months of Hajj.

Ilmaam Sahih Invalidates Tamattu'
Ruling on ilmaam in tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of ilmaam sahih and ilmaam fasid, and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine whether a mutamatti' retains his status.

Core Idea
Ilmaam sahih voids tamattu'; ilmaam fasid does not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical condition in tamattu' Hajj: returning to one's family after 'umrah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a valid return that breaks the tamattu' sequence and an invalid return that preserves it. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in performing Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ilmaam
The text distinguishes ilmaam sahih (valid return) and ilmaam fasid (invalid return). Recognize that the ruling depends on this classification.
2
Define ilmaam sahih
Ilmaam sahih is returning to one's homeland without any remaining attribute of ihram and without being obligated to return to 'umrah (i.e., no hadiy driven).
This applies only to non-Makkans.
3
Define ilmaam fasid
Ilmaam fasid occurs when the return is done either while still in ihram or when the return is obligated (e.g., after driving a hadiy).
Driving hadiy makes the return obligatory, so ilmaam is not valid.
4
Apply the rule to scenarios
Use the definitions: if ilmaam sahih, tamattu' is invalidated; if ilmaam fasid, tamattu' remains valid.
Example: a mutamatti' who drives a hadiy and returns home still has valid tamattu'.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may not consider ilmaam as affecting tamattu'. This is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text

And its conclusion is that if he returned to his family between them with a valid return (ilmaaman sahihan), his tamattu' is invalidated, otherwise not. The valid one is that the return is not obligatory upon him. It is said 'he returned to his family' in a way that befits him, so it includes the Makkan. His saying: (and the valid one from it i.e. from ilmaam). He said in al-`Inayah: It is said 'alama bi-ahlihi' when he alights, and it is of two types: valid and invalid. The first is an expression of alighting in his homeland without the remaining of the attribute of ihram. This only occurs in the mutamatti' who did not drive the hadiy. The second is contrary to it, and it occurs in one who drove it. And he said in al-Mi'raj after what preceded: In al-Muhit: Al-ilmaam al-sahih is that he returns to his family after 'umrah and the return to 'umrah is not obligatory upon him. From this we say: There is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah and the people of the mawaqit. And this is what the author mentioned. It is apparent that the first interpretation is concerning the Aafaaqi, and the second is more general. This is indicated by what is in al-Hidayah: If he drove the hadiy, his ilmaam is not valid, unlike the Makkan if he went out to Kufa and entered ihram for 'umrah and drove the hadiy, where he is not a mutamatti' because the return there is not obligatory upon him, so his ilmaam with his family is valid. He said in al-`Inayah: Because what is meant by the return is from the homeland to the Haram or to Makkah, and it is not here. And he cuts the talbiyah at the beginning of tawaf, then he enters ihram for Hajj on the day of Tarwiyah from the Haram and performs Hajj and slaughters. If he descends and visits, it is ilmaam, i.e. occasionally. Thus in al-Mughrib. And he only cuts the talbiyah in it at its beginning because Abu Dawud authenticated from Ibn 'Abbas that he (peace be upon him) used to refrain from talbiyah in 'umrah when he touched the Black Stone. And he did not mention tawaf al-qudoom because there is no tawaf al-qudoom for the mutamatti'. Thus in al-Mubtagha. i.e. it is not sunnah in his case, unlike the qarin, because the mutamatti' at his arrival is only in ihram for 'umrah, and it has no tawaf al-qudoom nor tawaf al-sadr. The wisdom is that the mu'tamir is able to perform it when he arrives at the House, while the hajj is not able to perform tawaf al-ziyarah due to its time not being there, so tawaf al-qudoom is prescribed for him until its time comes. Tawaf is a great rukn in 'umrah, so it is not repeated in the sadr, just as standing in 'Arafat for Hajj is not repeated. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in his saying 'and he performs Hajj' is an indication that he does sa'y for Hajj and does ramal in his tawaf, and what he performed first is only for 'umrah. If the mutamatti' performed sa'y and ramal in his tawaf after his ihram for Hajj, he does not repeat them in tawaf al-ziyarah because they are not repeated. His saying: (and he slaughters, and if he is unable, it has passed) i.e. in the chapter on Qiran, for their rulings are one. His saying: (if he fasts three days in Shawwal and then performs 'umrah, it does not suffice for the three days) because the cause of its obligation is tamattu', and in this state he is not a mutamatti', so it is not permissible to perform it before its cause. His saying: (and it is valid if after he entered ihram for it before he performs tawaf) the three days means the fast after he entered ihram for 'umrah before tawaf is valid, because it is performance after the cause. Because its cause is tamattu' in the linguistic sense which is comfort, because it is based on tamattu' by text and the derivation of the word is the cause for the dependent. And 'umrah in the months of Hajj is the cause in it because it is that by which comfort is achieved which was prohibited in Jahiliyyah, and that is the meaning of tamattu'. Since he cannot exit its ihram without action, the ihram is taken as its substitute, so it is permissible after its ihram before completion of it. He restricted the three days because, regarding fasting the seven days, it is not permissible except after completion, even though the cause for both is one, because Allah separated between them, making the three in Hajj i.e. in its time, and the seven after completion. He restricted 'tawaf' meaning by existing (i.e. being in the Haram or Makkah) so the return is not conceivable. And if he drove the hadiy, he is not a mutamatti', so if he had not driven, it would be more appropriate. Thus he made the ilmaam of this Makkan valid even though he drove the hadiy. His saying: (and he did not mention tawaf al-qudoom etc.) He said in al-`Inayah: His saying: 'and if this mutamatti' after he entered ihram for Hajj performed tawaf al-qudoom and sa'y before going out to Mina, he does not do ramal in tawaf al-ziyarah nor sa'y after it, because he has done that once and there is no repetition.' In this speech is an indication that tawaf al-tahiyyah is prescribed for the mutamatti' where he considered his ramal and sa'y in it. He said in al-Fath: This is not without something, for the apparent meaning is that he intended that if he performed tawaf and then sa'y in place of sa'y, not that it is a condition for validity that it be considered tawaf al-tahiyyah. Rather the point is that sa'y must be based on tawaf in Shari'ah. So if we assume that the mutamatti' after ihram for Hajj performed a supererogatory tawaf and then performed sa'y after it, the sa'y of Hajj is dropped. Whoever restricts its validity to the tawaf being tawaf al-tahiyyah must provide evidence. Its conclusion is that the source of the misunderstanding is carrying the tawaf as tawaf al-qudoom, as stated, and nothing necessitates restricting it to that. His saying: (whether it is after he entered ihram)
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings related to tamattu', but our focus here is the condition of ilmaam (returning to family). The text states that if a person between 'umrah and Hajj returns to his home validly (ilmaaman sahihan), his tamattu' is invalidated. Valid ilmaam is defined as returning to his homeland without any remaining attribute of ihram, and such that he is not obliged to return to 'umrah. This applies only to those who did not drive a hadiy (sacrificial animal). If he drove a hadiy, his ilmaam is not valid, and thus tamattu' remains intact. The text cites a case from al-Hidayah: a Makkan who goes to Kufa, performs 'umrah with a hadiy, then returns to his family in Kufa – his ilmaam is sahih because the return is not obligatory, so he becomes a non-mutamatti'. The section also discusses cutting talbiyah, tawaf al-qudoom, sa'y, and fasting, which are separate topics but included in the continuous text. For the lesson, we extract the core rule: ilmaam sahih nullifies tamattu'.

Key Terms
إلمام صحيح (ilmaam sahih): Returning to one's home after 'umrah without the attribute of ihram and without being obligated to return to 'umrah.
إلمام فاسد (ilmaam fasid): Returning to one's home while still in ihram or when obligated to return to 'umrah (e.g., after driving hadiy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a mutamatti' who drives a hadiy and then returns to his family after 'umrah has an ilmaam that is considered:
A) Sahih (valid)
B) Fasid (invalid)
C) Not applicable
D) Invalid

Key Takeaway
Ilmaam sahih cancels tamattu'; ilmaam fasid does not.

intermediate

Tawaf al-Qudoom and Sa'y for the Mutamatti'
Clarifies absence of tawaf al-qudoom for mutamatti' and non-repetition of sa'y/ramal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a mutamatti' does not perform tawaf al-qudoom and explain that sa'y/ramal performed after entering ihram for Hajj are not repeated in tawaf al-ziyarah.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' has no sunnah tawaf al-qudoom because his 'umrah tawaf fulfills arrival; sa'y after ihram for Hajj is not repeated.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in Hajj fiqh: a mutamatti' (performing 'umrah first, then Hajj) does not have the sunnah tawaf al-qudoom that a qarin or ifrad hajj does. Furthermore, if he performs a voluntary tawaf with sa'y after entering ihram for Hajj, that sa'y counts for his Hajj and is not repeated during tawaf al-ziyarah. Understanding these rulings prevents confusion and improper repetition of rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act in question is tawaf al-qudoom (arrival tawaf). According to the Hanafi school, it is sunnah for those performing Hajj (ifrad or qiran) but not for the mutamatti'. The mutamatti' is in ihram for 'umrah upon arrival, so his tawaf al-'umrah suffices.
The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) omitted mentioning it for the mutamatti'.
2
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The mu'tamir can perform the essential tawaf ('umrah tawaf) immediately upon arrival. The hajj cannot perform tawaf al-ziyarah until after 'Arafah, so tawaf al-qudoom is prescribed for him as a substitute. For the mutamatti', no such substitute is needed.
This is based on the principle that a rukn (like tawaf in 'umrah) is not repeated as sunnah.
3
Apply the logic to sa'y and ramal
If the mutamatti' performs sa'y and ramal in a voluntary tawaf after entering ihram for Hajj, that sa'y is considered for his Hajj and is not repeated in tawaf al-ziyarah. Similarly, ramal performed then is not repeated.
The text explicitly states: 'لا يعيدهما في طواف الزيارة لأنهما لا يتكرران'.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider tawaf al-qudoom sunnah for the mutamatti' as well. This lesson focuses on the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi position is confirmed by al-Mubtagha, al-`Inayah, and al-Fath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر طواف القدوم لأنه ليس على المتمتع طواف قدوم كذا في المبتغى. أي لا يكون مسنوناً في حقه بخلاف القارن لأن المتمتع حين قدومه محرم بالعمرة فقط وليس لها طواف قدوم ولا صدر، والحكمة فيه أن المعتمر متمكن من أدائها حين وصل إلى البيت، وأما الحاج فغير متمكن من طواف الزيارة لعدم وقته فسن له طواف القدوم إلى أن يجيء وقته، والطواف ركن معظم في العمرة فلا يتكرر في الصدر كالوقوف للحج لا يتكرر كذا في النهاية. وفي قوله «ويحج» دلالة على أنه يسعى للحج ويرمل في طوافه والذي أتى به أولاً إنما هو عن العمرة فإن سعى المتمتع ورمل في طوافه بعد إحرامه بالحج لا يعيدهما في طواف الزيارة لأنهما لا يتكرران قوله : ( ويذبح فإن عجز فقد مر ) أي في باب القرآن فإن حكمهما واحد
And he did not mention tawaf al-qudoom because there is no tawaf al-qudoom for the mutamatti'. Thus in al-Mubtagha. i.e. it is not sunnah in his case, unlike the qarin, because the mutamatti' at his arrival is only in ihram for 'umrah, and it has no tawaf al-qudoom nor tawaf al-sadr. The wisdom is that the mu'tamir is able to perform it when he arrives at the House, while the hajj is not able to perform tawaf al-ziyarah due to its time not being there, so tawaf al-qudoom is prescribed for him until its time comes. Tawaf is a great rukn in 'umrah, so it is not repeated in the sadr, just as standing in 'Arafat for Hajj is not repeated. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in his saying 'and he performs Hajj' is an indication that he does sa'y for Hajj and does ramal in his tawaf, and what he performed first is only for 'umrah. If the mutamatti' performed sa'y and ramal in his tawaf after his ihram for Hajj, he does not repeat them in tawaf al-ziyarah because they are not repeated. His saying: (and he slaughters, and if he is unable, it has passed) i.e. in the chapter on Qiran, for their rulings are one.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage addresses the rulings on tawaf al-qudoom (arrival tawaf) and sa'y for a mutamatti'. The author notes that the matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) did not mention tawaf al-qudoom because it is not prescribed for the mutamatti'. Unlike the qarin (who combines 'umrah and Hajj in one ihram), the mutamatti' enters ihram for 'umrah first, which has its own tawaf that is performed immediately upon arrival, so there is no need for a separate tawaf al-qudoom. The wisdom is that the mu'tamir can perform the essential tawaf (tawaf al-'umrah) right away, whereas a hajj cannot perform tawaf al-ziyarah until after 'Arafah. Therefore, tawaf al-qudoom is sunnah for the hajj to compensate, but not for the mu'tamir. Furthermore, if a mutamatti' after entering ihram for Hajj performs a voluntary tawaf and sa'y, that sa'y will count for Hajj and he does not need to repeat it during tawaf al-ziyarah. Similarly, if he performed ramal (quick walking with shoulders bared) in that tawaf, it is not repeated. The passage concludes with a reminder that the ruling on slaughtering (dam) for tamattu' is the same as for qiran, as mentioned earlier.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudoom): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah before going to Mina, sunnah for hajj but not for mutamatti'.
رمل (ramal): Walking quickly with short steps and baring the right shoulder in tawaf.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs 'umrah first, then Hajj in the same trip, offering a sacrifice.

C) Because tawaf al-qudoom is only for the qarin.
D) Because the mutamatti' performs tawaf al-ziyarah earlier.

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' does not perform tawaf al-qudoom, and any sa'y/ramal done after entering ihram for Hajj is not repeated.

Timing of the Three-Day Fast for Tamattu'
Explains timing and validity of fasting for tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of the three-day fast in tamattu' and explain the Hanafi reasoning regarding the timing.

Core Idea
The three-day fast for tamattu' is only valid after its cause (tamattu') has occurred; fasting before 'umrah does not count.

The Hajj of tamattu' requires a sacrifice (hadiy) or, for those unable, fasting three days during Hajj and seven after returning. However, the timing of these fasts is not flexible—the three-day fast must follow the existence of its cause (sabab), which is tamattu' itself. This lesson clarifies the earliest point at which the three-day fast becomes valid according to the Hanafi school, distinguishing it sharply from the seven-day fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its obligation
The three-day fast is wajib for the mutamatti' who cannot afford a hadiy. It is a substitute for the sacrifice.
This obligation is specific to tamattu' and qiran.
2
Understand the cause (sabab)
The cause of this obligation is tamattu' itself—the combination of 'umrah and Hajj in one journey with a break in between.
The cause must exist before the obligation can be fulfilled.
3
Apply the rule of causality
A wajib act cannot be performed before its cause exists. Therefore, fasting three days in Shawwal before performing 'umrah is invalid because at that time the person is not yet a mutamatti'.
The act must be performed after the sabab is established.
4
Determine the earliest valid time
The three-day fast becomes valid as soon as the person enters ihram for 'umrah, even before performing tawaf. The entry into ihram marks the beginning of tamattu' (linguistically 'comfort') because it initiates the sequence of 'umrah followed by Hajj.
Ihram serves as a substitute for the complete 'umrah in making the cause effective.
5
Contrast with the seven-day fast
The seven-day fast, though sharing the same cause, can only be performed after the completion of Hajj (returning home), as Allah explicitly separated the times: three during Hajj, seven after.
The difference is based on the Qur'anic text (2:196).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن صام ثلاثة أيام من شوال فاعتمر لم يجزه عن الثلاثة لأن سبب وجوبه التمتع وهو في هذه الحالة غير متمتع فلا يجوز أداؤه قبل سببه قوله : (وصح لو بعد ما أحرم بها قبل أن يطوف) الثلاثة أي صح صوم بعد ما أحرم بالعمرة قبل الطواف لأنه أداء بعد السبب لأن سببه التمتع بالمعنى اللغوي وهو الترفق لترتيبه على التمتع بالنص ومأخذ الاشتقاق علة للمترتب، والعمرة في أشهر الحج هي السبب فيه لأنها التي بها يتحقق الترفق الذي كان ممنوعاً في الجاهلية وهو معنى التمتع، ولما لم يمكنه الخروج عن إحرامها بلا فعل نزل الإحرام منزلتها فلذا جاز بعد إحرامها قبل الفراغ منها. قيد الثلاثة لأن بصوم صوم . السبعة لا يجوز إلا بعد الفراغ وإن كان السبب فيهما واحداً لأن الله تعالى فصل بينهما فجعل الثلاثة في الحج أي في وقته والسبعة بعد الفراغ . وقيد طاف يعني بموجود لكونه في الحرم أو في مكة فلا يتصور العود، وإذا ساق الهدي لا يكون متمتعاً فلأن لا يكون إذا لم يسق كان أولى ا هـ . فقد جعل إلمام هذا المكي صحيحاً مع أنه قد ساق الهدي
His saying: (if he fasts three days in Shawwal and then performs 'umrah, it does not suffice for the three days) because the cause of its obligation is tamattu', and in this state he is not a mutamatti', so it is not permissible to perform it before its cause. His saying: (and it is valid if after he entered ihram for it before he performs tawaf) the three days means the fast after he entered ihram for 'umrah before tawaf is valid, because it is performance after the cause. Because its cause is tamattu' in the linguistic sense which is comfort, because it is based on tamattu' by text and the derivation of the word is the cause for the dependent. And 'umrah in the months of Hajj is the cause in it because it is that by which comfort is achieved which was prohibited in Jahiliyyah, and that is the meaning of tamattu'. Since he cannot exit its ihram without action, the ihram is taken as its substitute, so it is permissible after its ihram before completion of it. He restricted the three days because, regarding fasting the seven days, it is not permissible except after completion, even though the cause for both is one, because Allah separated between them, making the three in Hajj i.e. in its time, and the seven after completion. He restricted 'tawaf' meaning by existing (i.e. being in the Haram or Makkah) so the return is not conceivable. And if he drove the hadiy, he is not a mutamatti', so if he had not driven, it would be more appropriate. Thus he made the ilmaam of this Makkan valid even though he drove the hadiy.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage discusses the fasting required for tamattu' (three days during Hajj and seven days after returning). The key ruling is that the three days can only be fasted after the cause (tamattu') has come into existence. If someone fasts three days in Shawwal before performing 'umrah, it does not count because the cause (being a mutamatti') is not yet present. However, after entering ihram for 'umrah, even before completing it (i.e., before tawaf), the three days fast becomes valid because the definition of tamattu' as comfort (tarafuq) is now applicable. The seven days, on the other hand, can only be fasted after completing the Hajj rituals (after return). The text explains the reasoning: the three days are to be fasted during the Hajj period (within the months of Hajj), while the seven are after completion, as per Qur'anic division. The passage also touches on the case of driving a hadiy, which affects the status of mutamatti', but that part is not fully developed here.

Key Terms
صوم التمتع (sawm al-tamattu'): The obligatory fast for those performing tamattu' who cannot afford a hadiy: three days during Hajj and seven after returning.
سبب الوجوب (sabab al-wujub): The cause that necessitates the obligation; here, tamattu' itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because the cause of the obligation (tamattu') has not yet occurred.
C) Yes, because fasting is allowed before Hajj.
D) No, only seven days can be fasted before Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The three-day fast for tamattu' is only valid after the cause (tamattu') has been established, which begins with entering ihram for 'umrah; the seven-day fast is only valid after completing Hajj.

Timing Conditions for the Tamattu' Fasts
Ruling on fasting timing for tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing condition for the three fasts of tamattu' and identify when fasting in Shawwal is invalid.

Core Idea
The three fasts of tamattu' must be performed within the months of Hajj; fasting in Shawwal before these months is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a key condition for the tamattu' pilgrim who must fast instead of offering a hadi. It explains that the three fasts are only valid if performed within the months of Hajj, and that fasting in Shawwal before the Hajj months begin does not fulfill the requirement. The author also notes the preferred practice of postponing the fasts to the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under consideration is fasting three days for tamattu' when unable to afford a sacrifice. The ruling is that these fasts are wajib, but they are subject to a timing condition.
2
Identify the invalid scenario
The text states that if one fasts three days in Shawwal before the months of Hajj and then performs umrah, those fasts do not count. This is the key invalid case.
Shawwal is part of the months of Hajj according to the definition, but the author considers fasting before the Hajj period proper (perhaps before entering ihram) as invalid.
3
Identify the valid scenario
The fasts are valid if they are performed after entering ihram for umrah before tawaf. This indicates that the fasts must be done after the pilgrim has started the umrah rites.
Valid: after entering ihram for umrah but before tawaf (i.e., during the state of ihram for umrah).
4
Identify the preferred practice
The author mentions that the best is to postpone the three fasts to the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah, hoping to be able to offer the hadi instead, as sacrifice is superior to fasting.
Postponement is recommended, not obligatory.
5
Identify the rationale
The basis given is that fasting before the months of Hajj is not permissible. This timing condition ensures that the fasts are linked to the Hajj season.
The months of Hajj are defined as Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.

Source Text

It has preceded that the best is to postpone it to the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah due to hope of ability for the original (obligation), which is the hadi.

This passage deals with the tamattu' pilgrim who cannot afford a sacrificial animal (hadi) and must fast three days during Hajj. However, if one fasts after entering ihram for umrah before tawaf, it is valid. The commentary explains that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. Fasting before these months is not accepted for tamattu'. The preferred practice is to delay the three fasts to the seventh of Dhul-Hijjah, hoping to be able to offer the hadi instead, as sacrifice is superior to fasting.

The Ruling on Ish'ar: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar with evidence analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on ish'ar, identify the evidence each side uses, and explain the mufta bihi position in later Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is disputed: Abu Hanifa sees it as mutilation, while the Sahibayn follow the Prophet's action.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the recommended actions for a tamattu' pilgrim who brings a sacrificial animal, and then delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar (marking the animal). Abu Hanifa considers it makruh because it resembles mutilation, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it hasan because the Prophet himself did it. Understanding this dispute sharpens your skill in weighing conflicting evidences (ta'arud al-adilla) within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions for the mutamatti' with a hadi
The passage begins by describing the sequence: enter ihram, drive the animal, garland it (taqlid) with a water-skin or sandal, and do not do ish'ar. Note that garlanding is only for badanah (camel/cow), not sheep. This sets the context for the ish'ar discussion.
The text emphasizes following the Prophet's practice.
2
Understand the linguistic meaning of ish'ar and how it is performed
Ish'ar means making the animal known as a hadi; the practice is to split its hump from the right side (or left, as debated) to draw blood. This physical marking distinguishes it from other animals.
It is a physical act that some consider a form of muthlah.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa rules ish'ar as makruh because it is a form of mutilation (muthlah), which is prohibited by a general hadith. He prioritizes the prohibition (nahy) over the Prophet's action (fi'l), as a saying (qawl) takes precedence over an action in case of conflict.
The principle: 'al-qawl muqaddam 'ala al-fi'l' or 'al-nahy muqaddam 'ala al-ibahah'.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider ish'ar hasan (good) because the Prophet performed it in the Farewell Hajj, as recorded in Sahih Muslim. They follow the overt action (fi'l) of the Prophet as a sunnah.
They also note that mutilation is excessive disfigurement, not a simple cut on the hump.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to reconcile and identify the mufta bihi
The passage presents the rebuttal to Abu Hanifa: the Prophet's ish'ar was not mutilation but a protective measure to prevent theft. Al-Tahawi clarifies that Abu Hanifa only disliked excessive ish'ar that risks death. Later authorities (Fath al-Qadir, Ghayat al-Bayan) prefer the view of the Sahibayn, making ish'ar permissible and even preferable.
The mufta bihi today is permissibility, provided it is not harmful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن أراد سوق الهدى أحرم وساق وقلد بدنته بمزادة أو نعل ولا يشعر بيان لأفضل التمتع اقتداء برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. والواو في قوله «وساق» بمعنى «ثم لأن الأفضل أن لا يحرم بالسوق والتوجه بل يحرم بالتلبية والنية ثم يسوق، وأفاد بالتقليد أنه أفضل من التجليل وبالسوق أنه أفضل من القود إلا إذا كانت لاتنساق فيقودها. والضمير في قوله «أراد ) عائد إلى المتمتع بمعنى مريده، والمراد بالإحرام إحرام العمرة، وقيد بالبدنة لأن الشاة لا يسن تقليدها. والإشعار في اللغة الإعلام بأن البدنة هدي والمراد هنا أن يشق سنامها من الجانب الأيمن. كذا في شرح الأقطع . وفي الهداية قالوا: والأشبه هو الأيسر بسر وهو مكروه عند أبي حنيفة حسن عندهما للإتباع الثابت في صحیح مسلم وغيره، وأجيب لأبي حنيفة بأنه مثلة وقد نهى عنه فتعارضا فرجحنا المنع لأنه قول وهو مقدم على الفعل أو نهي وهو مقدم على المبيح، ورد بأنه ليس منها لأنها ما يكون تشويهاً كقطع الأنف والأذنين فليس كل . مثلة وجرح ولأنه نهى عنها في أول الإسلام وفعل الإشعار في حجة الوداع. فلو كان منها لم يفعله وبأن إشعاره عليه السلام لصيانة الهدي لأن المشركين لا يمتنعون عن تعرضه إلا به . وقال الطحاوي : إنما كره أبو حنيفة الإشعار المحدث الذي يفعل على وجه المبالغة ويخاف منه السراية إلى الموت لا مطلق الإشعار، واختاره في غاية البيان وصححه وفي فتح القدير أنه الأولى
His saying: 'If he intends to drive the hadi, he enters ihram, drives it, garlands his badanah with a water-skin or sandal, and does not mark it.' Explanation of the best form of tamattu' following the Messenger of Allah. The waw in 'and drives' means 'then', because the best is that he does not enter ihram with the driving and facing, but enters ihram with talbiyah and intention, then drives. It is derived that garlanding is better than covering, and driving is better than leading, unless it does not follow, then he leads it. The pronoun in 'he intends' refers to the mutamatti', meaning its desirer. By ihram is meant the ihram of umrah. It is restricted to the badanah because the sheep is not prescribed to be garlanded. Ish'ar linguistically means informing that the badanah is a hadi; here it means to split its hump from the right side. This is in Sharh al-Aqta'. In al-Hidayah: They said: The more similar is the left side. And it is makruh according to Abu Hanifah, good according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the established following in Sahih Muslim and others. It was answered for Abu Hanifah that it is mutilation and he was prohibited from it, so they conflict, so we preferred the prohibition because it is a saying and a saying takes precedence over an action, or a prohibition takes precedence over permission. It was refuted that it is not mutilation because mutilation is disfigurement like cutting the nose and ears, so not every wound is mutilation, and because it was prohibited in early Islam, and he performed ish'ar in the Farewell Hajj. So if it were mutilation, he would not have done it, and because his ish'ar was to protect the hadi, as the polytheists would not refrain from attacking it except with it. Al-Tahawi said: Abu Hanifah only disliked the innovated ish'ar that is done excessively and from which death may be feared, not absolute ish'ar. And it was chosen in Ghayat al-Bayan and verified, and in Fath al-Qadir it is preferable.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage details the recommended actions for the tamattu' pilgrim who decides to bring a sacrificial animal (hadi). He should enter ihram first with the intention and talbiyah, then drive the animal, garland it with a water-skin or sandal, and not mark it (ish'ar). Garlanding is better than covering the animal, and driving is better than leading unless the animal is unruly. The discussion then focuses on ish'ar (splitting the hump to mark the animal). Abu Hanifa considers it makruh because it is a form of mutilation (muthlah), which is prohibited. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it good (hasan) because the Prophet himself performed ish'ar and it is proven in authentic hadith. The Hanafi response reconciles that the Prophet's ish'ar was not mutilation because it was done to protect the animal from thieves and was not excessive. Al-Tahawi limits the dislike to excessively dangerous marking. The preferred position in later works is that it is permissible and preferable.

Key Terms
إشعار (ish'ar): Marking the sacrificial animal by splitting its hump from the right or left side to indicate it is a hadi.
تقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the sacrificial animal with a water-skin or sandal to distinguish it.
بدنة (badanah): A large sacrificial animal such as a camel or cow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later (mufta bihi) position on ish'ar in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) It is makruh tanzih and should be avoided.
B) It is haram because it is mutilation.
C) It is permissible and even preferable.
D) It is wajib because the Prophet did it.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar is resolved by later authorities who consider it permissible, following the Sahibayn, provided it is not excessive.

Prohibition of Tahlil for the Mutamatti' with Hadi
States the prohibition of tahlil for mutamatti' with hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tahlil for a tamattu' pilgrim with a hadi and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
A tamattu' pilgrim with a hadi must not perform tahlil until after sacrificing his hadi.

In this passage, the author establishes a key restriction for the mutamatti' who drives a sacrificial animal (hadi). The ruling prevents the pilgrim from leaving ihram after umrah until the day of Nahr. The proof is a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct performance of tamattu' hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tahlil (leaving ihram) after completing umrah for a tamattu' pilgrim who has brought a hadi. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: 'I matted my hair and garlanded my hadi, so I will not be free until I sacrifice.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'fala aḥillu' (so I will not be free) explicitly indicates prohibition of tahlil until the sacrifice is performed, establishing that the hadi prevents tahlil.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If the pilgrim shaves his head (or performs tahlil) after umrah while having a hadi, he must offer a dam (sacrificial penalty).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يتحلل بعد عمرته) لأن سوق الهدي يمنعه من التحلل لحديث البخاري : أني لبدت رأسي وقلدت هديي فلا أحل حتى أنحر. وقد قدمنا أنه لو حلق رأسه بعد الفراغ من عمرته وقد كان ساق الهدي لزمه دم، ومقتضاه أنه لا يشعر ولا يتحلل بعد عمرته ويحرم بالحج يوم التروية وقبله أحب فإذا حلق يوم النحر حل من إحراميه أي من إحرامي الحج والعمرة وهو تصريح ببقاء إحرام العمرة بعد الوقوف بعرفة إلى الحلق وأورد عليه في النهاية بأن القارن إذا قتل صيداً بعد الوقوف بعرفة لا يلزمه قيمتان، وأجاب بأن إحرام العمرة قد انتهى بالوقوف في حق سائر الأحكام وإنما يبقى في حق التحلل لا غير كأحكام الحج تنتهي بالحلق في يوم النحر ولا يبقى إلا في حق النساء خاصة، واستعبده الشارح الزيلعي وهو المراد عند إطلاق الشارح في هذا الكتاب بأن القارن إذا جامع بعد الوقوف يجب عليه بدنة للحج والعمرة شاة وبعد الحلق قبل الطواف شاتان ا هـ. لكن صاحب النهاية لم يجزم به إنما عزاه إلى شيخ الإسلام في مبسوطه وهو اختياره، وأكثر عبارات الأصحاب كما قال الشارح. وفي فتح القدير وهو الظاهر إذ قضاء الأعمال يمنع بقاء الإحرام والوجوب إنما هو باعتبار أنه جناية على الإحرام لا على الأعمال، والفرع المنقول في الجماع يدل على ما قلنا وقد تناقض كلام شيخ الإسلام فإنه أوجب في
His saying: 'He does not perform tahlil after his umrah' because driving the hadi prevents him from tahlil, based on the hadith of Bukhari: 'I matted my hair and garlanded my hadi, so I will not be free until I sacrifice.' And we have previously stated that if he shaves his head after finishing his umrah while he has driven the hadi, a dam is required. Its implication is that he does not mark (ish'ar) nor perform tahlil after his umrah, and he enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah and before it is better. When he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes free from both ihrams, i.e., from the ihrams of hajj and umrah, which is an explicit statement of the continuation of the umrah ihram after standing at Arafat until shaving. An objection was raised in al-Nihayah that if a qarin kills game after standing at Arafat, two values are not required. He answered that the umrah ihram has ended with standing with respect to all other rulings, and it remains only with respect to tahlil, just as the rulings of hajj end with shaving on the day of Nahr and remain only with respect to women specifically. The commentator al-Zayla'i considered this far-fetched. And it is what is meant when the sharh in this book is unrestricted that if a qarin has intercourse after standing, a badanah is required for hajj and a sheep for umrah, and after shaving before tawaf, two sheep. But the author of al-Nihayah did not assert it; he attributed it to Shaykh al-Islam in his Mabsut, and it is his choice. Most expressions of the companions are as the sharh said. In Fath al-Qadir, it is the apparent view because performing actions prevents continuation of ihram, and the obligation is only considered as transgressing against ihram, not against actions. The transmitted branch on intercourse indicates what we said. And the speech of Shaykh al-Islam is contradictory, for he required in...
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage establishes that a tamattu' pilgrim who brings a hadi must not perform tahlil (leave ihram) after his umrah; he remains in a state of ihram until after the sacrifice on the day of Nahr. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet in Sahih al-Bukhari. If he shaves his head after umrah while having a hadi, he owes a dam (sacrificial penalty). He should enter ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul-Hijjah) or earlier. When he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes free from both the ihram of umrah and the ihram of hajj. This implies that the ihram of umrah continues even after standing at Arafat until shaving. An objection from al-Nihayah uses the example of a qarin (one who combines umrah and hajj) who kills game after standing at Arafat; he does not have to pay double penalty, suggesting the umrah ihram has ended. The response is that the umrah ihram ends for most rulings but remains only for the purpose of tahlil (the act of leaving ihram). Al-Zayla'i finds this far-fetched. The preferred view in later works (Fath al-Qadir) is that the ihram of umrah ends with standing at Arafat, as performing the major actions terminates the ihram; the obligation of a penalty for violations after standing is only because it is a transgression against ihram state, not against the actions. The contradiction in Shaykh al-Islam's statements is noted.

Key Terms
تحلل (tahlil): The act of leaving the state of ihram by shaving or trimming hair.
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim who enters ihram for both umrah and hajj together or makes umrah and then hajj without tahlil between them.
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for pilgrimage, which prohibits certain actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence for a tamattu' pilgrim who shaves his head after umrah while having brought a hadi?
A) Nothing
B) A dam (sacrificial penalty)
C) The pilgrimage becomes invalid
D) He must fast three days

Key Takeaway
A tamattu' pilgrim with a hadi must not perform tahlil until after sacrificing the hadi; violation incurs a dam.

The Qarin's Ihram After Standing at Arafat: Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the qarin's ihram after standing at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether the qarin's umrah ihram remains after standing at Arafat and identify the practical consequences.

Core Idea
The qarin's umrah ihram may persist only for tahlil after standing, but Fath al-Qadir prefers it ends entirely.

This passage delves into an internal Hanafi disagreement regarding the qarin—the pilgrim who combines umrah and hajj. The central question is whether his ihram for umrah continues after standing at Arafat. The answer affects penalties for violations. The commentary presents multiple views and attempts to reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The majority of Hanafi authorities hold that the qarin's umrah ihram ends after standing at Arafat for most rulings, but remains only for the purpose of tahlil.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Al-Zayla'i and the author of Fath al-Qadir hold that the umrah ihram ends entirely after standing; it does not remain even for tahlil.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Performing the actions (e.g., standing at Arafat) terminates the ihram. Penalties for violations after standing are due only because the violation occurred during the original ihram state, not because it continues.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority response: the ihram remains specifically for tahlil, analogous to hajj rulings that remain for women after shaving. This is supported by the hadith about tahlil.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a qarin commits a violation after standing (e.g., hunting), does he owe one penalty (for hajj ihram) or two (for both umrah and hajj ihrams)? The difference is practical.

Source Text

The Effect of Bringing a Hadi on the Mutamatti' and the Persistence of Umrah Ihram after Wuquf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on umrah ihram persistence after wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the persistence of umrah ihram after wuquf for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi, and apply the majority view to a scenario involving a hunting violation.

Core Idea
Bringing a hadi extends the mutamatti's umrah ihram until shaving, but its extent after wuquf is debated among Hanafi scholars.

In this lesson, we examine an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi). The core issue is whether the ihram of umrah persists in full force after standing at Arafah (wuquf) or whether it ends except for the purpose of becoming halal. This dispute has practical consequences for penalties incurred for violations like hunting or intercourse. We will explore the positions of the majority (al-Zayla'i) and the minority (author of al-Nihayah), and understand the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The dispute is about whether the ihram of umrah for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi remains in full force after standing at Arafah (wuquf) or whether it ends, except for the ability to become halal (tahlil).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: both positions are within the Hanafi school.
2
State the majority view (al-Zayla'i)
Al-Zayla'i and most Hanafi scholars hold that the ihram of umrah persists in full force until shaving on the day of Nahr. Therefore, violations like hunting or intercourse after wuquf incur separate penalties for both hajj and umrah ihrams.
The majority view is considered the mufta bihi as per al-Bahr al-Raiq.
3
State the minority view (al-Nihayah)
The author of al-Nihayah (and Shaykh al-Islam in al-Mabsut) holds that after wuquf, the ihram of umrah ends for all purposes except enabling the mutamatti' to become halal. Therefore, violations after wuquf only incur penalties for hajj ihram, not umrah.
This view is based on the ruling for a qarin who kills game after wuquf – only one penalty is owed.
4
Analyse the proofs
The majority relies on the clear statement in the text: 'when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes halal from his two ihrams', implying both ihrams were active until then. The minority argues from the qarin case: if umrah ihram persisted, a qarin killing game would owe two penalties, but only one is owed.
The author of al-Nihayah responds that the umrah ihram remains only for tahlil, not for penalties.
5
Apply the majority view to a scenario
Consider a mutamatti' with a hadi who hunts after wuquf. According to the majority, he owes two valuations (one for hajj, one for umrah). According to the minority, he owes only one. Similarly, if he has intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah, the majority says one badanah for hajj and one sheep for umrah; the minority says one badanah for hajj only.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: the number of penalties varies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

له أثر في استدامة الإحرام أيضاً بل أولى لأن البقاء أسهل. كذا في النهاية قوله : ( ويحرم بالحج يوم التروية وقبله أحب لما ذكرناه في متمتع لا يسوق الهدي، وإنما ذكر يوم التروية لأن الأفعال بعد ذلك تتعقب الإحرام قوله : (فإذا حلق يوم النحر حل من إحراميه) أي من إحرامي الحج والعمرة وهو تصريح ببقاء إحرام العمرة بعد الوقوف بعرفة إلى الحلق وأورد عليه في النهاية بأن القارن إذا قتل صيداً بعد الوقوف بعرفة لا يلزمه قيمتان، وأجاب بأن إحرام العمرة قد انتهى بالوقوف في حق سائر الأحكام وإنما يبقى في حق التحلل لا غير كأحكام الحج تنتهي بالحلق في يوم النحر ولا يبقى إلا في حق النساء خاصة، واستعبده الشارح الزيلعي وهو المراد عند إطلاق الشارح في هذا الكتاب بأن القارن إذا جامع بعد الوقوف يجب عليه بدنة للحج والعمرة شاة وبعد الحلق قبل الطواف شاتان ا هـ. لكن صاحب النهاية لم يجزم به إنما عزاه إلى شيخ الإسلام في مبسوطه وهو اختياره، وأكثر عبارات الأصحاب كما قال الشارح. وفي فتح القدير وهو الظاهر إذ قضاء الأعمال يمنع بقاء الإحرام والوجوب إنما هو باعتبار أنه جناية على الإحرام لا على الأعمال، والفرع المنقول في الجماع يدل على ما قلنا وقد تناقض كلام شيخ الإسلام فإنه أوجب في لا : بهديه ما شاء ولا شيء عليه، ولو أراد أن يذبح هديه ويحج لم يكن له ذلك، وإن نحره ثم رجع بعد الحلق إلى أهله ثم حج لا شيء عليه أي لأنه غير متمتع، ولو رجع إلى غير أهله الآفاق حج من يكون متمتعاً وعليه هديان هدي التمتع وهدي الحلق قبل الوقت ا هـ. وفي شرحه عن المحيط : فإن ذبح الهدي فرجع إلى أهله فله أن لا يحج لأنه لم يوجد في حق الحج إلا مجرد النية فلا يلزمه الحج، وإن أراد أن ينحر هديه ويحل ولا يرجع ويحج من عامه لم يكن له ذلك لأنه مقيم على عزيمة التمتع فيمنعه الهدي من الإحلال فإن فعله إلى أهله ثم حج لا شيء عليه لأنه غير متمتع، ولو حل النهاية قوله : (يجب عليه بدنة للحج والعمرة شاة) أي اتفاقاً، وقوله وبعد الحلق قبل الطواف شاتان فيه خلاف وقيل بدنة وشاة. وقال الوبري : بدنة للحج ولا شيء عليه للعمرة، واستصوبه في الفتح كما سيأتي معللاً في الجنايات بما ظاهره بقاء الإحرام للعمرة قبل الحلق فقط لا مطلقاً كما هو ظاهر كلام الزيلعي قوله : ( وأكثر عبارات الأصحاب) «أكثر» مبتدأ خبره قوله «كما قال الشارح قوله : (وقد تناقض كلام شيخ الإسلام الخ) قال في النهر : يمكن أنه حل من إحراميه ولا تمتع ولا قران لمكي ومن حولها فإن عاد المتمتع إلى بلده بعد العمرة ولم جماع القارن بعد الوقوف شاتين فلا يخلو من أن يكون إحرام العمرة بعد الوقوف توجب الجناية عليه شيئاً أو لا، فإن أوجبت لزم شمول الوجوب وإلا فشمول العدم. فالحاصل أن المذهب بقاء إحرام العمرة إلى الحلق ويحل منه في كل شيء حتى في حق النساء إذا كان متمتعاً ساق الهدي لأن المانع له من التحلل سوقه
