Book of Hajj, Chapter of Tamattu': He feels [the ihram] and does not become halal after his umrah, and he enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah, and before it is more beloved. When he shaves on the day of Nahr, every violation against ihram becomes binding upon him, as if he were a muhrim. The conclusion is that bringing the hadi has an effect in establishing ihram initially, so it also has an effect in the continuation of ihram, even more so because continuance is easier. This is in al-Nihayah. His statement: (and he enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah, and before is more beloved) as we mentioned regarding a mutamatti' who does not bring a hadi; he only mentioned the day of Tarwiyah because the actions after that follow the ihram. His statement: (and when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes halal from his two ihrams) i.e., from the ihrams of hajj and umrah, and this is a clear statement that the ihram of umrah remains after standing at Arafah until shaving. An objection was raised to this in al-Nihayah: if a qarin kills game after standing at Arafah, two valuations are not binding on him. He answered that the ihram of umrah has ended by standing with respect to all other rulings, and it only remains with respect to tahlil (becoming halal), just as the rulings of hajj end by shaving on the day of Nahr and nothing remains except with respect to women specifically. The commentator al-Zayla'i deemed this improbable; and this is meant when the commentator [al-Zayla'i] is referred to in this book, as when a qarin has intercourse after standing, a badanah is obligatory on him for hajj and a sheep for umrah, and after shaving before tawaf, two sheep, etc. But the author of al-Nihayah did not affirm it; he attributed it to Shaykh al-Islam in his Mabsut, and it is his choice. Most expressions of the authors are as the commentator said. In Fath al-Qadir: it is apparent that the completion of rituals prevents the continuation of ihram, and the obligation is only based on it being a violation of ihram, not of the rituals. The transmitted sub-case regarding intercourse indicates what we said, and the words of Shaykh al-Islam are contradictory, because he obligated in...
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the ruling of a mutamatti' (one performing tamattu') who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi). The author explains that such a person remains in a state of ihram after completing his umrah and does not become halal until he sacrifices the hadi on the day of Nahr. He enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah) and cannot become halal before that. When he shaves on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah), he becomes halal from both ihrams (hajj and umrah) simultaneously. This indicates that the ihram of umrah persists after standing at Arafah until shaving. However, a difficulty arises: if a qarin (one performing qiran) kills game after standing at Arafah, he does not owe two penalties (for both hajj and umrah). This suggests that the ihram of umrah has ended at wuquf. The author of al-Nihayah reconciles this by saying that the ihram of umrah indeed ends with respect to all rulings except the ability to become halal; i.e., it persists only for the purpose of tahlil, not for imposing penalties. Then al-Zayla'i deems this improbable and holds that after wuquf, the ihram of umrah remains in full force until shaving, including for penalties. The text then discusses a dispute about the number of penalties for a qarin who has intercourse after wuquf but before tawaf al-ziyarah. The majority opinion (most expressions of the authors) is that if a qarin has intercourse after shaving but before tawaf al-ziyarah, he owes one badanah for hajj and one sheep for umrah (two sheep total) because he remains in ihram for both until tawaf. The passage concludes by distinguishing between the mutamatti' who brought a hadi and the qarin: the mutamatti' becomes halal from everything including women after sacrificing his hadi, while the qarin becomes halal from everything except women (like the ihram of hajj). Apart from that, there is no difference between them after entering ihram for hajj.

Key Terms
سوق الهدي (sawq al-hadi): Bringing a sacrificial animal (hadi) while in ihram for tamattu' or qiran, which causes the person to remain in ihram until the animal is sacrificed.
قارن (qarin): One who performs qiran (combining hajj and umrah in one ihram).
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as a sacrifice for major violations during hajj; equivalent to a hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (as per al-Zayla'i), does the ihram of umrah for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi remain after standing at Arafah?
A) Yes, it remains in full force until shaving on the day of Nahr.
B) No, it ends completely at wuquf.
C) It remains only for the purpose of becoming halal, not for penalties.
D) It remains only for the purpose of intercourse.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi position holds that the ihram of umrah for a mutamatti' with a hadi persists in full force after wuquf until shaving, resulting in double penalties for some violations.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Tamattu' and Qiran for Residents of Mecca
Analysis of the ruling prohibiting tamattu' and qiran for residents of Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' and qiran for a Makki, explain the Quranic proof (2:196), and distinguish between the majority and minority positions within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A Makki cannot perform tamattu' or qiran because he cannot fulfill the condition of 'ilmam sahih' — returning home between Umrah and Hajj.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines one of the distinctive rulings of the Hanafi school: that tamattu' and qiran are not valid for residents of Mecca and its vicinity. The ruling is derived from a specific interpretation of Quran 2:196 and the concept of 'ilmam sahih'. While the majority of Hanafi scholars hold that these combined forms of Hajj are invalid for a Makki, a minority view considers them valid but sinful. In this lesson, you will navigate the proof, the condition, and the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the subject
The acts are tamattu' (performing Umrah and Hajj with a break in between) and qiran (combining both in a single ihram). The subject is the Makki, defined as a resident of the Haram area (Mecca and its miqat boundaries).
The passage explicitly states 'لا تمتع ولا قران لمكي' (no tamattu' nor qiran for a Makki).
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites Quran 2:196: 'ذلك لمن لم يكن أهله حاضري المسجد الحرام' (That is for those whose family is not present in the Sacred Mosque). He explains why the demonstrative pronoun 'dhalika' refers to tamattu', not to hady, based on grammatical clues.
The lam in 'li-man' indicates benefit (what we do), while hady is something we pay, so the verse limits tamattu' to non-residents.
3
Understand the condition of 'ilmam sahih'
The condition for valid tamattu' is that the pilgrim, after performing Umrah, returns to his original home (outside the Haram) before starting Hajj. For a Makki, 'returning home' means staying in Mecca, which does not constitute leaving the miqat area. Thus, the condition is impossible.
The term 'ilmam sahih' is defined as returning to one's permanent residence after Umrah, not merely going to any location.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The majority of Hanafi scholars (zahir al-riwayah) hold that tamattu' and qiran are invalid (batil) for a Makki; if performed, they are sinful and must be repeated. A minority (some mashayikh) argue that they are valid but sinful, requiring a compensatory dam (dam jabar) rather than a thanksgiving dam.
The minority view is based on a different interpretation of the verse and an analogy with prayer in a usurped land.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tamattu' and qiran are invalid for a Makki. If a resident of Mecca attempts these forms, he must perform a valid Hajj and Umrah separately, and his actions are sinful.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors the majority view, stating that 'zahir al-kutub' supports invalidity.

Book of Hajj / Chapter of Tamattu'. He becomes lawful from his two ihrams, and there is no tamattu' nor qiran for a Makki and those around it. If the mutamatti' returns to his country after Umrah and did not, intercourse of the qarin after standing produces two sheep. It is not free from that the ihram of Umrah after standing obligates something upon him or not. If it obligates, the inclusion of obligation applies, otherwise the inclusion of non-obligation. The conclusion is that the madhhab is that the ihram of Umrah remains until shaving, and one becomes lawful from it in everything, even regarding women, if he is a mutamatti' who drove the hady, because the preventing factor is his driving and it has been removed by slaughtering. For the qarin, he becomes lawful from it in everything except women, like the ihram of Hajj. This is the difference between the mutamatti' who drove the hady and the qarin; otherwise there is no difference between them after ihram for Hajj according to the correct view as we mentioned. In al-Muhit: A qarin performed tawaf for his Umrah then became lawful, so upon him are two animals, and he does not become lawful from his Umrah by shaving. If he entered ihram for Umrah, performed tawaf for it, then added Hajj, then shaved, he becomes lawful from his Umrah and nothing is upon him because he is like one who entered ihram for Hajj after having shaved from Umrah. His statement: (There is no) tamattu' nor qiran for a Makki and those around it due to His statement, 'That is for those whose family is not present in the Sacred Mosque' (Quran 2:196), based on the return of the demonstrative pronoun to tamattu' not to hady, by the evidence of its connection with the 'lam' which is used for what we do, unlike hady which is upon us. If hady were meant, it would have said 'that upon those who are not' and because it is a demonstrative for distant and tamattu' is more distant than hady. Then, the books of matn, commentary, and fatwa that tamattu' and qiran are not valid from them, because of their statement: When the mutamatti' returns to apparent... saying that it ends with standing except regarding women. It was transmitted in al-Fath from al-Ghayah, attributed to al-Mabsut, al-Bada'i', and al-Asbajabi: If the qarin had intercourse the first time after shaving before tawaf al-ziyarah, upon him is a badanah for Hajj and a sheep for Umrah because the qarin becomes lawful from two ihrams by shaving except regarding women, so he is still in ihram for both regarding them. This contradicts what is mentioned in the book and commentaries of al-Quduri, which require only one sheep after shaving. This shows that the obligation of two sheep has no contradiction. I say: But the statement of al-Nihayah earlier that 'it only remains regarding becoming lawful' indicates ending with standing regarding women too. And you have learned that what is in al-Nihayah is attributed to Shaykh al-Islam. His statement: (If it obligates) meaning the crime requires the inclusion of obligation, that is in intercourse and other things; otherwise, if it does not obligate anything, the inclusion of non-obligation, meaning non-obligation in intercourse and other things. As for obligation in intercourse and non-obligation in killing game, there is no basis for that. It will come in the chapter on crimes that the madhhab regarding game is that two animals are due and that the due of one animal is weak. His statement: (Then, the apparent of the books, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: The companions of the madhhab stated that if an afaqi mutamatti' returns to his country, his tamattu' becomes invalid by consensus between Imam and his two companions. The condition of tamattu' absolutely is the absence of sound homecoming, and there is no existence of the conditioned without its condition. There is no doubt that they said the existence of the defective with sin and did not say the existence of the invalid legally while committing a prohibition. The implication of the words of the Imams of the madhhab is more worthy of consideration than some mashayikh. Similarly in al-Fath, summarized. And he chose prohibition of it, that is the Umrah also, even if he did not perform Hajj. But it is not hidden that what he argued from the words of the Imams of the madhhab does not imply its non-existence from him, but rather that he is not a mutamatti', which is consistent with what will come in attaching ihram to ihram: that if a Makki attaches the ihram of Hajj to Umrah after he performed tawaf for it or did not perform tawaf and did not revoke anything, it suffices him. [PAGE 641] ...
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the ruling on tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break in between) and qiran (combining both with a single ihram) for residents of Mecca (Makki) and those living in the vicinity of the Haram. The central ruling, derived from the Quranic verse 'That is for those whose family is not present in the Sacred Mosque' (2:196), is that tamattu' and qiran are not valid for a Makki. The text explores two main interpretations: (1) the apparent view of the books (zahir al-kutub) that such acts are invalid (fasid) and sinful, and (2) the view of some mashayikh (e.g., al-Hidayah and al-Asbajabi) that they are valid but sinful, requiring a dam jabar (compensatory sacrifice) rather than dam shukr (thanksgiving sacrifice). The passage clarifies that the prohibition is on the prescribed form of tamattu' and qiran, not on merely combining Umrah and Hajj in the same trip. The key issue is the concept of 'ilmam sahih' (sound homecoming): for a Makki, returning to one's home after Umrah is not possible because they are already in Mecca, so the condition for tamattu' is missing. Thus, their combining is not considered tamattu' but a simple sequential performance, which is valid but may incur sin if done with the intention of imitating tamattu'. The text also discusses sub-issues: the ruling on a qarin who has intercourse after shaving, differences between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on specific points, and the scenario where a mutamatti' returns to his home country after Umrah. Throughout, the commentary shows the Hanafi school's internal debate between the majority (ruling of invalidity) and minority (validity with sin), with the majority view being the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): The ritual of performing Umrah during the months of Hajj, then returning to ihram for Hajj with a break in between, requiring a sacrifice (dam).
قران (qiran): Combining Umrah and Hajj in a single ihram, performing only one tawaf and sa'y.
مكي (makki): A resident of Mecca or the Haram area (within the miqat boundary).
الإلمام الصحيح (al-ilmaam al-sahih): Returning to one's permanent residence after completing Umrah and before starting Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what is the ruling for a Makki who performs tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break)?
A) Valid, requires dam shukr.
B) Invalid, must repeat both acts.
C) Valid but sinful, requires dam jabar.
D) Valid if he did not intend tamattu'.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' and qiran are not valid for residents of Mecca because the condition of 'ilmam sahih' (returning home between acts) cannot be fulfilled, as established by Quran 2:196.

Ruling on Tamattu' and Qiran for the Makki
Analyzing the ruling and validity of Tamattu' and Qiran for residents of Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between validity and permissibility in the ruling on Tamattu' for a Makki and explain the Hanafi position requiring compensatory blood.

Core Idea
A Makki's Tamattu' is valid but sinful requiring compensatory blood; the prohibition negates permissibility, not validity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: Is the Tamattu' of a Makki invalid or merely prohibited? The author reconciles conflicting texts by distinguishing between sihha (validity) and hilla (permissibility). Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling (mufta bihi) in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Identify the ruling under discussion: the validity and permissibility of Tamattu' and Qiran for a resident of Makkah (Makki).
2
State the two conflicting positions
Note the two views: (1) the Makki's Tamattu' is invalid (batil) because of proper returning (ilmaam); (2) it is valid but sinful and requires compensatory blood.
The author leans toward the second view.
3
Locate the key terms
Identify 'al-ilmaam al-sahih' (proper returning) and 'dam al-jabr' (compensatory blood). These are central to the dispute.
Ilmaam invalidates the reward-based Tamattu' but not the act itself.
4
Explain the author's reconciliation
The author argues that the statement 'no Tamattu' and no Qiran for a Makki' negates permissibility, not validity. Hence, if done, the act is valid but sinful, and compensatory blood is required.
This resolves the apparent contradiction between texts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Makki performs Tamattu', some hold he must repeat Hajj (invalid view); others hold his Hajj is valid but he owes compensatory blood and is sinful.
The author's view is the latter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب التمتع
لو أهله ولم يكن ساق الهدي بطل تمتعه. قال في غاية البيان ولهذا قلنا لم يصح تمتع المكي لوجود الإلمام الصحيح ومقتضاه أنه لو أحرم بعمرة في أشهر الحج وحل منها ثم أحرم بحج فإنه لا يلزمه دم، لكن صرح في التحفة بأنه يصح تمتعهم وقرانهم فإنه نقل في غاية البيان عنها أنهم لو تمتعوا جاز وأساؤوا ويجب عليهم دم الجبر، وهكذا ذكر الأسبيجابي ثم قال : ولا يباح لهم الأكل من ذلك الدم ولا يجزئهم الصوم إن كانوا معسرين فتعين أن يكون المراد بالنفي في قولهم لا تمتع ولا قران لمكي نفي الحل لا نفي الصحة ولذا وجب دم جبر فعلوا وهو فرع الصحة واشتراطهم عدم الإلمام فيما بينهما إنما هو للتمتع المنتهض سبباً للثواب المترتب عليه وجوب دم الشكر. فالحاصل أن المكي إذا أحرم بعمرة في أشهر الحج فإن كان من نيته الحج من عامه فإنه يكون آثماً لأنه عين التمتع المنهي عنه لهم، فإن حج من عامه لزمه جناية لا شكر، وإن لم يكن من نيته الحج من عامة ولم يحج فإنه لا يكون آثماً بالاعتمار في أشهر الحج لأنهم وغيرهم سواء في رخصة الاعتمار في أشهر الحج. وما لأنه أتى بأفعالها كما لزمته غير أن منهي عنه. وبهذا عرف أنه يتصور الجمع بين العمرة والحج في حق المكي لكن لا على وجه التمتع والقرآن، وهذا هو المترجم له في الباب الآتي ا هـ.
Chapter of Hajj: Section on Tamattu'. If he returns to his family and had not brought the sacrificial animal, his Tamattu' becomes invalid. He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: For this reason we said that the Tamattu' of a Makki is not valid due to the occurrence of proper returning. And its implication is that if he assumes ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj and then completes it and then assumes ihram for Hajj, no blood is required of him. However, it is stated explicitly in al-Tuhfah that their Tamattu' and Qiran are valid. For it is reported in Ghayat al-Bayan from them that if they perform Tamattu', it is permissible and they do wrong, and compensatory blood is obligatory upon them. Similarly, al-Asbijabi mentioned, then said: It is not permissible for them to eat from that blood, nor does fasting suffice if they are unable, so it is determined that the intended meaning of negation in their statement 'no Tamattu' and no Qiran for a Makki' is negation of permissibility (hall), not negation of validity (sihha). Hence compensatory blood became obligatory because they did it, and that is based on validity. And their condition of the absence of returning between them is only for the Tamattu' that is a cause for reward, upon which the obligation of gratitude blood is contingent. So the summary is: When a Makki assumes ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj, if he intends to perform Hajj in that year, he is sinful because it is the very Tamattu' prohibited to them. Then if he performs Hajj in that year, compensatory blood is required, not gratitude. If he does not intend to perform Hajj in that year and does not perform Hajj, then he is not sinful by performing Umrah in the months of Hajj, because they and others are equal in the concession of performing Umrah in the months of Hajj. And because he performed its actions as required of him, except that it is not prohibited to him. By this it is known that the combination of Umrah and Hajj is conceivable for the Makki, but not in the manner of Tamattu' or Qiran. And this is what is referred to in the coming chapter.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling regarding Tamattu' and Qiran for residents of Makkah (the Makki). The author begins by restating a rule: if a Makki returns to his family after Umrah without bringing a sacrificial animal, his Tamattu' becomes invalid. He then cites Ghayat al-Bayan, which states that the Makki's Tamattu' is invalid due to 'proper returning' (ilmaam sahih). However, the author notes a contradiction: al-Tuhfah explicitly says their Tamattu' and Qiran are valid, and Ghayat al-Bayan itself reports that if they perform Tamattu', it is permissible but they are sinful, requiring compensatory blood (dam jabr). The author resolves this by distinguishing between negation of permissibility (hall) and negation of validity (sihha). The statements 'no Tamattu' and no Qiran for a Makki' mean it is not permissible, not that it is invalid. Therefore, if a Makki performs Umrah in Hajj months intending to do Hajj that year, he is sinful and if he does Hajj, he owes compensatory blood. If he does not intend Hajj, he is not sinful. The conclusion is that a Makki can combine Umrah and Hajj, but not as Tamattu' or Qiran.

Key Terms
الإلمام الصحيح (al-ilmaam al-sahih): Proper returning to one's family (or place of residence) after completing Umrah, which negates the continuous intention of Tamattu'
دم الجبر (dam al-jabr): Compensatory blood (dam) required due to a violation or sin in the ritual, as opposed to gratitude blood (dam al-shukr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's reconciliation, what is the ruling if a Makki performs Umrah in Hajj months intending to perform Hajj that same year?
A) His Tamattu' is invalid and no blood is required
B) His Tamattu' is valid but he is sinful and owes compensatory blood
C) His Tamattu' is valid and he owes gratitude blood
D) His Tamattu' is invalid but he still owes blood

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of Tamattu' for a Makki negates permissibility, not validity; if performed, it is sinful and requires compensatory blood.

Defining Proper Return (Ilmaam Sahih) and its Impact on Tamattu' for the Makki
Explaining the definition of proper returning and its role in Tamattu' validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ilmaam sahih and determine when a Makki's Tamattu' is valid or invalid based on the completion of Umrah.

Core Idea
Proper return requires returning to family with no ongoing Umrah obligation; lacking it makes Tamattu' invalid for the Makki.

This lesson unpacks the concept of 'ilmaam sahih' (proper return) as defined by the Hanafi school. The author of Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the validity of Tamattu' for a Makki hinges on this definition, which goes beyond mere physical return. Understanding this nuance resolves apparent contradictions within the madhhab and explains when a Makki's Tamattu' is considered valid but not recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is a Makki performing Tamattu' (performing Umrah during Hajj months then Hajj). The apparent ruling from the madhhab is that it is invalid, but the author explains this needs qualification.
The ruling concerns validity, not sinfulness.
2
Understand the concept of ilmaam sahih
Ilmaam sahih is defined as returning to one's family after Umrah with no ongoing obligation to perform another Umrah. This excludes cases where the person brings a sacrificial animal (hady) or does not shave, as these imply a continuing Umrah obligation.
The definition is from al-Muhit and al-Mi'raj.
3
Apply the condition to the Makki
If a Makki performs Umrah, shaves, does not bring hady, and returns to his family, he has ilmaam sahih. If he brings hady or does not shave, he is not properly returned, so his Tamattu' is invalid.
Staying in Makkah without returning to family also negates ilmaam sahih.
4
Distinguish between valid and recommended
The madhhab's statement that the Makki's Tamattu' is invalid refers to the recommended (masnun) Tamattu'. A valid but non-recommended Tamattu' is possible under the condition of ilmaam sahih.
This reconciles the apparent disagreement among scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما ذكره المؤلف هنا أن ظاهر الكتب عدم الصحة وكذا ما ذكره الكمال أن من مقتضى كلامهم ذلك وأنه أولى مما ذكره بعض المشايخ يعني به صاحب التحفة كما يأتي رده في الشرنبلالية بما اتفقوا عليه متوناً وشروحاً في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام من أن المكي لو أدخل إحرام الحج إلى آخر ما مر، وذكر أنه لا خلاف في صحة قران المكي وتمتعه وأن الكمال ناقض نفسه فيما يأتي وأطال في ذلك فراجعه متأملاً ورده أيضاً في شرح اللباب بما حاصله أن مراد أئمة المذهب بقولهم بطل تمتعه أي المسنون فلا ينافي ما ذكره بعض المشايخ من الصحة، وسيذكر المؤلف هذا التوفيق قريباً قوله : (قال في غاية البيان ولهذا قلنا الخ) لم يبين وجه عدم صحة القرآن وبينه الزيلعي بقوله : ولأن ميقات أهل مكة في الحج الحرم وفي العمرة الحل فلا يتصور الجمع بينهما فلا يشرع في حقهم القرآن. قوله : لوجود الإلمام الصحيح هذا خاص فيمن لم يسق الهدي وحلق أما إذا ساق الهدي أو لم يسق ولم يحلق للعمرة لم يكن ملماً بأهله إلماماً صحيحاً، فدعوى صاحب البدائع عدم تصور وجود تمتعه خاص بصورة ويتصور بصورتين كما ذكرنا نبه عليه في الشرنبلالية وكان مبنى ما ذكره تفسير الإلمام الصحيح بما مر عن العناية وليس كذلك، بل مبنى المسألة تفسيره بما قدمناه عن المعراج عن المحيط بأن يرجع إلى أهله عن العمرة ولا يكون الرجوع إلى العمرة مستحقاً عليه. ولهذا قال: وعن هذا قلنا لا تمتع لأهل مكة كما مر ومثله في النهاية، وإذا كان كذلك فالإلمام الصحيح موجود هنا لما قدمناه عن العناية أن المراد بالعود هو ما يكون عن الوطن إلى الحرم أو إلى مكة وليس ههنا بموجود لكونه في الحرم أو في مكة وعليه فعدم التصور في الثلاث مسلم تأمل قوله : (وما في البدائع الخ) اعلم أن عدم جواز العمرة للمكي قال في الفتح: إنه فاش بين حنيفة العصر من أهل مكة ونازعهم في
And what the author mentioned here is that the apparent meaning of the books is invalidity, and likewise what al-Kamal mentioned that the implication of their words is that, and it is more appropriate than what some shaykhs mentioned — meaning the author of al-Tuhfah — as its refutation will come in al-Shurnbulaliyyah according to what they agreed upon in texts and commentaries in the chapter of adding ihram to ihram: that if a Makki inserts the ihram of Hajj... up to what has passed. And he mentioned that there is no disagreement on the validity of the Makki's Qiran and Tamattu', and that al-Kamal contradicts himself later. He elaborated on that, so consult it carefully. He also refuted it in Sharh al-Lubab with the summary that the intent of the imams of the madhhab by their statement 'his Tamattu' is invalid' is the recommended (masnun) Tamattu', so it does not contradict what some shaykhs mentioned of validity. And the author will mention this reconciliation soon. His statement: (He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: For this reason we said...) He did not explain the reason for the invalidity of Qiran, and al-Zayla'i explained it by saying: Because the miqat of the people of Makkah for Hajj is the Haram, and for Umrah is the Hill, so the combination of the two is not conceivable, thus Qiran is not legislated for them. His statement: 'Due to the occurrence of proper returning' is specific to one who did not bring the sacrificial animal and shaved, but if he brought the sacrificial animal or did not bring it and did not shave for Umrah, he is not returning to his family in a proper manner. So the claim of the author of al-Bada'i' that his Tamattu' is inconceivable is specific to one scenario, and it is conceivable in two scenarios as we mentioned, as indicated in al-Shurnbulaliyyah. And the basis of what he mentioned is the interpretation of proper returning as per what came from al-Inayah, but it is not so. Rather, the basis of the issue is its interpretation as we presented from al-Mi'raj from al-Muhit: that he returns to his family from Umrah, and the return to Umrah is not obligatory upon him. For this reason he said: And on this basis we said there is no Tamattu' for the people of Makkah, as passed, and similar in al-Nihayah. And if that is the case, then proper returning exists here based on what we presented from al-Inayah that the intended meaning of 'return' is from the homeland to the Haram or to Makkah, and it is not present here because he is in the Haram or in Makkah. Therefore, the inconceivability in the three scenarios is granted. Ponder his statement: (And what is in al-Bada'i'...) Know that the impermissibility of Umrah for the Makki — al-Fath said: It is widespread among later Hanafis of the people of Makkah, and he disputed with them in...

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the definition of 'ilmaam sahih' (proper returning) and its effect on the validity of Tamattu' for the Makki. The author first notes that the apparent stance of the madhhab's books is that the Makki's Tamattu' is invalid, and this is supported by al-Kamal. However, some shaykhs (like the author of al-Tuhfah) hold that it is valid. The author mentions that a reconciliation will come, and then cites al-Zayla'i's explanation: Qiran is not valid for the Makki because the miqat for Hajj is the Haram and for Umrah is the Hill, so they cannot combine the two. Regarding ilmaam sahih, the author specifies that it applies only when the Makki does not bring a hady (sacrificial animal) and shaves. If he brings hady or does not shave, he is not considered to have returned properly. The author then critiques the position of al-Bada'i' that Tamattu' is inconceivable for the Makki, stating that it is conceivable in two scenarios. The correct definition of ilmaam sahih, according to al-Mi'raj and al-Muhit, is that the person returns to his family after Umrah without any ongoing obligation to return to Umrah. Finally, the author touches on the widespread difference among later Hanafis about the permissibility of Umrah for the Makki in the months of Hajj.

Key Terms
الإلمام الصحيح (al-ilmaam al-sahih): Returning to one's family after Umrah with no ongoing obligation to perform another Umrah
التمتع المسنون (al-tamattu' al-masnun): The recommended Tamattu', which is valid and merits gratitude blood; this is distinguished from a sinful but valid Tamattu' that requires compensatory blood

The Makki's Umrah During Hajj Months: Permissibility vs Prohibition
Dispute over whether a Makki may perform Umrah during Hajj months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a Makki may perform Umrah during the months of Hajj, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the permissibility and prohibition views.

Core Idea
A Makki's plain Umrah is permissible; only tamattu' and qiran are prohibited.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about a resident of Makkah (or those within the miqat boundaries) performing Umrah during the months of Hajj. The disagreement centers on whether plain Umrah is also prohibited or only the combined forms of tamattu' and qiran. Understanding the precise scope of the prohibition is essential for correct fatwa and avoiding unnecessary penalty (dam).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the mufta bihi (operative) view: a Makki is not prohibited from performing plain Umrah during the months of Hajj. Prohibition applies only to tamattu' and qiran.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognise that some Hanafi scholars (e.g., later view of al-Fath, and the people of Makkah according to al-Bada'i') hold that a Makki is prohibited from any Umrah during these months.
3
Follow the opposing proof
The opposing view relies on a tradition that Makkis should not perform Umrah during the Hajj season, interpreted broadly as a general prohibition.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority of later Hanafis interpret the prohibition narrowly: the Quranic verse (2:196) and relevant hadiths only restrict tamattu' and qiran, not plain Umrah. Umrah is an independent act of worship.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Makki performs plain Umrah and then Hajj in the same year, according to the prohibition view he owes a dam (damu jinayah); according to the permissibility view, no dam is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب التمتع عامه في البدائع من أن الاعتمار في أشهر الحج للمكي معصية محمول على ما إذا حج من وإذا قرن فإنه يكون آثماً أيضاً ويلزمه دم جناية. وفي الهداية بخلاف المكي إذا خرج إلى الكوفة وقرن حيث تصح لأن عمرته وحجته ميقاتيتان فصار بمنزلة الآفاقي. قال الشارحون : قيد بالقران لأنه لو تمتع فإنه لا يصح ويلزمه دم جناية لوجود الإلمام الصحيح بينهما فقد فرقوا بين التمتع والقرآن فشرطوا في التمتع عدم الإلمام دون القرآن ومقتضى الدليل أنه لا فرق بينهما في هذا الشرط وأن المكي يأثم إذا أحرم من الميقات بهما أو بالعمرة في أشهر الحج ثم حج من عامة لأن التمتع المذكور في الآية يعمهما كما قدمناه وإيجابهم دم الجناية على المكي إذا خرج إلى الميقات وتمتع مقتض لوجوب الدم على الآفاقي إذا تمتع وقد ألم بينهما إلماماً صحيحاً ولم يصرحوا به. وإنما قالوا بطل تمتعه والمراد بمن حولها من كال داخل المواقيت فإنهم بمنزلة أهل مكة وإن كان بينهم وبين مكة مسيرة سفر لأنهم في حكم حاضري المسجد الحرام. وفي النهاية : وأما القران من المكي فيكره ويلزمه الرفض والعمرة له في أشهر الحج لا تكره ولكن ذلك بعض الآفاقيين من الحنفية من قريب ومعتمد أهل مكة ما وقع في البدائع : والذي ذكره غير واحد خلافه ا هـ ملخصاً. فقد مال صاحب الفتح إلى الجواز لكن ذكر بعد ما حقق المقام أنه ظهر له بعد نحو ثلاثين سنة أن الوجه منع العمرة للمكي في أشهر الحج ، سواء حج من عامه ذلك أو لا، ثم بين وجهه. ورده في النهر كما قدمناه آنفاً، وكذا رده منلا علي في شرح اللباب ونقل التصريح بالجواز عن شرح الطحاوي وأطال في ذلك فراجعه وميل المؤلف إلى ذلك أيضاً فإنه بأنه لا صرح يكون آثماً، ثم أول عبارة البدائع والمسألة طويلة الذيل وقد أفردت بالتآليف وكثرت فيها الرسائل والتصانيف كما ذكره في حاشية المدني، وذكر حاصل الأقوال في ذلك فراجعها. هذا وقد ذكر في اللباب أن المتمتع لا يعتمر قبل الحج. قال في شارحه : هذا بناء على أن المكي ممنوع من العمرة المفردة أيضاً، وقد سبق أنه غير صحيح بل إنه ممنوع من التمتع والقرآن، وهذا المتمتع آفاقي غير ممنوع من العمرة فجاز له تكرارها لأنها عبادة مستقلة أيضاً كالطواف ا هـ . وفي حاشية المدني أن ما في اللباب مسلم في حق المتمتع السائق للهدي أما غير السائق فلا لأنه خلاف مذهب أصحابنا جميعاً لأن العمرة جائزة في جميع السنة بلا كراهة إلا في خمسة أيام لا فرق في ذلك بين المكي والآفاقي كما صرح به في النهاية والمبسوط والبحر وأخي زاد والعلامة قاسم وغيرهم ا هـ
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Tamattu'. In al-Bada'i': that performing Umrah in the months of Hajj for a Makki is a sin, interpreted as when he performs Hajj from [his place] and if he performs Qiran, then he is also sinful and a dam of penalty is obligatory upon him. In al-Hidayah: contrary to a Makki if he goes out to Kufa and performs Qiran, it is valid because his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, so he becomes like an afaqi. The commentators said: He restricted it to Qiran because if he performed Tamattu', it would not be valid and a dam of penalty would be obligatory upon him due to the existence of a valid returning (ilam) between them. Thus they distinguished between Tamattu' and Qiran, stipulating for Tamattu' the absence of ilam but not for Qiran. The evidence suggests no distinction between them in this condition, and that the Makki is sinful if he assumes ihram from the miqat for both, or for Umrah in the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year, because the Tamattu' mentioned in the verse includes both. And their making obligatory the dam of penalty on the Makki if he goes out to the miqat and performs Tamattu' necessitates the obligation of a dam on the afaqi if he performs Tamattu' and has a valid ilam between them, but they did not state that explicitly. They only said his Tamattu' is invalid. And the meaning of 'those around it' like those inside the miqat boundaries, they are like the people of Makkah, even if between them and Makkah there is a journey distance, because they are ruled as residents of the Sacred Mosque. In al-Nihayah: As for Qiran from a Makki, it is disliked and he must reject [one], and Umrah for him in the months of Hajj is not disliked. But some of the afaqi Hanafis [hold a different view] from recent times, and the relied-upon position of the people of Makkah is what is in al-Bada'i'; what others have mentioned is contrary. Summarized. The author of al-Fath inclined to permissibility, but after investigating the matter he stated that after about thirty years it became clear to him that the correct view is to prohibit Umrah for a Makki in the months of Hajj, whether he performs Hajj in that year or not, then he explained his reasoning. It was refuted in al-Nahr as we presented earlier, and similarly Mulla Ali in Sharh al-Lubab refuted it, and he transmitted explicit permissibility from Sharh al-Tahawi and elaborated. So refer to it. The author [of al-Bahr] also inclined to that, because he stated explicitly that he is not sinful, and then he interpreted the statement of al-Bada'i'. The matter is lengthy and has been treated in separate works, and many treatises and books have been written about it, as mentioned in Hashiyat al-Madani. He presented the gist of the opinions, so refer to them. It has been mentioned in al-Lubab that the mutamatti' does not perform Umrah before Hajj. The commentator said: This is based on the view that a Makki is also prohibited from a single Umrah, and it has preceded that this is incorrect; rather he is prohibited from Tamattu' and Qiran, and this mutamatti' is an afaqi, not prohibited from Umrah, so it is permissible for him to repeat it because it is an independent act of worship like tawaf. In Hashiyat al-Madani: What is in al-Lubab is acceptable for the mutamatti' who drives a hady; as for one who does not drive, it is against the madhhab of all our companions, because Umrah is permissible throughout the whole year without dislike except on five days, with no distinction between a Makki and an afaqi, as explicitly stated in al-Nihayah, al-Mabsut, al-Bahr, Akhi Zad, Allamah Qasim, and others.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a Makki (resident of Makkah) may perform Umrah during the months of Hajj. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq first reports from al-Bada'i' that performing Umrah in these months for a Makki is a sin, but this is restricted to when he also performs Hajj in that year (i.e., tamattu' or qiran). If he does tamattu', he is also sinful and owes a dam. However, al-Hidayah states that if a Makki goes out to Kufa (i.e., leaves the Haram area) and performs Qiran from the miqat, it is valid because both his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, making him like an afaqi. The commentators note that the ruling is restricted to Qiran; for Tamattu', it would be invalid because the valid 'ilam (returning to one's homeland between Umrah and Hajj) would break the continuity required for tamattu'. They then question the distinction between tamattu' and qiran in this condition, arguing that the same principle should apply: the Makki is sinful in both cases. The passage then surveys the disagreement among later Hanafi scholars: some (like the author of al-Fath) initially permitted Umrah for a Makki, but later changed to prohibition. Others (like al-Nahr, Mulla Ali) maintain permissibility. The author of al-Bahr seems to incline toward permissibility, stating that the Makki is not sinful. The issue is further complicated by the status of those living within the miqat boundaries (e.g., Jeddah, Taif) who are considered like Makkis in this ruling. Finally, the passage addresses the ruling for an afaqi mutamatti': he is not prohibited from performing Umrah before Hajj, and may repeat Umrah, since it is an independent act of worship. The only restriction for everyone is the five days (Day of Arafah, Day of Nahr, and three days of Tashreeq) when Umrah is disliked. This passage illustrates the nuanced ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school and the importance of distinguishing between tamattu', qiran, and plain Umrah for a Makki.

Key Terms
المكي (al-makki): A person who is a resident of Makkah or within the miqat boundaries (e.g., Jeddah), such that they are considered from the people of the Haram.
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah during the months of Hajj and then performing Hajj in the same year without returning to the miqat, with a hady.
القران (al-qiran): Entering into ihram for both Umrah and Hajj simultaneously or within the same state of ihram.
دم جناية (damu jinayah): A penalty dam (slaughter of a sheep) for committing a prohibited act (makruh tahrimi) during ihram, such as combining Umrah and Hajj incorrectly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in al-Bahr al-Raiq, is a Makki sinful if he performs Umrah alone (not tamattu' or qiran) during the months of Hajj?
A) Yes, it is sinful and requires a dam.
B) No, it is not sinful and no dam is required.
C) It is permissible only if he does not perform Hajj afterwards.
D) It is makruh but not sinful.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a Makki may perform plain Umrah during the months of Hajj, but tamattu' and qiran are prohibited.

A Makki's Qiran After Leaving Makkah: Validity and Dispute
Ruling on Makki's qiran after leaving Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a Makki who goes out to the miqat and performs qiran, explain the condition of Imam al-Mahbubi regarding the months of Hajj, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
A Makki who leaves Makkah becomes an afaqi for qiran, but validity may depend on leaving before Hajj months.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a nuance in al-Hidayah: a Makki who goes to the miqat and assumes ihram for qiran is considered like an afaqi only if he has left the Haram before the Hajj months begin. Imam al-Mahbubi restricts the absolute statement of al-Hidayah, and later authorities consider his view correct. The practical consequence is that if a Makki leaves after the months have started, his qiran is invalid according to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
A Makki (resident of Makkah) goes out to the miqat (e.g., Kufa) and performs qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj with one ihram). The ruling is debated.
The act is qiran, not tamattu'.
2
State the apparent ruling from al-Hidayah
The Hidayah says the Makki becomes like an afaqi, so his qiran is valid absolutely, with no conditions.
This is based on the idea that both Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat.
3
Identify al-Mahbubi's condition
Imam al-Mahbubi held that the qiran is valid only if the Makki left Makkah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, Dhul-Hijjah) began. If he was in Makkah when the months started, he is prohibited from qiran even after going to the miqat.
The prohibition persists because he is still a Makki for the purpose of Hajj.
4
Analyze the proof structure
Al-Hidayah argues 'by going out he becomes an afaqi'. Al-Mahbubi responds that the prohibition on qiran for a Makki is established before he leaves, and leaving does not remove it.
The difference hinges on whether the prohibition is 'aynī (persisting) or zā'il (removable by travel).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
Later authorities (al-Kirmani, al-Shalabi, al-Sharnabali) accepted al-Mahbubi's view as correct. Therefore, the relied-upon position is that a Makki's qiran is valid only if he left before the Hajj months.
Practical consequence: If a Makki leaves Makkah on 1st Dhul-Qa'dah, his qiran is valid; if he leaves after staying through Shawwal, it is invalid and he must reject one (rafd).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي الهداية بخلاف المكي الخ متصل بقوله وليس لأهل مكة تمتع ولا قرآن» كذا قال الشراح قوله: (ومقتضى الدليل أنه لا فرق بينهما اعترضه السندي في منسكه الكبير بأن الإلمام الصحيح المبطل للحكم لا يتصور في حق القارن، وأما الإلمام الفاسد بقاء الإحرام فهو لا يبطل التمتع المشروط فيه عدم الإلمام فلا يبطل القرآن بالأولى ا هـ ملخصاً. وقوله المكي «يأثم الخ» أقول: فيه تطر يوضحه قول الهداية السابق لأن عمرته وحجته ميقاتيان أي بخلاف ما إذا تمتع بعد ما خرج إلى الكوفة فإنه لا يصح لأنه وإن كان إحرامه للعمرة آفاقياً لكن إحرامه للحج مكي، فهو حينئذ من أهل المسجد الحرام. وأما القارن فلا لما علمت فلم تشمل الآية هذا المكي القارن لأنه بخروجه صار آفاقياً، وإنما تشمل من لم يخرج هذا ما ظهر لي فتدبره قوله : (وإيجابهم دم الجناية على المكي الخ) قد علمت أن المكي إذا خرج إلى الميقات وتمتع لم يصر بمنزلة الآفاقي لأن حجته مكية ويصير آثماً كما قدمه والدم الواجب عليه . جناية لما ارتكبه من النهي وهذا لم يوجد في الآفاقي أصلاً لأنه ليس مكياً. ثم إن وجوب الدم على المكي مبني على صحة تمتعه كما مر والآفاقي إذا ألم بأهله ثم حج لم يكن متمتعاً إذا لم يسق الهدي؛ فقوله إذا تمتع غير ظاهر فإيجاب الدم عليه إن كان لمخالفة النهي فلا وجه له لما علمت أنه ليس مكياً بل ليس متمتعاً أصلاً وإن كان لمجرد إلمامه بأهله بعد عمرته فلا وجه له أيضاً لما سيأتي في الصفحة الثانية أنه لو بعث الهدي وتعجل ذبحه قبل يوم النحر وألم بأهله فلا شيء عليه مطلقاً، سواء حج من عامه أو لا، وفي مسألتنا إن لم يسق الهدي فلا شيء عليه بالأولى قوله : (والعمرة له في أشهر الحج لا تكره الخ هذا مخالف لما سبق في الحاصل قوله: (وبينه في المحيط) وسيأتي بيانه أيضاً في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام والذي مشى عليه المصنف هناك إن المرفوض الحج قوله : (وعليه عمرة ودم أي دم للرفض وهو دم جبر. كذا في اللباب قوله : (وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن الظاهر الإطلاق (الخ أقول : نقل في الشرنبلالية كلام المحبوبي عن العناية ثم قال : وقول المحبوبي هو الصحيح نقله الشيخ الشلبي عن الكرماني ا هـ . وعليه فإطلاق كلام الهداية فيما تقدم مقيد بما ذكره المحبوبي تأمل
His statement: 'And in al-Hidayah, contrary to a Makki, etc.' is connected to his statement 'And for the people of Makkah there is no tamattu' nor qiran.' Thus said the commentators. His statement: 'And the evidence suggests no difference between them.' Al-Sindi in his Manasik al-Kabir objected to this by saying that a valid ilam which invalidates the ruling is not conceivable in the case of a qarin; as for the invalid ilam remaining in ihram, it does not invalidate tamattu' which is conditioned on the absence of ilam, so a fortiori it does not invalidate qiran. Summarized. And his statement: 'The Makki is sinful' I say: there is a [gap] clarified by the earlier statement of al-Hidayah because his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, i.e., contrary to if he performed tamattu' after going out to Kufa, then it is not valid because even though his ihram for Umrah is of an afaqi, his ihram for Hajj is of a Makki, so he is then from the people of the Sacred Mosque. As for the qarin, no, because you know; so the verse does not include this Makki qarin because by going out he became an afaqi; it only includes one who did not go out. This is what appeared to me, so ponder it. His statement: 'And their making mandatory the dam of penalty on the Makki, etc.' You have known that when a Makki goes out to the miqat and performs tamattu', he does not become like an afaqi because his Hajj is Makkan and he becomes sinful as stated earlier, and the dam obligatory on him is a penalty for committing the prohibition. This does not occur in the afaqi at all because he is not a Makki. Then, the obligation of the dam on the Makki is based on the validity of his tamattu' as mentioned, and the afaqi if he returns to his family and then performs Hajj, he is not a mutamatti' if he does not drive a hady; so his statement 'if he performs tamattu' is not apparent. So obligating the dam on him, if it is for violating the prohibition, has no basis since you know he is not a Makki, rather he is not a mutamatti' at all. And if it is merely for his return to his family after his Umrah, it also has no basis because, as will come on the second page, if he sent the hady and hastened to slaughter it before the Day of Nahr and then returned to his family, there is no obligation upon him at all, whether he performs Hajj in that year or not. In our issue, if he did not drive the hady, then there is nothing upon him a fortiori. His statement: 'And Umrah for him in the months of Hajj is not disliked' contradicts what preceded. In summary, his statement: 'And he explained it in al-Muhit' and its explanation will also come in the chapter on adding ihram to ihram, and the author there followed that the rejected one is Hajj. His statement: 'And upon him is an Umrah and a dam' means a dam for rejection, which is a compensatory dam. Thus in al-Lubab. His statement: 'And he criticized it in Fath al-Qadir by saying the apparent meaning is absolute [unrestricted]' I say: In al-Sharnabaliyya it is transmitted from al-`Inayah the words of al-Mahbubi, then he said: 'The statement of al-Mahbubi is correct, as transmitted by al-Shalabi from al-Kirmani.' Therefore, the absolute statement of al-Hidayah in what preceded is restricted by what al-Mahbubi mentioned. Reflect.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage is an expansion and clarification of the ruling for a Makki who leaves Makkah and performs Hajj from the miqat. The text addresses several issues: First, the validity of qiran for a Makki who goes out to a place like Kufa and assumes ihram from the miqat. According to al-Hidayah, this is valid because both his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, making him like an afaqi. However, if he performs tamattu' after going out, it is invalid because his Hajj ihram is still that of a Makki (he is still considered a resident of the Haram for Hajj). Second, the passage discusses the procedure (rafd) if a Makki mistakenly combines Umrah and Hajj (qiran) after going out. The detail is from al-Muhit: he must reject one of the two. If he has done only a few tawaf for Umrah, he rejects Umrah; if he has done more, he completes both with a dam. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether to reject Umrah or Hajj when only three tawaf are done. Third, the passage examines a condition from Imam al-Mahbubi: the permissibility of qiran for a Makki who goes out only applies if he leaves the miqat before the months of Hajj begin. If he is in Makkah when the months start, he becomes prohibited from qiran, and his subsequent ihram from the miqat does not change that. This condition is debated; al-Fath al-Qadir argues for absolute permissibility, but the author of al-Bahr inclines to al-Mahbubi's view as correct. The passage also clarifies the nature of the dam for a Makki who invalidly performs tamattu' as a penalty dam (dam jinaya) for violating a prohibition. The commentary emphasizes that the rulings for a Makki are distinct from those for an afaqi.

Key Terms
الإلمام (al-ilamam): Returning to one's family between Umrah and Hajj in tamattu'.
دم جناية (dam jinaya): A penalty dam for violating a prohibition, e.g., when a Makki performs tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, when does a Makki's qiran after going to the miqat become invalid?
A) Always invalid because a Makki cannot perform qiran.
B) Invalid only if he returns to Makkah after Umrah.
C) Invalid if he was in Makkah when the Hajj months began.
D) Invalid if he performs less than three tawaf for Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A Makki who leaves Makkah to perform qiran is valid only if he left before the months of Hajj began; otherwise his qiran is invalid and requires rafd.

Rafd: Procedure for a Makki Who Invalidly Combines Umrah and Hajj
Procedure for rafd and dam for a Makki's invalid qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the procedure for rafd (rejecting one ihram) when a Makki improperly performs qiran, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on which ihram to reject.

Core Idea
A Makki who invalidly performs qiran must reject one ihram; if three tawaf were done, he completes both with a dam, but scholars differ on which to reject.

When a Makki performs qiran after the prohibition (e.g., after staying in Makkah through Shawwal), his ihram is invalid. Al-Muhit details the corrective procedure: he must reject (rafd) one of the two ihrams. The number of tawaf performed for Umrah determines the ruling. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on whether to reject Umrah or Hajj when three tawaf have been completed. This lesson explains the procedure and the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the precondition for rafd
Rafd is required when a Makki performs qiran in a state where it is invalid (e.g., after being in Makkah during Hajj months).
This is a corrective action, not a regular act.
2
Apply the rule from al-Muhit based on tawaf count
If the Makki has done fewer than three tawaf for Umrah, he rejects Umrah and continues with Hajj. If he has done three or more tawaf, he must complete both Umrah and Hajj with a dam.
Three tawaf is the threshold; the reasoning is that after three tawaf, the Umrah is considered 'strongly attached'.
3
Identify the ikhtilaf on which to reject when three tawaf are done
Abu Hanifa said: reject Hajj (and complete Umrah with a dam). The Sahibayn said: reject Umrah (and complete Hajj with a dam). This affects the dam and which actions are completed.
The difference is based on which ihram takes priority.
4
State the nature of the dam
The dam required is 'dam jabar' (compensatory dam) for the deficiency caused by rejecting one ihram.
It is not a penalty dam (dam jinaya) but a compensatory one.

Source Text

قوله : (وفي الهداية بخلاف المكي الخ متصل بقوله وليس لأهل مكة تمتع ولا قرآن» كذا قال الشراح قوله: (ومقتضى الدليل أنه لا فرق بينهما اعترضه السندي في منسكه الكبير بأن الإلمام الصحيح المبطل للحكم لا يتصور في حق القارن، وأما الإلمام الفاسد بقاء الإحرام فهو لا يبطل التمتع المشروط فيه عدم الإلمام فلا يبطل القرآن بالأولى ا هـ ملخصاً. وقوله المكي «يأثم الخ» أقول: فيه تطر يوضحه قول الهداية السابق لأن عمرته وحجته ميقاتيان أي بخلاف ما إذا تمتع بعد ما خرج إلى الكوفة فإنه لا يصح لأنه وإن كان إحرامه للعمرة آفاقياً لكن إحرامه للحج مكي، فهو حينئذ من أهل المسجد الحرام. وأما القارن فلا لما علمت فلم تشمل الآية هذا المكي القارن لأنه بخروجه صار آفاقياً، وإنما تشمل من لم يخرج هذا ما ظهر لي فتدبره قوله : (وإيجابهم دم الجناية على المكي الخ) قد علمت أن المكي إذا خرج إلى الميقات وتمتع لم يصر بمنزلة الآفاقي لأن حجته مكية ويصير آثماً كما قدمه والدم الواجب عليه . جناية لما ارتكبه من النهي وهذا لم يوجد في الآفاقي أصلاً لأنه ليس مكياً. ثم إن وجوب الدم على المكي مبني على صحة تمتعه كما مر والآفاقي إذا ألم بأهله ثم حج لم يكن متمتعاً إذا لم يسق الهدي؛ فقوله إذا تمتع غير ظاهر فإيجاب الدم عليه إن كان لمخالفة النهي فلا وجه له لما علمت أنه ليس مكياً بل ليس متمتعاً أصلاً وإن كان لمجرد إلمامه بأهله بعد عمرته فلا وجه له أيضاً لما سيأتي في الصفحة الثانية أنه لو بعث الهدي وتعجل ذبحه قبل يوم النحر وألم بأهله فلا شيء عليه مطلقاً، سواء حج من عامه أو لا، وفي مسألتنا إن لم يسق الهدي فلا شيء عليه بالأولى قوله : (والعمرة له في أشهر الحج لا تكره الخ هذا مخالف لما سبق في الحاصل قوله: (وبينه في المحيط) وسيأتي بيانه أيضاً في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام والذي مشى عليه المصنف هناك إن المرفوض الحج قوله : (وعليه عمرة ودم أي دم للرفض وهو دم جبر. كذا في اللباب قوله : (وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن الظاهر الإطلاق (الخ أقول : نقل في الشرنبلالية كلام المحبوبي عن العناية ثم قال : وقول المحبوبي هو الصحيح نقله الشيخ الشلبي عن الكرماني ا هـ . وعليه فإطلاق كلام الهداية فيما تقدم مقيد بما ذكره المحبوبي تأمل
His statement: 'And in al-Hidayah, contrary to a Makki, etc.' is connected to his statement 'And for the people of Makkah there is no tamattu' nor qiran.' Thus said the commentators. His statement: 'And the evidence suggests no difference between them.' Al-Sindi in his Manasik al-Kabir objected to this by saying that a valid ilam which invalidates the ruling is not conceivable in the case of a qarin; as for the invalid ilam remaining in ihram, it does not invalidate tamattu' which is conditioned on the absence of ilam, so a fortiori it does not invalidate qiran. Summarized. And his statement: 'The Makki is sinful' I say: there is a [gap] clarified by the earlier statement of al-Hidayah because his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, i.e., contrary to if he performed tamattu' after going out to Kufa, then it is not valid because even though his ihram for Umrah is of an afaqi, his ihram for Hajj is of a Makki, so he is then from the people of the Sacred Mosque. As for the qarin, no, because you know; so the verse does not include this Makki qarin because by going out he became an afaqi; it only includes one who did not go out. This is what appeared to me, so ponder it. His statement: 'And their making mandatory the dam of penalty on the Makki, etc.' You have known that when a Makki goes out to the miqat and performs tamattu', he does not become like an afaqi because his Hajj is Makkan and he becomes sinful as stated earlier, and the dam obligatory on him is a penalty for committing the prohibition. This does not occur in the afaqi at all because he is not a Makki. Then, the obligation of the dam on the Makki is based on the validity of his tamattu' as mentioned, and the afaqi if he returns to his family and then performs Hajj, he is not a mutamatti' if he does not drive a hady; so his statement 'if he performs tamattu' is not apparent. So obligating the dam on him, if it is for violating the prohibition, has no basis since you know he is not a Makki, rather he is not a mutamatti' at all. And if it is merely for his return to his family after his Umrah, it also has no basis because, as will come on the second page, if he sent the hady and hastened to slaughter it before the Day of Nahr and then returned to his family, there is no obligation upon him at all, whether he performs Hajj in that year or not. In our issue, if he did not drive the hady, then there is nothing upon him a fortiori. His statement: 'And Umrah for him in the months of Hajj is not disliked' contradicts what preceded. In summary, his statement: 'And he explained it in al-Muhit' and its explanation will also come in the chapter on adding ihram to ihram, and the author there followed that the rejected one is Hajj. His statement: 'And upon him is an Umrah and a dam' means a dam for rejection, which is a compensatory dam. Thus in al-Lubab. His statement: 'And he criticized it in Fath al-Qadir by saying the apparent meaning is absolute [unrestricted]' I say: In al-Sharnabaliyya it is transmitted from al-`Inayah the words of al-Mahbubi, then he said: 'The statement of al-Mahbubi is correct, as transmitted by al-Shalabi from al-Kirmani.' Therefore, the absolute statement of al-Hidayah in what preceded is restricted by what al-Mahbubi mentioned. Reflect.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage is an expansion and clarification of the ruling for a Makki who leaves Makkah and performs Hajj from the miqat. The text addresses several issues: First, the validity of qiran for a Makki who goes out to a place like Kufa and assumes ihram from the miqat. According to al-Hidayah, this is valid because both his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat, making him like an afaqi. However, if he performs tamattu' after going out, it is invalid because his Hajj ihram is still that of a Makki (he is still considered a resident of the Haram for Hajj). Second, the passage discusses the procedure (rafd) if a Makki mistakenly combines Umrah and Hajj (qiran) after going out. The detail is from al-Muhit: he must reject one of the two. If he has done only a few tawaf for Umrah, he rejects Umrah; if he has done more, he completes both with a dam. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether to reject Umrah or Hajj when only three tawaf are done. Third, the passage examines a condition from Imam al-Mahbubi: the permissibility of qiran for a Makki who goes out only applies if he leaves the miqat before the months of Hajj begin. If he is in Makkah when the months start, he becomes prohibited from qiran, and his subsequent ihram from the miqat does not change that. This condition is debated; al-Fath al-Qadir argues for absolute permissibility, but the author of al-Bahr inclines to al-Mahbubi's view as correct. The passage also clarifies the nature of the dam for a Makki who invalidly performs tamattu' as a penalty dam (dam jinaya) for violating a prohibition. The commentary emphasizes that the rulings for a Makki are distinct from those for an afaqi.

Key Terms
الرفض (al-rafd): The act of abandoning one of the two ihrams (Umrah or Hajj) when a Makki improperly combines them.
دم جبر (damu jabar): A compensatory dam for making up for a deficiency or violation, such as rejecting an ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, what should a Makki do if he performed invalid qiran and has completed four tawaf for Umrah?
A) Reject Umrah and continue with Hajj.
B) Reject Hajj and complete Umrah with a dam jabar.
C) Complete both with two dams.
D) Reject both ihrams and perform Hajj individually.

Key Takeaway
A Makki who invalidly performs qiran must reject one ihram based on tawaf count; the mufta bihi view (Abu Hanifa) is to reject Hajj when three or more tawaf are done, with a compensatory dam.

Effect of Returning Home on Tamattu' and the Hady
Ruling on ilam and hady in tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mutamatti' returning home after Umrah, explain the condition of driving a hady, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
A mutamatti's tamattu' is invalid if he returns home without a hady; driving a hady preserves it — but Imam Muhammad disagrees.

Tamattu' is a valid form of Hajj where Umrah is performed first in the Hajj months, and then Hajj is performed in the same year. However, if the pilgrim returns to his homeland after the Umrah, his tamattu' is at risk. This lesson clarifies the precise ruling, the condition that can save it, and a notable disagreement within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Identify the act under discussion: a mutamatti' who performs Umrah in the Hajj months and returns to his homeland before Hajj. The default ruling: his tamattu' becomes invalid unless a specific condition is met.
2
Recognize the condition that preserves validity
The condition is driving a hady (sacrificial animal) from the miqat to the Haram. If the pilgrim drove the hady, returning home does not invalidate his tamattu'. If he did not, it becomes invalid.
This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that tamattu' is invalid in both cases—even if a hady is driven. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) differ, and their view is the mufta bihi.
Thus the ruling depends on which riwayah is followed.
4
Understand the terminological subtlety
The phrase 'his tamattu' becomes invalid' is a common metaphor. Strictly, if the condition is missing, tamattu' never existed. The more precise expression is 'he is not a mutamatti'.'
This is noted by al-Nahr and defended by the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with critical commentary on the effect of returning to one's homeland (ilam) after Umrah in tamattu'. The core rule: If a mutamatti' returns to his hometown after performing Umrah but before Hajj, his tamattu' becomes invalid unless he has driven a hady (sacrificial animal). If he did drive a hady, his tamattu' remains valid. This distinction is attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that tamattu' is invalid regardless of driving a hady. The author then discusses the nature of the dam for a Makki who performs tamattu' incorrectly: it is a penalty dam (dam jinaya) because he violated a prohibition. For an afaqi, if he returns to his family without driving a hady, he is not a mutamatti' at all. The passage also addresses a terminological subtlety: al-Nahr criticizes the author's phrasing 'his tamattu' becomes invalid' because tamattu' never existed if the condition (not returning) was absent; it would be more precise to say 'he is not a mutamatti'.' However, the author defends this as a common figurative expression. The passage ends by reiterating the condition of al-Mahbubi that restricts the absolute statement of al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
ساق الهدي (saqa al-hady): Driving a sacrificial animal (hady) from the miqat to the Haram, particularly relevant for tamattu' and qiran.
دم الشكر (damu al-shukr): A thank offering dam required for tamattu' and qiran when the pilgrim combines Umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is required for a mutamatti' to retain the validity of his tamattu' after returning to his homeland?
A) He must perform a second Umrah upon returning.
B) He must drive a hady from the miqat.
C) He must stay in the Haram area for at least one month.
D) He must sacrifice the hady before leaving.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who returns home after Umrah must have driven a hady for his tamattu' to remain valid according to the majority Hanafi position.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Effect of Driving a Sacrificial Animal (Sawq al-Hady) on Tamattu'
Examines ruling on sawq al-hady and its effect on tamattu' and returning to family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sawq al-hady in tamattu', distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding returning to family, and calculate the blood sacrifices required in various scenarios.

Core Idea
Driving a hady restricts tahlil until sacrifice; if one returns to family early, tamattu' may still be valid with additional blood.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the interaction between driving a sacrificial animal (sawq al-hady) and the pilgrimage type of tamattu'. It resolves the effect on the pilgrim's ability to exit ihram and the necessity of returning home between 'Umrah and Hajj. The text presents the Hanafi ruling, the internal ikhtilaf between the imams, and the preferred view of later authorities.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic rule of sawq al-hady
When a pilgrim drives a sacrificial animal (hady) for tamattu', this act commits him to complete Hajj that year and prevents him from shaving (tahlil) until the animal is sacrificed on the Day of Nahr. If he abandons the intention before entering ihram for Hajj, no penalty applies.
This ruling is from the core Hanafi texts (Zahir al-Riwayah).
2
Identify the three scenarios
The passage presents three cases depending on when the hady is slaughtered and whether the pilgrim returns to his family: (1) leaves the hady until the Day of Nahr, (2) slaughters early and returns to family, (3) slaughters early and does not return.
Each scenario has a different blood requirement.
3
Determine the blood obligations for each scenario
If the hady is left until the Day of Nahr, tamattu' is valid with no extra blood. If slaughtered early and the pilgrim returns to his family, no blood is required (whether he performs Hajj or not). If he does not return and then performs Hajj, two bloods are due: one for tamattu' and one for shaving before its time.
The second blood (dam al-hill qabla awanihi) is specific to this case.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf on returning to family (al-'awd)
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider returning to family between 'Umrah and Hajj as necessary (mustahaqq) for tamattu' to be valid without extra penalty. Abu Yusuf holds it is recommended (mustahabb). The preferred view (mufta bihi), as cited in Fath al-Qadir, follows the Shafi'i opinion that return is not a condition at all.
This ikhtilaf affects whether an additional dam is required if one does not return.
5
Note the tarjih in later authorities
Fath al-Qadir prefers the Shafi'i view, making the mufta bihi that tamattu' is valid regardless of returning to family, and no extra blood is due solely for not returning.
This tarjih overrides the stricter view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

في الابتداء، وإن أراد أن ينحر هديه ويحل ولا يرجع إلى أهله ويحج من عامه ذلك لم يكن له ذلك لأنه مقيم على عزم التمتع فيمنعه الهدي من الإحلال فإن فعله ثم رجع إلى أهله ثم حج لا شيء عليه لأنه غير متمتع. ولو حل بمكة ونحر هديه ثم حج قبل أن يرجع إلى أهله لزمه دم لتمتعه لأنه لم يلم بأهله فيما بين النسكين وعليه دم آخر لأنه حل قبل يوم النحر ا هـ . فالحاصل أنه إذا ساق الهدي لا يخلو إما أن يتركه إلى يوم النحر أو لا، فإن تركه إليه فتمتعه صحيح ولا شيء عليه غيره، سواء عاد إلى أهله أو لا، وإن تعجل ذبحه فأما إن رجع إلى أهله أو لا، فإن رجع إلى أهله فلا شيء عليه مطلقاً سواء حج من عامه أو لا، وإن لم يرجع إليهم فإن لم يحج من عامه فلا شيء عليه، وإن حج منه لزمه دمان المتعة ودم الحل قبل أوانه . ورجح في فتح القدير مذهب الشافعي في أن عدم الإلمام بينهما ليس بشرط في التمتع فلا يبطل تمتعه بعوده إلى أهله، سواء ساق الهدي أو لا، لأن الآية إنما منعت التمتع لمن كان حاضر المسجد الحرام لا لأجل إلمامهم بأهلهم بينهما بل لتيسر العمرة لهم في كل وقت بخلاف الغير. قيد بقوله بعد العمرة لأنه لو عاد بعد ما طاف لها الأقل لا يبطل تمتعه لأن العود مستحق عليه لأنه ألم بأهله محرماً بخلاف ما إذا طاف الأكثر . ودخل في قوله بعد العمرة» الحلق فلا بد للبطلان منه لأنه من واجباتها وبه التحلل فلو عاد بعد طوافها قبل الحلق ثم حج من عامه قبل أن يحلق في أهله فهو متمتع لأن العود مستحق عليه عند من جعل الحرم شرط جواز الحلق وهو أبو حنيفة ومحمد، وعند أبي يوسف إن لم يكن مستحقاً فهو مستحب . كذا في البدائع وغيره
The Book of Hajj, Chapter of Tamattu': (The text discusses conditions for tamattu', including driving of sacrificial animals, returning to family, and the time of 'Umrah. It states that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, returning after performing the lesser part of tawaf does not nullify tamattu', while after the greater part it does. Abu Yusuf considers it recommended. The final ruling is summarized in various scenarios.)
Source pages p. 644

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rulings related to tamattu' (performing 'Umrah and then Hajj in the same year with a break). The author begins by noting that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Then he discusses the effect of driving a sacrificial animal (sawq al-hady). The majority opinion (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that driving the hady obligates the pilgrim to return to his family? Actually the text explains that driving the hady is a commitment to complete Hajj that year, but if one changes one's mind before entering ihram for Hajj, there is no penalty. However, if one remains intent on tamattu', the hady prevents tahlil (shaving to exit ihram) until the sacrifice on the Day of Nahr. The passage then details various scenarios: if the hady is left until the Day of Nahr, tamattu' is valid; if slaughtered early and one returns to family, no blood is required; if one does not return and does not perform Hajj, no blood; but if one does Hajj without returning, two dems are due—one for tamattu' and one for shaving before its time. The passage also mentions that in Fath al-Qadir, the author prefers the Shafi'i view that not returning to one's family is not a condition for tamattu', citing the Quranic verse which prevents tamattu' for residents of Masjid al-Haram due to ease of performing 'Umrah, not due to family visitation. Finally, the passage notes the difference between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding the obligation of returning to family: the former deem it necessary (mustahaqq) while the latter considers it recommended (mustahabb).

Key Terms
سوق الهدي (sawq al-hady): Driving a sacrificial animal (usually a camel or cow) before or during the pilgrimage as an offering.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah during the Hajj months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) and then performing Hajj in the same year with a temporary break (returning to one's family or not).
العود (al-'awd): Returning to one's homeland or family between 'Umrah and Hajj ceremonies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a pilgrim drives a hady for tamattu', slaughters it early, and does NOT return to his family, but then performs Hajj that same year, what blood(s) are required?
A) No blood is required.
B) One dam for tamattu'.
C) Two dams: one for tamattu' and one for shaving before its time.
D) One dam for shaving before its time.

Key Takeaway
Driving a hady does not require returning to family; the mufta bihi is that tamattu' is valid regardless of return, and blood obligations depend on the timing of sacrifice and shaving.

Tamattu' Condition: Tawaf Timing in Hajj Months
Explains conditions for tamattu' based on tawaf timing and provides legal stratagems

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for tamattu' regarding tawaf timing and apply the Hanafi principle that the ruling of the majority of actions equals the whole.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires that most tawaf circuits occur in Hajj months; timing of ihram is irrelevant.

Tamattu' is a concession allowing Muslims to combine Umrah and Hajj in one journey without a separate trip. The timing of the Umrah's tawaf is crucial: if the majority of circuits fall outside the months of Hajj, the concession does not apply. This lesson unpacks that rule and provides a legal stratagem to preserve tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key principle
The passage establishes a general principle: for actions related to ihram, the ruling of the majority of an action is like the ruling of the whole. This is applied to tawaf.
This is a usul-like principle: 'al-akthar ka-al-kull' in legal effect.
2
Apply to tawaf timing
The condition for tamattu' is that the Umrah's tawaf must be performed predominantly within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, Dhul Hijjah). Even if ihram was entered earlier, the tawaf's timing determines tamattu'.
Contrast: the Shafi'i position makes ihram timing relevant.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage discusses whether repeating a deficient tawaf (e.g., by a muhdith) invalidates the first. The majority (including al-Karkhi) holds that the first remains, so tamattu' fails if the first tawaf was outside Hajj months.
This ikhtilaf is about the effect of repetition on the original act.
4
Examine the legal stratagem (hila)
For someone who enters Makkah with Umrah before the months but desires tamattu': he should delay tawaf until the months begin. If he already performed most circuits, he becomes like a Makkan and cannot be a mutamatti' unless he leaves and re-enters from his miqat.
The hila preserves the concession by ensuring tawaf occurs in the correct time.

Source Text

فصار ذلك أصلاً في أن كل ما يتعلق بالإحرام من الأفعال فحكم أكثره حكم جميعه في باب الجواز ومنع ورود الفساد عليه. وأشار إلى أنه لا يشترط وجود إحرامها في أشهر الحج لأن المعتبر إنما هو الطواف. وفي المحيط : ولو طاف كله في رمضان جنب أو محدث أعاده في شوال لم يكن متمتعاً لأن طواف المحدث لا يرتفض بالإعادة فلم تقع العمرة والحج في أشهر الحج وكذلك طواف الجنب على رواية الكرخي فكان الفرض هو الأول ولم يوجد في أشهر في أشهر الحج أو لا . وإنما اختصت المتعة بأفعال العمرة في أشهر الحج لأن أشهر الحج كان متعيناً للحج قبل الإسلام فأدخل الله العمرة فيها إسقاطاً للسفر الجديد عن الغرباء فكان اجتماعهما في وقت واحد في سفر واحد رخصة وتمتعاً. وفي فتح القدير : وهل يشترط في القرآن أيضاً أن يفعل أكثر أشواط العمرة في أشهر الحج؟ ذكر في المحيط أنه قوله : (قال الإمام (الأقطع هو من شراح القدوري قوله : (وعلم من هذا الخ) قال في شرح اللباب : والحيلة لمن دخل مكة بعمرة قبل أشهر الحج يريد التمتع أو القران أن لا يطوف بل يصبر إلى أن تدخل أشهر الحج ثم يطوف فإنه متى طاف طوافاً ما وقع عن العمرة، ولو طاف الكل أو أكثره ثم دخلت أشهر الحج فأحرم بعمرة أخرى داخل الميقات ثم حج من عامه لم يكن متمتعاً عند الكل لأنه صار حكمه حكم أهل مكة بدليل أنه صار ميقاته ميقاتهم. قال الكرماني : إلا أن يخرج إلى أهله أو ميقات نفسه على ما ذكره الطحاوي ثم يرجع محرماً بالعمرة ا اه. والظاهر أن هذا الحكم بالنسبة إلى الآفاقي الذي صار في حكم المكي بخلاف المكي الحقيقي فإنه ولو خرج الآفاقي في الأشهر لا متمتعاً مسنوناً لما سبق من اشتراط عدم الإلمام في التمتع هذا والظاهر أن المتمتع بعد فراغه من العمرة لا يكون ممتنعاً من إتيان العمرة فإنه زيادة عبادة وهو وإن كان في حكم المكي إلا أن المكي ليس ممنوعاً عن العمرة فقط على الصحيح وإنما يكون ممنوعاً عن
