So that became a principle that everything related to ihram from actions, the ruling of its majority is the ruling of its entirety in the chapter of permissibility and prevention of corruption. He indicated that the existence of her ihram is not required during the months of Hajj because what is considered is only the tawaf. In al-Muhit: if he performed all the tawaf in Ramadan as junub or hadath and repeated it in Shawwal, he would not be mutamatti' because the tawaf of the one with hadath is not invalidated by repetition, so Umrah and Hajj did not occur in the months of Hajj, and similarly the tawaf of the junub according to the narration of al-Karkhi, the obligation is the first and it did not occur in the months of Hajj, and according to the view of others, the first is invalidated by repetition, but the prohibition of Umrah for this travel is attached to this tawaf in Ramadan, as evidence that if he completed this Umrah then began the ihram of Umrah in the months of Hajj, then performed a new Umrah and Hajj in the same year, he would not be mutamatti'; so this first tawaf is not invalidated by repetition, unlike tawaf al-ziyarah because no prohibition is attached to it such that it would be invalidated by repetition. From this it is known that performing Umrah in a year before the months of Hajj prevents tamattu' in its years, whether he performs another Umrah in the months of Hajj or not. Tamattu' was only specified for actions of Umrah in the months of Hajj because the months of Hajj were designated for Hajj before Islam, and Allah inserted Umrah into them to eliminate a new journey for strangers, so their combination in one time and one journey is a concession and enjoyment. In Fath al-Qadir: is it also required in qiran that he perform most circuits of Umrah in the months of Hajj? It is mentioned in al-Muhit that his statement: (al-Aqta' is one of the commentators of al-Quduri, his statement: (And it is known from this etc.) He said in Sharh al-Lubab: The stratagem for one who enters Makkah with Umrah before the months of Hajj intending tamattu' or qiran is not to perform tawaf, but to wait until the months of Hajj enter, then perform tawaf; for whenever he performs any tawaf, it counts as Umrah. If he performed all or most of the tawaf, then the months of Hajj entered, and he entered ihram for another Umrah within the miqat, then performed Hajj in the same year, he would not be mutamatti' according to everyone, because his ruling becomes that of the people of Makkah, as evidence that his miqat becomes their miqat. Al-Kirmani said: Unless he goes out to his family or his own miqat as al-Tahawi mentioned, then returns in ihram for Umrah. And the apparent is that this ruling applies to the afaqi who becomes like a Makkan, unlike a true Makkan; for even if the afaqi goes out during the months, he is not a mutamatti' as sunnah due to the requirement of not having visited (al-ilman) in tamattu'. And the apparent is that the mutamatti' after finishing his Umrah is not prevented from performing another Umrah, for it is an increase in worship; although he is like a Makkan, the Makkan is not prevented from Umrah absolutely according to the correct view, but is only prevented from tamattu' as previously. End of what is in al-Lubab. The beginning of ihram before it is disliked, and if a Kufan performed Umrah therein and stayed in Makkah or Basra and performed Hajj, it is valid and it is not required, and it seems it is based on what we presented from Muhammad, and we presented its answer in the chapter of qiran.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and explanation of a key principle in tamattu': the timing of the majority of tawaf determines whether Umrah occurs within the months of Hajj. The author first states the principle that for actions related to ihram, the ruling of the majority is like the ruling of the whole. Then he addresses an objection: the timing of the ihram itself is not required in the months of Hajj; what matters is the tawaf. He cites Al-Muhit with an example: if a person in the state of janabah or minor hadath performs all of tawaf in Ramadan and then repeats it in Shawwal, he is not a mutamatti' because the first tawaf—though repeated—does not become invalid; thus the Umrah was not performed in the months of Hajj. This is because for a muhdith, the tawaf is valid but deficient; repeating it does not erase the first occurrence. On another view, repetition invalidates the first, but the prohibition of Umrah in that same journey attaches to the first tawaf. The author distinguishes from tawaf al-ziyarah (the visit tawaf) which carries no such prohibition. From this it is deduced that performing Umrah in a year before the months of Hajj prevents tamattu' in that year, even if another Umrah is performed within the months. He explains that tamattu' is a concession combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey, originally to spare strangers a second journey; so it only applies when the actions of Umrah occur within the months of Hajj. The passage then quotes Fath al-Qadir raising the question of whether the same applies to qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined), and references al-Muhit. Then a long excerpt from Sharh al-Lubab provides a legal stratagem (hila) for one who enters Makkah with Umrah before the months but later wants to do tamattu': he should postpone tawaf until the months begin. If he already performed most of the tawaf before the months, he becomes like a Makkan, and cannot be a mutamatti' unless he leaves Makkah to his miqat and re-enters in ihram for Umrah. The passage concludes that this ruling applies to non-Makkans (afaqi) who become like Makkans; true Makkans are never mutamatti'. It also clarifies that after finishing Umrah, the mutamatti' may perform another Umrah; being like a Makkan does not prohibit Umrah, only tamattu'. Finally, the text adds a brief ruling: it is disliked to begin ihram before it (perhaps meaning before the months), but if a Kufan performs Umrah and stays in Makkah or Basra and then does Hajj, it is valid and does not require anything, referencing Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey during the months of Hajj, with a break in between, as a concession.
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding prohibition.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (lack of wudu).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs all circuits of tawaf for Umrah in Ramadan and then repeats them in Shawwal, does he become a mutamatti'?
A) Yes, because he repeated tawaf in Shawwal.
B) No, because the first tawaf is not invalidated by repetition.
C) Yes, because the majority of tawaf was in Shawwal.
D) No, because the ihram was not in Shawwal.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires that the majority of tawaf circuits be performed within the months of Hajj; a legal stratagem allows delaying tawaf to achieve this.

Definition of the Months of Hajj
Defines the months of Hajj and explores linguistic and legal dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of the months of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and identify the legal implications of this timing.

Core Idea
The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah; no Hajj act is valid outside them.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the precise months during which Hajj rituals must be performed. It also addresses a linguistic nuance: how two months and part of a third can be called 'months'. The author then explains the practical consequences of this timing for various Hajj-related acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition
State the months of Hajj as given in the text: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
This is the unanimous Hanafi position, narrated from the three Abdullahs.
2
Understand the Linguistic Justification
Analyze why two months and part of a third can be called 'months'. The text quotes al-Kashshaf: the plural applies to more than one, as in Quran 66:4.
The author rejects the idea that 'months' is a general term made specific, because that would require at least three individuals.
3
Recognize the Legal Implication
All acts of Hajj must be performed within these months. Examples: fasting for tamattu' before the months is invalid; sa'i after tawaf al-qudum must be in the months.
Ihram for Hajj outside the months is disliked but not invalid.
4
Note the Exception
Tawaf al-ziyarah (the main tawaf of Hajj) can be performed on the 11th and 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah, after the ten days.
This shows that not every single act is confined to the first ten days.
5
Apply to a Scenario
Consider a person who performs Umrah in Shawwal and then performs Hajj later the same year. This is tamattu' because both occur within the months of Hajj.
The text discusses a scenario where a person does Umrah on the Day of Nahr (10th) and then Hajj the next year; that case is problematic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول المصنف : (وهي شوال وذو القعدة وعشر ذي الحجة) أي أشهر الحج المرادة في قوله تعالى الحج أشهر معلومات [البقرة : ۱۹۷] وهو مروي عن العبادلة الثلاثة ورواه البخاري في صحيحه عن ابن عمر، فالمراد حينئذ من الجمع شهران وبعض الثالث وذكر في الكشاف : فإن قلت فكيف كان الشهران وبعض الثالث أشهراً؟ قلت : اسم الجمع يشترك فيه ما وراء الواحد بدليل قوله تعالى فقد صغت قلوبكما ﴾ [التحريم: ٤] فلا سؤال فيه إذن، وإنما يكون موضعاً للسؤال لو قيل ثلاثة أشهر معلومات ا هـ . وما في غاية البيان من أنه عام مخصوص ففيه نظر لأن أخص الخصوص في العام إذا كان جمعاً ثلاثة لا يجوز التخصيص بعده فالأولى ما ذكره في الكشاف وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر أن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها حتى إذا صام المتمتع أو القارن ثلاثة أيام قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، وكذا السعي بين الصفا والمروة عقب طواف القدوم لا يجوز إلا في أشهر الحج وأنه لا يكره الإحرام بالجج فيه مع أنه يكره الإحرام بالحج في غير أشهر الحج وأنه لو أحرم بعمرة يوم النحر فأتى بأفعالها ثم أحرم من يومه ذلك بالحج وبقي محرماً إلى قابل فحج كان متمتعاً. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يعكر على ما تقدم ويوجب أن يضع مكان قولهم وحج من عامه ذلك في تصوير التمتع وأحرم بالحج من عامه ذلك ا هـ . وسيأتي في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام أنه لو أحرم بعمرة يوم النحر وجب عليه الرفض والتحلل لارتكابه النهي فينبغي أن لا يكون متمتعاً لأنه مكي وعمرته وحجته مكية والمتمتع من عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية. والقعدة بالكسر والفتح اعترض القهستاني على هذا الجواب بأنه مخرج للعشر لأنه خارج عن الشهرين على أنه قول مرجوح لا يليق بفصاحة القرآن واختار في الجواب أن الجمع المراد به ثلاثة لكن جعل بعض الشهر شهراً تسامحاً أو مجازاً، وهذا الجواب نقله في النهر عن الكشاف أيضاً لقوله أو نزل بعض الشهر منزلة كله . ورده في العناية أيضاً بأن فيه إلباساً بخلاف قوله تعالى فقد صغت قلوبكما [التحريم: ٤] ثم قال: وأقول هو من باب ذكر الكل وإرادة الجزء وقرينة المجاز سياق الكلام لأنه قال الحج أشهر [البقرة: ١٩٧] والحج نفسه ليس بأشهر فكان تقديره - والله أعلم - الحج في أشهر، والظرف لا يستلزم الاستفراق فكان البعض مراداً وعينه ما روى عن العبادلة وغيرهم ا هـ . قوله : (وما في غاية البيان الخ) قال في النهر : الذي في غاية البيان ما لفظه يجوز أن يراد من العام الخاص إذا دل الدليل وقد دل نقلاً وعقلاً ا اهـ. والفرق بين العام المخصوص والعام الذي أريد به خاص لا يخفى ا هـ. وما ذكره المؤلف مسبوق إليه في العناية وفيها : لأن الخصوص إنما يكون بإخراج بعض أفراد العام لا بإخراج بعض كل فرد ا.هـ. وهذا وارد قوله : وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر إن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها أقول : يرد عليه طواف الزيارة فإنه يجوز في يومين بعد عشر ذي الحجة
The author's statement: (They are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) meaning the months of Hajj intended in His saying: 'Hajj is (in) known months' [2:197]. This is narrated from the three Abdullahs, and al-Bukhari narrated it in his Sahih from Ibn Umar. So what is meant by the plural is two months and part of the third. It is mentioned in al-Kashshaf: For if you say, how can two months and part of the third be months? I say: the plural noun applies to more than one, as evidence of His saying: 'your hearts have inclined' [66:4], so there is no question. It would be a question if it said 'three known months'. End. What is in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is a general term made specific is questionable because the most specific of specific in a general if it is a plural of three does not permit specification after it. So what is preferred is what al-Kashshaf mentioned. The benefit of timing by these months is that no act of Hajj is permissible except in them, such that if a mutamatti' or qarin fasts three days before the months of Hajj, it is not permissible; likewise, sa'i between Safa and Marwa after tawaf al-qudum is not permissible except in the months of Hajj; and that it is not disliked to enter ihram for Hajj in them, while it is disliked to enter ihram for Hajj outside the months of Hajj; and that if one entered ihram for Umrah on the Day of Nahr, performed its actions, then entered ihram for Hajj on that same day, and remained in ihram until the next year and performed Hajj, he would be a mutamatti'. In Fath al-Qadir: this contradicts what came before and requires that they replace their statement 'and performed Hajj in that same year' in the depiction of tamattu' with 'and entered ihram for Hajj in that same year'. End. It will come in the chapter of conjoining ihram to ihram that if one enters ihram for Umrah on the Day of Nahr, he must cancel and exit ihram due to violating the prohibition, so he should not be mutamatti' because he is a Makkan and his Umrah and Hajj are Makkan; the mutamatti' has his Umrah from the miqat and his Hajj Makkan. And al-Qi'dah with kasr and fatha. Al-Qahistani objected to this answer that it excludes the ten because it is outside the two months, and it is a weak statement not befitting the eloquence of the Quran. He chose in the answer that the plural is meant to be three, but part of a month is made a month by tolerance or metaphor. This answer is transmitted in al-Nahr from al-Kashshaf as well due to his saying 'or part of a month is taken as the whole'. It was refuted in al-Inayah also that there is confusion in it, unlike His saying 'your hearts have inclined' [66:4]. Then he said: I say it is from the category of mentioning the whole and intending the part, and the indication of metaphor is the context of the speech because He said 'Hajj (is) months', and Hajj itself is not months, so its estimation is—and Allah knows best—'Hajj is in months', and the adverb does not necessitate covering all, so part is intended, and it is specified by what is narrated from the three Abdullahs and others. End. His statement: (And what is in Ghayat al-Bayan etc.) He said in al-Nahr: what is in Ghayat al-Bayan is the wording: it is permissible to intend specific from general if evidence indicates, and it has indicated both by transmission and reason. End. The difference between a general term made specific and a general term intended as specific is not hidden. End. What the author mentioned is preceded in al-Inayah, in which: because specificity is only by excluding some individuals of the general, not by excluding some part of each individual. End. And this is relevant to his statement: The benefit of timing by these months is that no act of Hajj is permissible except in them. I say: tawaf al-ziyarah refutes this, for it is permissible in the two days after the ten of Dhu al-Hijjah.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is a definition and linguistic analysis of the months of Hajj. It begins by stating that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, as narrated from the three Abdullahs (Ibn Umar, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Zubayr) and recorded by Bukhari. The author then addresses a linguistic issue: how can two months and part of a third be called 'months'? He quotes al-Kashshaf which answers that the plural noun in Arabic covers more than one, as in 'your hearts have inclined' (the hearts of two women are referred to as plural). So calling two months and part of a third 'months' is valid. The author rejects the view from Ghayat al-Bayan that it is a general term made specific, because that would require the general to have at least three individuals, and you cannot specify it to less than three. He prefers the answer of al-Kashshaf. Then he discusses the legal implications: all acts of Hajj must be performed within these months. Examples: fasting three days for tamattu' before the months is invalid; sa'i after tawaf al-qudum must be in the months; it is not disliked to enter ihram for Hajj in these months, but it is disliked outside them. He then discusses a specific case: if one enters ihram for Umrah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah), performs its actions, then enters ihram for Hajj and remains in ihram until the next year and performs Hajj, he would be mutamatti' according to some, but Fath al-Qadir says this is contradictory and should be corrected to entering ihram for Hajj in that same year. The passage then criticizes this by noting that on the Day of Nahr, the ruling is to abandon ihram due to the prohibition, so such a person would be a Makkan, and his Umrah and Hajj would be Makkan, not qualifying for tamattu', which requires Umrah from the miqat. The author then records a disagreement with al-Qahistani over whether the ten days count as a month linguistically, and various interpretations are given. Finally, the author notes a possible exception to the rule that no Hajj act is permissible outside these months: tawaf al-ziyarah is permissible in the two days after the ten days (i.e., 11th and 12th Dhu al-Hijjah), though he does not resolve it here.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
جمع قلة (jam' qilla): A plural form for three to ten items, e.g., 'af'ilu' patterns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the definition of the months of Hajj?
A) Quranic verse 2:197 alone
B) Hadith from the three Abdullahs
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Qiyas on the months of fasting

Key Takeaway
The months of Hajj are defined by transmitted reports as Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah; this timing is essential for the validity of Hajj rituals.

Definition and Ruling on the Months of Hajj and Ihram Before Them
Defines the months of Hajj and rules on ihram before them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the months of Hajj, explain the Hanafi ruling on ihram before them (sahih wa makruh tahrimi), and identify the reason for the karahah.

Core Idea
Ihram before the months of Hajj is valid but prohibitively disliked due to risk of violating prohibitions.

This lesson clarifies the definition of the months of Hajj and the ruling on performing ihram before them. Although ihram before the prescribed time is valid, it carries a level of dislike (karahah) that is almost prohibited. We will explore why it is valid, the type of dislike, and the scholarly difference on its reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the months of Hajj
From the text, note that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah. This is based on Quran 2:197 and narrations from the Companions.
The phrase 'ashhur' (months) interpreted as two months and part of the third, as discussed in the commentary.
2
Understand the ruling on ihram before these months
Ihram before the months is valid (sahih) because it is a condition (shart) for Hajj, not a pillar. However, it is disliked (makruh) due to the prolonged period leading to potential prohibitions.
The Hanafi default for 'karahah' is tahrimi (prohibitive) unless specified otherwise.
3
Analyze why ihram before months is valid
Ihram is a shart, not a rukn. Just as purification before prayer time is valid, ihram before its time is valid. Acts of Hajj can be performed only in the months, but the state of ihram can begin earlier.
Analogies: taharah before waktu, or ihram before miqat.
4
Determine the type of karahah and its reason
The karahah is tahrimi because the text uses 'karahah' absolutely. The reason is the fear of committing prohibited acts (like sexual intercourse or hunting) during the prolonged ihram.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: some say ihram itself is disliked; the preferred view is the latter.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the reason
Ibn Shuja held that ihram before months is disliked because ihram itself is disliked before its time. The faqih Abu Abdullah held that it is disliked only if one fears violating prohibitions; if safe, it is not disliked. The preferred view is Abu Abdullah's.
This difference does not affect the ruling but refines the rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبح الإحرام به قبلها وكره

قوله : (وهي شوال وذو القعدة وعشر ذي الحجة) أي أشهر الحج المرادة في قوله تعالى الحج أشهر معلومات [البقرة : ۱۹۷] وهو مروي عن العبادلة الثلاثة ورواه البخاري في صحيحه عن ابن عمر، فالمراد حينئذ من الجمع شهران وبعض الثالث وذكر في الكشاف : فإن قلت فكيف كان الشهران وبعض الثالث أشهراً؟ قلت : اسم الجمع يشترك فيه ما وراء الواحد بدليل قوله تعالى فقد صغت قلوبكما ﴾ [التحريم: ٤] فلا سؤال فيه إذن، وإنما يكون موضعاً للسؤال لو قيل ثلاثة أشهر معلومات ا هـ . وما في غاية البيان من أنه عام مخصوص ففيه نظر لأن أخص الخصوص في العام إذا كان جمعاً ثلاثة لا يجوز التخصيص بعده فالأولى ما ذكره في الكشاف وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر أن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها حتى إذا صام المتمتع أو القارن ثلاثة أيام قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، وكذا السعي بين والمروة عقب طواف القدوم لا يجوز إلا في أشهر الحج وأنه لا يكره الإحرام بالجج فيه مع أنه يكره الإحرام بالحج في غير أشهر الحج وأنه لو أحرم بعمرة يوم النحر فأتى بأفعالها ثم أحرم من يومه ذلك بالحج وبقي محرماً إلى قابل فحج كان متمتعاً. قال في فتح القدير : وهذا يعكر على ما تقدم ويوجب أن يضع مكان قولهم وحج من عامه ذلك في تصوير التمتع وأحرم بالحج من عامه ذلك ا هـ . وسيأتي في باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام أنه لو أحرم بعمرة يوم النحر وجب عليه الرفض والتحلل لارتكابه النهي فينبغي أن لا يكون متمتعاً لأنه مكي وعمرته وحجته مكية والمتمتع من عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية. والقعدة بالكسر والفتح

واعترض القهستاني على هذا الجواب بأنه مخرج للعشر لأنه خارج عن الشهرين على أنه قول مرجوح لا يليق بفصاحة القرآن واختار في الجواب أن الجمع المراد به ثلاثة لكن جعل بعض الشهر شهراً تسامحاً أو مجازاً، وهذا الجواب نقله في النهر عن الكشاف أيضاً لقوله أو نزل بعض الشهر منزلة كله . ورده في العناية أيضاً بأن فيه إلباساً بخلاف قوله تعالى فقد صغت قلوبكما [التحريم: ٤] ثم قال: وأقول هو من باب ذكر الكل وإرادة الجزء وقرينة المجاز سياق الكلام لأنه قال الحج أشهر [البقرة: ١٩٧] والحج نفسه ليس بأشهر فكان تقديره - والله أعلم - الحج في أشهر، والظرف لا يستلزم الاستفراق فكان البعض مراداً وعينه ما روى عن العبادلة وغيرهم ا هـ . قوله : (وما في غاية البيان الخ) قال في النهر : الذي في غاية البيان ما لفظه يجوز أن يراد من العام الخاص إذا دل الدليل وقد دل نقلاً وعقلاً ا اهـ. والفرق بين العام المخصوص والعام الذي أريد به خاص لا يخفى ا هـ. وما ذكره المؤلف مسبوق إليه في العناية وفيها : لأن الخصوص إنما يكون بإخراج بعض أفراد العام لا بإخراج بعض كل فرد ا.هـ. وهذا وارد قوله : وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر إن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها أقول : يرد عليه طواف الزيارة فإنه يجوز في يومين بعد عشر ذي الحجة

قوله : (وصح الإحرام به قبلها وكره) أي صح الإحرام بالحج قبل أشهر الحج مع الكراهة بناء على أنه شرط وليس بركن لعدم اتصال الأفعال به فجاز تقديمه على الزمان كالتقديم على المكان وكالطهارة للصلاة بخلاف تحريمتها فإنه لا يجوز تقديمها على الوقت وإن كانت شرطاً عندنا لما أن الأفعال متصلة بها لقوله تعالى وذكر اسم ربه فصلى [الأعلى : ١٥] لأن الفاء للوصل والتعقيب بلا تراخ وإنما كره للطول المفضي إلى الوقوع في محظوره أو على أنه شرط شبيه بالركن ولذا أذاً أعتق العبد بعد ما أحرم لا يتمكن عن أن يخرج عن ذلك الإحرام للفرض فالصحة للشرط والكراهة للشبه، وأطلقوا الكراهة فهي تحريمية لأنها المرادة عند إطلاقهم لها

قال في النهر : اختلف المتأخرون في المعنى الذي لأجله كره التقديم فكان ابن شجاع يقول لأنه إحرام، وكان الفقيه أبو عبد الله يقول لأنه لا يأمن من مواقعة المحظور فإذا أمن ذلك لا يكره كذا في الذخيرة وفيها لا يكره الإحرام بالجج يوم النحر ويكره قبل أشهر الحج. أقول : فيه إفادة أن المراد بالوقت وقت الحج ولو لعام مضى إلا أن الظاهر ما قاله الفقيه إذ لا معنى لكراهة فعل شرط قبل وقت مشروط إلا كما قال ولذا لم يعرج أكثر الشراح على غيره وإحرامه يوم النحر ينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً حيث لم يأمن وإن كان في أشهر الحج، وما في الكتاب مقيد بذلك وإطلاقه يفيد التحريم وقد صرح في النهاية بإساءته ا هـ.
Ihram for it before them is valid and disliked. He (the author) said: (They are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah) meaning the months of Hajj intended in the verse 'Hajj is in well-known months' [2:197]. It is narrated from the three Abdullahs, and Bukhari narrated it from Ibn Umar. Then the meaning of the plural is two months and part of the third... (continued) He (the author) said: (And ihram for it before them is valid and disliked) meaning ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj is valid with dislike based on it being a condition and not a pillar... The later scholars differed on the reason for the dislike...
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on ihram for Hajj before its prescribed months. It first defines the months of Hajj as Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, based on the Quranic verse and reports from the three Abdullahs. The author discusses the interpretation of the plural 'ashhur' for two months and part of the third. Then the ruling: ihram for Hajj before these months is valid because it is a condition (shart) and not a pillar (rukn), analogous to performing ritual purification before prayer time. However, it is disliked (makruh) due to the prolonged ihram leading to potential violations of prohibitions. The karahah is tahrimi (prohibitive) according to the Hanafi usage. The passage also includes a discussion on the reason for the dislike, with some scholars saying it is because ihram itself is disliked before its time, and others saying it is only disliked if there is a fear of committing prohibited acts; if safe, it is not disliked. The relied-upon view is that it is makruh tahrimi.

Key Terms
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): A level of dislike close to prohibition; the default when karahah is used absolutely in Hanafi texts.
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhul-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj?
A) Invalid (batil) and sinful
B) Valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tahrimi)
C) Valid and recommended (mustahabb)
D) Invalid unless one fears missing Hajj

Key Takeaway
Ihram before the months of Hajj is valid because it is a condition, but it is prohibitively disliked due to the extended period of restriction.

The Kufi's Tamattu': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' for a non-Makki staying within miqat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tamattu' for a non-Makki who performs Umrah in Hajj months and stays within the miqat, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A non-Makki who performs Umrah in Hajj months and stays, then does Hajj, is a mutamatti' per Abu Hanifa, requiring a dam.

The Hanafi school addresses a nuanced scenario: a person from beyond the miqat (afiqi) performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, then stays in Makkah or a place like Basra, and later performs Hajj without returning home. Does this constitute tamattu' obligating a dam? The primary sources reveal a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions. This lesson dissects their proofs and resolves to the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the subject: a Kufi (afiqi) who performs Umrah in the Hajj months, stays in Makkah or Basra (a miqat place), and then performs Hajj.
The term 'Kufi' is generic for any non-Makki.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds this to be tamattu', requiring a dam.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that it is not tamattu' because both rituals are performed from within the miqat.
4
Analyze the proofs
Examine the dalil: Abu Hanifa argues the Umrah is miqati but the Hajj is Makki since the original journey is ongoing; the Sahibayn argue both are miqati as the person is now within the miqat.
The difference hinges on whether the 'first journey' is considered subsisting.
5
Determine the tarjih and thamarah al-khilaf
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as upheld by Fakhral-Islam and the author. The practical consequence: a dam is obligatory. If the Sahibayn's view were taken, no dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اعتمر كوفي فيها وأقام بمكة أو بصرة وحج صح تمتعه

أراد بالكوفي الآفاقي الذي يشرع له التمتع والقرآن كما أن المراد بالبصرة مكان لأهل التمتع والقرآن، سواء كان البصرة أو غيرها. أما إذا أقام بمكة أو خارجها داخل المواقيت فلأن عمرته آفاقية وحجته مكية فلذا كان متمتعاً اتفاقاً، وأما إذا خرج إلى مكان لأهله التمتع وليس وطنه فلأن السفر الأولى قائمة ما لم يعد إلى وطنه وقد اجتمع له نسكان فيها فوجب دم التمتع . ثم اختلف الطحاوي والجصاص فنقل الطحاوي أن هذا قول الإمام وأن قول صاحبيه بطلان التمتع لما أن نسكه هذان ميقاتيان ولا بد فيه أن تكون حجته مكية، ونقل الجصاص أنه متمتع اتفاقاً. قال فخر الإسلام إنه الصواب. وقوى الأول الشارح. وأطلق في إقامة مكة أو بصرة فشمل ما إذا اتخذهما داراً أولاً كما صرح به الأسبيجابي والكيساني، فما في الهداية من التقييد باتحادهما داراً اتفاقي. وقيد بكونه اعتمر في
And if a Kufi performs Umrah in them (the months of Hajj) and stays in Makkah or Basra and then performs Hajj, his tamattu' is valid. He meant by 'Kufi' the afiqi (one from outside the miqat) for whom tamattu' and qiran are legislated, just as by 'Basra' he meant a place for the people of tamattu' and qiran, whether it is Basra or other. As for if he stays in Makkah or outside it within the miqat, then his Umrah is miqati and his Hajj is Makkan, so he is mutamatti' by agreement. And if he goes out to a place of his people where tamattu' is legislated and it is not his home, then the first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his home, and two acts of worship have come together for him, so the dam of tamattu' is obligatory. Then al-Tahawi and al-Jassas differed: al-Tahawi narrated that this is the view of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and that the view of his two companions is the invalidity of tamattu' because both of his rituals are from the miqat and his Hajj must be Makkan, and al-Jassas narrated that he is mutamatti' by agreement. Fakhral-Islam said it is the correct view. And the commentator strengthened the first. And he made absolute the staying in Makkah or Basra, so it includes whether he made them a home or not, as stated by al-Asbijabi and al-Kasani. So what is in al-Hidayah of restriction to their being a home is accidental. And he restricted it to his performing Umrah in...
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a non-Makki (someone who is not a resident of Makkah, referred to here as a 'Kufi') who comes from beyond the miqat, performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, and then stays in Makkah or a place like Basra (which is a miqat) and then performs Hajj in the same year. According to Abu Hanifa, this constitutes tamattu', requiring a dam (sacrificial animal). The reason is that his Umrah is from the miqat (miqati) and his Hajj is from Makkah (Makki), fulfilling the definition of tamattu' (performing Umrah first and then Hajj in the same year without returning home). However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions) are reported to disagree, holding that it is not tamattu' because both rituals are from the miqat (since the person is now residing in the miqat area). Al-Tahawi and al-Jassas differed on whether the companions' view was contradictory to Abu Hanifa's. The preferred view is that of Abu Hanifa, as supported by Fakhral-Islam. The passage also clarifies that the ruling applies whether the person has made Makkah or Basra his home or not; the key is that he has not returned to his original home beyond the miqat.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs Umrah during the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year without returning to his home beyond the miqat.
آفاقي (afiqi): One who comes from beyond the miqat, i.e., a non-Makki.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, and he must offer a dam
B) No, because he is now a Makki
C) No, because both his Umrah and Hajj are from the miqat
D) Yes, but no dam is required

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a non-Makki who performs Umrah in Hajj months and stays within the miqat for Hajj is a mutamatti' per Abu Hanifa, and a dam is obligatory.

Entering Ihram for Hajj Before Its Months: Validity and Dislike
States ruling on ihram before Hajj months with proof and discussion on nature of dislike

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering ihram for Hajj before its months and explain the reason for its dislike, including the difference of opinion on the type of karahah.

Core Idea
Entering ihram for Hajj before its months is valid but makruh tahrimi—disliked due to potential prohibitions.

Is it valid to enter ihram for Hajj before Shawwal? The Hanafi school confirms it is valid because ihram is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn). However, it carries a strong dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah) due to the extended period in ihram, which may lead to violating prohibitions. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and the scholarly discussion over the nature of the dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position on entering ihram for Hajj before its months: valid or invalid? Disliked or not?
The matn says 'wa saha al-ihram bihi qablaha wa kurihat'.
2
Understand the Legal Basis: Shart vs Rukn
Recognize that ihram is a condition (shart) for Hajj, not a pillar (rukn). Conditions can be performed before their time, unlike pillars that are tied to the act.
The commentary compares it to purification before prayer time and contrasts it with the prohibition of prayer (tahrimah) which cannot be advanced.
3
Analyze the Proof from Quran
Examine the verse 'wa dhkara isma rabbihi fasalla' (Surah al-A'la 87:15). The fa' indicates immediate connection (ta'qib), showing that prayer follows the mention without delay, similar to how Hajj actions follow ihram. Thus, advancing ihram is unlike advancing the prayer prohibition.
The dalil supports that ihram is a condition that can be separated in time.
4
Explore the Reason for Dislike
Understand the two views among later Hanafi scholars: Ibn Shuja' said the dislike is because ihram itself is sacred (so early entry is inherently disliked); al-Faqih Abu Abdullah said it is due to fear of committing prohibited acts during the long period.
The commentator leans toward al-Faqih's view and notes that if one is safe from violations, it is not disliked.
5
Determine the Type of Karahah
Identify whether the karahah is tahrimi (prohibited dislike) or tanzihi (recommended dislike). The passage states that the absolute use of karahah in the madhhab indicates tahrimi, as confirmed by al-Qahastani.
The mufta bihi is makruh tahrimi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح الإحرام به قبلها وكره) أي صح الإحرام بالحج قبل أشهر الحج مع الكراهة بناء على أنه شرط وليس بركن لعدم اتصال الأفعال به فجاز تقديمه على الزمان كالتقديم على المكان وكالطهارة للصلاة بخلاف تحريمتها فإنه لا يجوز تقديمها على الوقت وإن كانت شرطاً عندنا لما أن الأفعال متصلة بها لقوله تعالى وذكر اسم ربه فصلى [الأعلى : ١٥] لأن الفاء للوصل والتعقيب بلا تراخ وإنما كره للطول المفضي إلى الوقوع في محظوره أو على أنه شرط شبيه بالركن ولذا أذاً أعتق العبد بعد ما أحرم لا يتمكن عن أن يخرج عن ذلك الإحرام للفرض فالصحة للشرط والكراهة للشبه، وأطلقوا الكراهة فهي تحريمية لأنها المرادة عند إطلاقهم لها قوله : (وإنما يكره للطول الخ) قال في النهر : اختلف المتأخرون في المعنى الذي لأجله كره. التقديم فكان ابن شجاع يقول لأنه إحرام، وكان الفقيه أبو عبد الله يقول لأنه لا يأمن من مواقعة المحظور فإذا أمن ذلك لا يكره كذا في الذخيرة وفيها لا يكره الإحرام بالجج يوم النحر ويكره قبل أشهر الحج. أقول : فيه إفادة أن المراد بالوقت وقت الحج ولو لعام مضى إلا أن الظاهر ما قاله الفقيه إذ لا معنى لكراهة فعل شرط قبل وقت مشروط إلا كما قال ولذا لم يعرج أكثر الشراح على غيره وإحرامه يوم النحر ينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً حيث لم يأمن وإن كان في أشهر الحج، وما في الكتاب مقيد بذلك وإطلاقه يفيد التحريم وقد صرح في النهاية بإساءته ا هـ. أي فظاهره عدم التحريم وقد شاع في كلامهم في كتاب الحج إطلاق الإساءة على ترك السنة، لكن صرح القهستاني بأنها تحريمية وقال : كما أشير إليه في شرح الطحاوي وقد تقدم قبيل باب الإحرام ذكر المؤلف الإجماع على الكراهة ونقلنا هناك خلاف أبي يوسف فيها فراجعه وبه يحصل التوفيق فتدبر
His statement: (And it is valid to enter ihram for it before it, and it is disliked) meaning: it is valid to enter ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj with dislike, based on the fact that it is a condition and not a pillar because the actions are not connected to it, so it is permissible to advance it before its time just as it is permissible to advance it before its place, and like purification for prayer, unlike the prohibition of prayer (tahrimah) for it is not permissible to advance it before its time even though it is a condition according to us because the actions are connected to it, due to His statement, exalted: 'And mention the name of his Lord and pray' [Surah al-A'la 15], because the fa' is for connection and immediate sequence without delay. Rather it is disliked because of the length leading to falling into prohibited acts, or it is a condition resembling a pillar. Therefore if a slave is freed after he has entered ihram, he is not able to exit that ihram for the obligatory (hajj). So validity is due to it being a condition and dislike is due to its resemblance. And they used the word dislike absolutely, so it is tahrimi because that is what is intended when they use it absolutely. His statement: (It is only disliked because of the length etc.) He said in al-Nahr: The later scholars differed concerning the reason for which it is disliked to advance it. Ibn Shuja' used to say because it is ihram, and al-Faqih Abu Abdullah used to say because he is not safe from perpetrating a prohibited act. So if he is safe from that, it is not disliked. This is in al-Dhakhirah, and in it: it is not disliked to enter ihram for Hajj on the day of Nahr, but it is disliked before the months of Hajj. I say: In it there is benefit that what is meant by time is the time of Hajj, even if for a past year, but the apparent is what al-Faqih said, for there is no meaning to dislike an act of a condition before its time except as he said, and therefore most of the commentators did not give weight to other than it. And his entering ihram on the day of Nahr should be disliked when he is not safe, even if it is in the months of Hajj. What is in the book is restricted to that and its generality indicates prohibition, and al-Nihayah has expressly stated that he is doing wrong. End. So its apparent meaning is non-prohibition, and it is common in their speech in the book of Hajj to use wrongdoing for leaving the sunnah, but al-Qahastani explicitly stated that it is tahrimi and said: as indicated in Sharh al-Tahawi, and it has preceded before the chapter of Ihram that the author mentioned consensus on the dislike and we transmitted there the difference of Abu Yusuf concerning it, so refer to it and through it harmony is achieved, so ponder.
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement 'Wa saha al-ihram bihi qablaha wa kurihat' (And it is valid to enter ihram for it before it, and it is disliked). The commentator explains that entering ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj is valid because it is a condition (shart) for Hajj, not a pillar (rukn). Conditions can be performed before their time, unlike pillars which are connected to the act. The commentator gives examples: advancing ihram before its months is like performing purification before prayer time, which is valid. However, the prohibition of prayer (tahrimah) cannot be advanced because the actions of prayer are connected to it, as indicated by the Quranic verse 'wa dhkara isma rabbihi fasalla' where the fa' indicates immediate sequence. The dislike (karahah) for advancing ihram is due to the length of time in ihram which may lead to committing prohibited acts, or because it resembles a pillar. The commentator then discusses the meaning of karahah: the later scholars differed on the reason. Ibn Shuja' said it is because it is ihram itself (which is sacred), while al-Faqih Abu Abdullah said it is due to fear of violating prohibitions. If one is safe from that, it is not disliked. The commentator leans towards the latter view, but notes that the general usage of karahah in the madhhab indicates tahrimi (prohibited dislike). The passage ends by noting that al-Qahastani confirmed it is tahrimi, and that there is a difference from Abu Yusuf on this issue.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): In this context, karahah is used absolutely and thus interpreted as tahrimi (prohibited dislike), not tanzihi (recommended dislike).
التحريمية (al-tahrimiyyah): The type of dislike that is closer to prohibition, where omitting the disliked act is better but performing it is sinful if done intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is entering ihram for Hajj before its months considered disliked (makruh)?
A) Because it is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Because it resembles a rukn and one may commit prohibited acts due to the long period in ihram.
C) Because it is agreed to be haram by consensus.
D) Because it is only disliked if one is traveling far.

Key Takeaway
Entering ihram for Hajj before its months is valid because it is a condition, but it is makruh tahrimi due to the risk of violating prohibitions; the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that the dislike is prohibited-level.

Tamattu' of an Afaqi Who Performs Umrah in Hajj Months and Stays in Mecca or Basra
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu' of a non-Meccan staying in Mecca after Umrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' of a non-Meccan who stays in Mecca after Umrah during Hajj months, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute and the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
A non-Meccan who stays in Mecca after Umrah is still a mutamatti' according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn's objection is overruled.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a non-Meccan (afaqi) who performs Umrah during the months of Hajj, then stays in Mecca (or another location) and performs Hajj in the same year. Is he considered a mutamatti'? The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. We will explore the reasoning on both sides and determine the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling scenario
Read the passage to understand the exact situation: a Kufi (non-Meccan) performs Umrah in the Hajj months, stays in Mecca or Basra, then performs Hajj.
2
State the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Hanifa, such a person is a mutamatti' because his Umrah was afaqi and his Hajj is Meccan, thus combining two journeys.
3
Identify the opposing view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that staying in Mecca invalidates tamattu' because the Umrah becomes Meccan.
4
Analyze the basis of the dispute
The core disagreement is whether the stay in Mecca changes the character of the Umrah from afaqi to maki.
5
Determine the tarjih
Fakhr al-Islam and many later scholars preferred Abu Hanifa's view, making it the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قول المصنف : (ولو اعتمر كوفي فيها أي في أشهر الحج قوله : (قال) فخر الإسلام أنه الصواب) قال في النهر : وفي المعراج أنه الأصح لكن قال في الحقائق كثير من مشايخنا قالوا: الصواب ما قاله [؟] سأشهر الحج إذ لو اعتمر قبلها لا يكون متمتعاً اتفاقاً، وقيد بالكوفي لأن المكي لا تمتع له اتفاقاً، وقيد بكونه رجع إلى غير وطنه لأنه لو رجع إلى وطنه بطل تمتعه اتفاقاً إذا لم يكن ساق الهدي، وعبارة المجمع وخرج إلى البصرة أولى من التعبير بالإقامة بها لأن الحكم عند الإمام لا يختلف بين أن يقيم بها خمسة عشر يوماً أو لا، والأول محل الخلاف وفي الثاني يكون متمتعاً اتفاقاً. كذا في المصفى
The author's statement: (And if a Kufi performs Umrah in it, i.e. in the months of Hajj, and stays in Mecca or Basra and performs Hajj, his tamattu' is valid) He said: (Fakhr al-Islam said that it is correct) He said in al-Nahr: And in al-Mi'raj it is the most correct, but in al-Haqa'iq many of our scholars said: what is correct is what he said [؟] the months of Hajj, for if he performs Umrah before them, he is not a mutamatti' by agreement. And it is restricted to the Kufi because the Meccan has no tamattu' by agreement. And it is restricted to him returning to other than his original home because if he returns to his home, his tamattu' becomes invalid by agreement if he has not driven the sacrificial animal. And the expression of al-Majma': 'and he went out to Basra' is better than the expression of staying there, because the ruling according to the Imam does not differ between him staying there for fifteen days or not. The first is a place of difference, and in the second he is a mutamatti' by agreement. So it is in al-Musaffa.
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a non-Meccan (afaqi) who performs Umrah during the months of Hajj and then stays in Mecca or another place like Basra and performs Hajj in the same year. The ruling is that such a person is considered a mutamatti' (one performing tamattu') according to Abu Hanifa, because his Umrah was performed from beyond the miqat (afaqi) and his Hajj is from Mecca, thus combining two journeys. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Tahawi reported that this is only the view of Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider that if he stays in Mecca, his tamattu' is invalid because his Umrah becomes Meccan and he is no longer a mutamatti'. On the other hand, al-Jassas reported that it is tamattu' by agreement. Fakhr al-Islam (al-Bazdawi) affirmed the latter view as correct, and many later scholars supported this. The passage also notes that the ruling is restricted to a Kufi (non-Meccan) because a Meccan cannot perform tamattu' by agreement. Additionally, if the person returns to his original home after the Umrah, his tamattu' becomes invalid according to all, unless he had driven a sacrificial animal (hadi). The commentator prefers the expression 'he went out to Basra' over 'he stayed in Basra' because the ruling does not depend on the length of stay.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah during the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year, exiting ihram between them, requiring a sacrificial animal.
آفاقي (afaqi): A person whose place of residence is outside the miqat (the boundaries around Mecca), as opposed to a Meccan or someone residing within the miqat.
مكي (maki): A resident of Mecca or within the miqat boundary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) His tamattu' is valid and he must offer a dam.
C) His tamattu' is valid but no dam is required.
D) It depends on his intention.

Key Takeaway
A non-Meccan who performs Umrah in Hajj months and stays in Mecca without returning home is a mutamatti' according to the dominant Hanafi view, and must offer a dam.

Invalidated Umrah: Tamattu' Ruling When Staying in Mecca
Intra-Hanafi ruling on tamattu' after Umrah invalidation when staying in Mecca or elsewhere.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when a non-Meccan invalidates his Umrah and stays in Mecca, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from the Sahibayn's.

Core Idea
If a Kufi invalidates his Umrah and makes it up from Mecca, he is not a mutamatti' unless he returns home first.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tamattu' when a pilgrim invalidates his Umrah and then performs a makeup Umrah while staying in Mecca or elsewhere. The key issue is whether the original journey is considered ended by the invalidation, affecting the status of tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and common ground
The pilgrim is a Kufi (non-Meccan) who invalidates his Umrah, then stays in a place (Mecca or other) and performs a makeup Umrah and later Hajj. There is agreement that if he stays in Mecca, he is not a mutamatti'.
The Umrah from Mecca is considered Meccan, and Meccans cannot perform tamattu'.
2
Recognize the point of dispute
The dispute arises when he stays in a place other than his home (e.g., Basra). Abu Hanifa says he is not a mutamatti'; the Sahibayn say he is.
The disagreement hinges on whether the first journey is considered ended by invalidation.
3
Analyze each school's reasoning
Abu Hanifa: the journey ended with invalidation, so staying elsewhere does not restart a fresh journey from the miqat; the makeup Umrah is like a Meccan Umrah. The Sahibayn: staying elsewhere is an initiation of a new journey, similar to returning home.
The Sahibayn consider the first journey remains as long as he hasn't returned to his original home.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether a dam is required: Abu Hanifa says no dam, the Sahibayn say yes. Also, the text introduces a condition about crossing the miqat in the months of Hajj.
Al-Mabsut adds that if he crosses the miqat before the months and then performs Umrah, even Abu Hanifa agrees he is a mutamatti'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage supports al-Tahawi's report that Abu Hanifa's view is correct. Thus, without returning home, he is not a mutamatti' and no dam is required.
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa.

قوله : (ولو أفسدها فأقام بمكة وقضى وحج لا إلا أن يعود إلى أهله) أي لو أفسد الكوفي عمرته فأقام بمكة وقضى العمرة من عامه لا يكون متمتعاً إلا أن يرجع إلى وطنه بعد الخروج عن إحرام الفاسدة ثم يعود محرماً من الميقات بعمرة ثم يحج من عامه فإنه يكون متمتعاً، أما الأول فلأن سفره انتهى بالفساد فلما قضاها صارت عمرته مكية ولا تمتع لأهل مكة، وأما الثاني فلأن عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية فصار متمتعاً ولا يضره كون العمرة قضاء عما أفسده إن كانت قضاء. وفي قوله إلا أن يعود إلى أهله» دلالة على أن المراد بالإقامة بمكة الإقامة بمكان غير وطنه، سواء كان مكة أو غيرها، ولا خلاف فيما إذا أقام بمكة . وأما إذا أقام بغيرها فهو مذهب الإمام. وقالا يكون متمتعاً لأنه إنشاء سفر فهو كالعود إلى وطنه، وله أن سفره الأول باق ما لم يعد إلى وطنه وقد انتهى بالفاسد، وهذه المسألة أيدت نقل الطحاوي، وقيده في المبسوط بأن يجاوز المواقيت في أشهر الحج، أما إذا جاوزها قبلها ثم أهل بعمرة فيها كان متمعاً عند الإمام أيضاً لأنه بمجاوزة الميقات صار في حكم من لم يدخل مكة إن كان في أشهر الحج فلأنه لما دخلت وهو داخل المواقيت حرم عليه التمتع كما هو حرام على أهل مكة فلا تنقطع هذه الحرمة بخروجه من المواقيت بعد ذلك كالمكي
His statement: (And if he invalidates it, and stays in Mecca and makes it up and performs Hajj, not unless he returns to his family) i.e., if a Kufi invalidates his Umrah, and stays in Mecca and makes up the Umrah from his year, he is not a mutamatti' unless he returns to his home after exiting the ihram of the invalidated one, then returns in ihram from the miqat for an Umrah, then performs Hajj from his year. In that case he is a mutamatti'. As for the first, because his journey ended with invalidation, so when he made it up, his Umrah became Meccan, and there is no tamattu' for the people of Mecca. As for the second, because his Umrah is from the miqat and his Hajj is Meccan, so he becomes a mutamatti', and it does not harm him that the Umrah was a make-up for what he invalidated if it was indeed a make-up. And in his statement 'unless he returns to his family' there is an indication that what is meant by staying in Mecca is staying in a place other than his home, whether it is Mecca or other. There is no disagreement when he stays in Mecca. As for when he stays elsewhere, it is the madhhab of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said he is a mutamatti' because it is an initiation of a journey, so it is like returning to his home. And he (Abu Hanifa) that his first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his home, and it ended with invalidation. This issue supports the report of al-Tahawi. And al-Mabsut restricted it such that he must cross the miqat in the months of Hajj. As for if he crossed it before them and then entered ihram for Umrah in them, he is a mutamatti' according to the Imam as well, because by crossing the miqat he became like one who has not entered Mecca if it is in the months of Hajj. Because when he entered while being inside the miqat, tamattu' became prohibited to him as it is prohibited to the people of Mecca, so this prohibition is not cut off by his exiting the miqat afterwards, like the Meccan.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a Kufi (non-Meccan) invalidates his Umrah (e.g., by having marital relations), then stays in Mecca, performs a makeup Umrah from Mecca, and then performs Hajj in the same year. According to the clear ruling, he is not a mutamatti' because his Umrah has become Meccan (since he performed it from within Mecca), and a Meccan cannot perform tamattu'. However, if he first returns to his home (outside the miqat), then comes back and enters ihram for Umrah from the miqat, and then performs Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. The commentator notes that this ruling supports the report of al-Tahawi that Abu Hanifa holds that if he stays in a place other than his home (like Basra), he is not a mutamatti', while the Sahibayn say he is, because staying elsewhere initiates a new journey. Additionally, a condition is that the cross the miqat during the months of Hajj for the makeup Umrah; if he crossed before the months and then performed Umrah, he is still a mutamatti' according to Abu Hanifa because crossing before the months does not establish residency. However, if he was inside the miqat at the start of the months, then tamattu' is prohibited for him like a Meccan, and exiting later does not change that.

Key Terms
الإفساد (al-ifsaad): Invalidation of the Umrah, e.g., by sexual intercourse, which requires making it up and offering a sacrifice.
القضاء (al-qada'): The makeup of an invalidated ritual performed later, in this case the Umrah performed after invalidation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does a Kufi who invalidates his Umrah become a mutamatti' after making it up?
A) If he makes up the Umrah from Mecca and then performs Hajj.
B) If he returns to his home, then comes back from the miqat with a new Umrah.
C) If he stays in a place other than his home and makes up the Umrah.
D) He never becomes a mutamatti' after invalidation.

Key Takeaway
For a non-Meccan who invalidates Umrah, tamattu' is only established if he returns home and re-enters ihram from the miqat.
